# ministr — commercial cloud roadmap

> Status: **draft** · drafted across 12 interleaved research+synthesis steps using deliberate + ministr + serpapi MCPs. Cloud surface (`mcp.ministr.ai`) is live with OAuth 2.1 + corpus REST + Tauri management; this document plans the rest of the open-core commercial product.

<!-- Sections are appended as drafting steps complete. -->

## Shipped this conversation (2026-05-22 / 2026-05-23)

Sustained `/roadmap` iteration ran 10 chunks back-to-back through the F5 track. Harness moved 181 → 215 PASS (+34). Snapshot of what landed:

- **F5.5-a-priority** (181→184) — customer-enqueue stamps tenant priority on `indexer_jobs` (Pro=1, Team=2, Enterprise=**4** bumped from 3 to match roadmap wording).
- **F5.5-a-plan-lookup** (184→186) — `PlanResolver` trait + `PostgresPlanResolver` wire OAuth tenants to `users.plan_id` (closes the `Tenant::local()`-defaults-to-Pro gap that made the Enterprise=4 lane unreachable through OAuth).
- **F5.4-e-revoke** (186→192) — JSONL revocation list + `MINISTR_LICENSE_REVOCATIONS` env var + `revoke-license` CLI; serve boot refuses revoked JWTs with `LicenseError::Revoked { hash, reason }`.
- **F5.4-e-rotate** (192→199) — `rotate-license-keys` CLI re-mints in-flight licenses against a new keypair; reads audit log, skips revoked + expired, writes per-customer JWTs to `--out-dir`.
- **F5.5-b-sla-skeleton** (199→204) — unauthenticated `GET /sla` endpoint returning `{status, version, uptime_secs, started_at_iso}`.
- **F5.5-b-latency** (204→207) — `LatencyTracker` middleware + `/sla.latency` field with `{count, p50_ms, p95_ms, p99_ms}`.
- **F5.5-b-persist-write** (207→210) — migration `0016_request_latency_snapshots` + `MINISTR_SLA_FLUSH_SECS` flush task persisting per-pod snapshots.
- **F5.5-b-persist-read** (210→212) — `SlaWindowStore` trait + `PostgresSlaWindowStore` + `/sla.latency.window_30d_max_p95_ms` field surfacing historical worst p95.
- **F5.5-b-persist-retention** (212→215) — `sla-prune-snapshots --older-than-secs` CLI for cron-driven retention; defensive 0-second refusal.
- **cleanup-iso-helper** (215, no behaviour change) — 4 copies of Howard Hinnant `civil_from_days` consolidated into one `ministr-api::format_unix_secs_iso`.
- **F5.5-b-page-skeleton** (docs-next build clean) — new `/status` route on `docs-next` polling `/sla` with `revalidate: 30`; renders four cards with SLA-target colouring.

**Full F5.5-b SLA backend track is now complete end-to-end**: skeleton (uptime) → latency (p95) → persist-write (snapshot flush) → persist-read (window 30d max) → persist-retention (CLI prune) → page-skeleton (customer-visible /status).

**Remaining unblocked code work is thinning**: F5.4-e-ui (admin webapp, requires architecture choice on key storage), F5.5-b-page-dashboard (full external status.ministr.ai), F5.4-e-revoke-mid-flight-graceful (axum graceful shutdown + 503 mode instead of process::exit; current implementation is k8s-friendly but brutal on in-flight requests). Larger chunks gated on Azure $$ opt-in: F5.5-c-dedicated-aca, F5.6 CMK BYOK. Blocked: F5.1 SAML (samael), F4.4 Atlas mirror (depends F4.2). *(F3.1b-ii-b landed 2026-05-23 — ResendMailSender + email-match enforcement on consume_invite. F5.4-e-revoke-mid-flight landed 2026-05-23, harness 229 → 231 — running serve self-detects revocation and exits within one refresh tick; F5.4-e-revoke-api-refresh landed 2026-05-23, harness 227 → 229; F5.4-e-revoke-api-fetch landed 2026-05-23, harness 224 → 227; F5.4-e-revoke-api-serve landed 2026-05-23, harness 220 → 224; F5.4-e-audit-db landed 2026-05-23, harness 215 → 220.)*


## 1. Positioning + moat thesis

**Positioning.** ministr is **hosted, polyglot, agent-aware code intelligence** for AI agents — a managed MCP service that combines a curated cross-codebase index (ministr Atlas) with cross-language bridge analysis, SOLID/coherence diagnostics, and per-agent session primitives. Not a coding assistant. Not a PR-review bot. Not a self-hosted single-language CLI. **The hosted intelligence layer every agent calls into.**

**Why this framing, given the crowd.** The "code intelligence MCP" category on directories like PulseMCP (14K+ servers) and Protodex includes pitlane-mcp, xray, Trace (44+ tools), intellij-mcp, and many more. **"We're the substrate" is what every newcomer says.** The differentiation is operational, not aspirational:

| Most code-intel MCPs | ministr |
|---|---|
| Self-hosted CLI you run locally | Hosted at `mcp.ministr.ai` with OAuth 2.1 + DCR + PKCE |
| Symbol grep / tree-sitter pass | 12 cross-language bridge detectors × 20+ language parsers |
| One repo at a time, on your disk | Atlas — curated network of pre-indexed OSS repos (Pro+) |
| Grep-style API | Agent-aware primitives: `ministr_compress`, `ministr_usage`, `ministr_dropped`, `ministr_extract`, coherence tracking |
| Mixed licenses, often abandoned | Permissive MIT open core, never demoting features to paid |

**The competitive gap.** Sourcegraph killed Cody Free/Pro in July 2025 (Enterprise-only, ~$50–75K/yr floor; Cody Enterprise ~$49/user/mo). Greptile at $30/seat is review-focused and GitHub/GitLab-only ($180M valuation; codebase-graph indexing is their core thesis but they don't host an OSS network and don't expose MCP primitives). IDE assistants (Cursor / Continue / Amp / Augment) own the chat surface, not the indexing substrate. The gap to claim: **hosted, multi-language, agent-aware code intelligence, with an MIT core**.

> **Refresh 2026-05-21 — Sourcegraph 7.0 repositioning.** On 2026-02-25 Sourcegraph announced 7.0 with the explicit framing "the intelligence layer for AI coding agents and developers" ([sourcegraph.com blog](https://sourcegraph.com/blog/a-new-era-for-sourcegraph-the-intelligence-layer-for-ai-coding-agents-and-developers)) — direct framing collision with ministr's positioning line. Their differentiation is still Enterprise-only price floor + closed-source posture; ours stays MIT core + paid cloud + Atlas. But the gap-narrative "Sourcegraph retreated to Enterprise; we own the rest" now needs sharpening: Sourcegraph is the named incumbent in this *exact* phrasing. Action: M4 below (positioning copy + R1 risk text both need a 2026-Q2 refresh before /pricing copy lands more eyes).

### Moat — four reinforcing prongs

1. **ministr Atlas** *(economies of scale)* — curated, weekly-re-indexed network of top OSS repositories. Late entrants must pay the same storage subsidy, recurring compute, and legal/curation overhead we did. The longer Atlas runs, the further the wall.
2. **Polyglot bridge depth** *(applied-research depth)* — `ministr-core/src/code/bridge/` ships detectors for `cgo`, `electron`, `ffi`, `flutter`, `grpc`, `http_route`, `jni`, `napi`, `pyo3`, `tauri`, `uniffi`, `wasm_bindgen` × ~20 language parsers in `lang/`. Each new detector compounds the cross-language graph's value. Years of heuristic tuning to reproduce from a standing start. (Plus `service/solid.rs` and `coherence.rs` in the same lineage.)
3. **Agent-aware primitives** *(integration stickiness)* — `ministr_compress` / `ministr_usage` / `ministr_dropped` / `ministr_extract` and per-session claim + coherence tracking encode AI-agent operational knowledge competitors don't model. Once an agent integrates against these, switching cost is the agent dev's integration time. Compounds with API users, not with our shipped code.
4. **Open-source trust** *(reputational moat)* — counter-positions Sourcegraph's enterprise-only retreat. The local stack stays MIT forever; we never demote OSS features to paid tiers. Hard to dislodge once established as cultural posture.

**Positioning one-liner**: *"Hosted, polyglot, agent-aware code intelligence — the MCP layer every AI agent calls into. MIT core, paid cloud."*

## 2. Open-core split principles

> **Current state, flagged.** The workspace is presently `license = "LicenseRef-Proprietary"` (see `Cargo.toml`). The open-core thesis below requires a **license flip on the core crates to MIT** before F1 begins — captured as **F0** in §4.

### Principles

1. **Local-first stays MIT, forever.** Anything that runs on the user's box is open. The existing six workspace members — `ministr-core`, `ministr-api`, `ministr-daemon`, `ministr-mcp`, `ministr-cli`, `ministr-app/src-tauri` — flip to `MIT` in F0. All 19 MCP tools, the SOLID detector (`ministr-core/src/service/solid.rs`), the cross-language bridge graph (`ministr-core/src/code/bridge/` — 12 detectors), coherence (`ministr-core/src/coherence.rs`), claim extraction (`ministr-core/src/extraction/`), and the ~20 language parsers in `ministr-core/src/code/lang/` are all open and stay open.

2. **Multi-tenant cloud is closed.** A new crate `ministr-cloud` (license `LicenseRef-Proprietary`) holds: tenant data model, Stripe glue + webhook receiver, GitHub-OAuth IdP adapter, quota enforcement middleware, billing portal handlers. None of this code is useful on the local stack — it only exists because we are running a multi-tenant service.

3. **Compliance + enterprise is closed.** Another new crate `ministr-enterprise` (proprietary) holds: SSO/SAML, OIDC federation, immutable audit log + SIEM export, license-key gating, the on-prem image entrypoint. Customers who self-host this tier pay for a license key.

4. **Atlas is closed.** A third new crate `ministr-atlas` (proprietary) holds: curated repo list, scheduler, re-index cron, license filter, opt-out registry. This is the moat made code; keeping it closed is part of the wall.

5. **Never demote OSS features to paid.** Borrowed verbatim from GitLab's stewardship handbook: *"When a feature is open source we won't move that feature to a paid tier."* New features land in the right tier from day one. Removing an MIT feature is allowed only when the feature itself is being removed from the whole product (not when it's being moved behind a paywall).

6. **Self-hosted single-user MCP serve must remain fully featured.** A user who runs `ministr serve --transport http --oauth` on their own box gets the complete tool surface, OAuth issuer included, private-repo PAT path included, bundle export/import included, all 19 MCP tools included. The cloud product sells *hosting + scale + team + compliance*, not the toolset itself.

### Resulting workspace shape

```
ministr/                              license
├── ministr-core/                     MIT  (flip in F0)
├── ministr-api/                      MIT  (flip in F0)
├── ministr-daemon/                   MIT  (flip in F0)
├── ministr-mcp/                      MIT  (flip in F0)
├── ministr-cli/                      MIT  (flip in F0)
├── ministr-app/src-tauri/            MIT  (flip in F0)
├── ministr-cloud/      (NEW, F1)     LicenseRef-Proprietary
├── ministr-enterprise/ (NEW, F5)     LicenseRef-Proprietary
└── ministr-atlas/      (NEW, F2.6)   LicenseRef-Proprietary
```

The split aligns with the GitLab template: *"GitLab's open core is published under an MIT open source license. The rest is source-available."* We adopt MIT for the same reason — minimum friction for contributors, integrators, and AI tools that need to vendor the SDK.

## 3. Tier matrix

> Decision **B3** (resolved earlier): **no Free Cloud tier.** The local stack is the free product; the cloud is paid from $20/mo.

| Tier | Price | Indexing lane | Corpora | Private repos | Atlas | Team | Audit | On-prem |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| **Local** | free (MIT) | local CPU | unlimited (your disk) | yes (PAT) | — | — | — | yes, self-host |
| **Pro** | **$20/mo** | shared fast lane (≤2 min queue p95) | 10 hosted | yes (GitHub App) | unlimited reads | — | — | — |
| **Team** | **$30/seat/mo** (3-seat min, $90/mo floor) | priority queue (jumps Pro) | 50 / org | yes | unlimited + annotation overlays | yes (orgs, ACL, dashboard, named API keys, Slack/Discord webhook, bridge visualizer) | audit-light, 90-day retention | — |
| **Enterprise** | **contact** (target $50K+/yr) | dedicated pool + SLA | unlimited | yes | unlimited + in-VPC mirror | yes | immutable audit + SIEM export | yes, license-gated image + Helm |

### Price anchors

- **Pro $20** lands at Cursor Pro parity ($20) and 2× Copilot Pro ($10). Justified by Atlas access + private-repo cloning + the hosted multi-language indexing — value Copilot Pro doesn't ship. We are not an IDE assistant; we are the substrate underneath.
- **Team $30/seat** matches Greptile ($30/seat for 50 reviews/mo) but delivers a different product: unlimited queries against an org-owned + Atlas-blended index, not 50 PR reviews. Undercuts Cursor Business ($40) by $10 and Cody Enterprise ($49) by $19.
- **Enterprise $50K+/yr** floor mirrors Sourcegraph's published Enterprise minimum ($50–75K/yr). Below that floor, customers should buy Team; the Enterprise SKU exists for SSO/audit/on-prem buyers.

### How the matrix maps to the closed crates

- **Pro** features (private-repo App, fast lane, Atlas reads) live in `ministr-cloud`.
- **Team** features (orgs, ACL, dashboard, webhooks, visualizer) live in `ministr-cloud`. Audit-light's data path also lives there; the immutable upgrade is `ministr-enterprise`.
- **Enterprise** features (SSO/SAML, OIDC, immutable audit, on-prem license-key gating, CMK) live in `ministr-enterprise`.
- **Atlas** access at any paid tier reads from `ministr-atlas`.

### The seam that makes this enforceable

A single `Plan` enum (`Pro`, `Team`, `Enterprise`) attached to the resolved `Tenant` at `ministr-mcp/src/auth/middleware.rs` (the existing token-resolution path) — every handler reads `Tenant.plan` from request extensions and a quota middleware short-circuits with **HTTP 402 + JSON paywall payload** when the request exceeds the tier's caps. Atlas access is just another quota check. (Greenfield: `grep -E "Plan|Tenant" ministr-mcp/src/auth/*.rs` returns empty today — no retrofit risk.)

## 4. Phased plan

> Notation: `[ ]` = todo · `[x]` = done · `[~]` = in flight. **No time estimates.**

### F0 — License flip (pre-launch, blocks F1)

- [x] **F0.1** Flip `license` from `LicenseRef-Proprietary` to `MIT` in the six core crate `Cargo.toml`s (workspace `[workspace.package]` + per-crate overrides as needed): `ministr-core`, `ministr-api`, `ministr-daemon`, `ministr-mcp`, `ministr-cli`, `ministr-app/src-tauri`.
- [x] **F0.2** Add `LICENSE-MIT` at repo root.
- [x] **F0.3** README + `ministr.ai` landing copy state the open-core posture explicitly (MIT core + proprietary cloud/enterprise/atlas).
- [x] **F0.4** Public commitment to the never-demote promise in `CONTRIBUTING.md` or `STEWARDSHIP.md` (borrow GitLab phrasing).
- **Validation:** `cargo metadata --format-version 1 | jq -r '.packages[] | "\(.name) \(.license)"'` shows MIT for all six core crates; the three new crates are not yet present (introduced in F1.1, F2.6, F5.4 respectively).

### F1 — Foundation (gates all paid tiers)

> Persistence + tenancy + identity + metering. Until this is done, every other phase is fiction.

- [x] **F1.1 Postgres + blob HNSW persistence** *(depends on F0; blocks F1.2, F1.4, F4.2)*
  - [x] Add `ministr-cloud` crate (`LicenseRef-Proprietary`); first carrier of cloud-only types.
  - [x] `azure-native` Azure Database for PostgreSQL Flexible Server (Burstable B1ms tier) module in `deploy/azure/lib/postgres.ts`; outputs `pgConnectionString` to `Pulumi.prod.yaml`.
  - [x] Extend `OAuthBackend` enum (`ministr-mcp/src/auth/storage/mod.rs`) with a `Postgres` variant; add `ministr-mcp/src/auth/storage/postgres.rs` mirroring `sqlite.rs`.
  - [x] Extend `JobQueueBackend` enum (`ministr-mcp/src/admin/jobs/mod.rs`) with a `Postgres` variant; add `ministr-mcp/src/admin/jobs/postgres.rs` mirroring `sqlite.rs`.
  - [x] HNSW serialised **per corpus** to Azure Blob (one blob = one corpus's vectors + metadata); cold-start path restores the blob into `/tmp` on pod boot; warm pods hold the in-memory cache. Reason for blob over pgvector: reuses the shipped `.ministr-index` export/import code in `ministr-core/src/bundle.rs`, sidesteps pgvector's 2000-dim HNSW ceiling, and keeps the SQLite path for self-hosted unchanged.
  - [x] Carry-over: replace the `/tmp` rsync hack with a proper "build on /tmp, fsync to blob, atomically swap the manifest" pipeline.
  - **Validation:** kill a pod mid-query; new pod restores from blob within 60s; corpora list shows zero drift; concurrent indexing across two pods on *different* corpora both complete; p95 query latency on warm cache stays sub-300ms.

- [x] **F1.2 Multi-tenant data model** *(depends on F1.1; blocks F2, F3, F4)*
  - [x] Schema in Postgres (migrations in `ministr-cloud/migrations/`):
    - `users(id, email, github_id, plan_id, stripe_customer_id, created_at)`
    - `orgs(id, name, plan_id, stripe_customer_id, billing_email, created_at)`
    - `org_members(org_id, user_id, role)`  — role ∈ {owner, admin, member}
    - `corpora(id, owner_user_id|owner_org_id, name, source_url, status, last_indexed_at, byte_size, vec_count)`
    - `corpus_acl(corpus_id, user_id|team_id, scope)`  — for shared corpora
    - `api_keys(id, owner_user_id|owner_org_id, name, hash, scopes, last_used_at, expires_at)`
    - `usage_events(tenant_id, kind, count, ts)`  — feeds F1.4
    - `audit_events(org_id, actor, action, resource, ts, ip, ua)`  — feeds F3.7 / F5.3
  - [x] **Tenant resolution at `ministr-mcp/src/auth/middleware.rs`** — the existing token-resolution flow gains a `Tenant { subject, org_id, plan }` struct attached to request extensions. Every downstream handler reads `Tenant` and filters queries by `owner_*`. Integration test: token A's request for corpus B (owned by user C) returns 404, not 403, to avoid leaking existence.
  - [x] **Bridge `MinistrServer` (`/mcp`) ↔ daemon's `CorpusRegistry`** (carry-over from previous plan) — both surfaces now read the same Postgres-backed registry through a shared `Arc<CorpusRegistry>` in `cmd_serve_http` (`ministr-cli/src/commands.rs`).
  - [x] OAuth token persistence (carry-over) — `oauth_clients` + `oauth_tokens` tables; `OAuthBackend::Postgres` becomes the cloud default.
  - **Validation:** RBAC test matrix — 4 token types (Pro user / Team owner / Team member / Pro user different org) × 4 resources (own corpus / org corpus / other-tenant corpus / Atlas) = 16 assertions all green.

- [x] **F1.3 GitHub OAuth as cloud IdP** *(depends on F1.2; blocks F2.1)*
  - [x] `IdentityProvider` trait in `ministr-cloud/src/idp/` so future Google/Microsoft/OIDC providers slot in; existing self-issued issuer in `ministr-mcp/src/auth/` remains the default for local/self-hosted serve.
  - [x] GitHub OAuth app registration (deployment env: `MINISTR_GITHUB_CLIENT_ID`/`MINISTR_GITHUB_CLIENT_SECRET`/`MINISTR_CLOUD_BASE_URL`); `users.github_id` populated on first sign-in via `upsert_github_user` from the `/auth/github/callback` handler; "Sign in with GitHub" button (with inline Octocat mark) wired to `cloud_authenticate_github` Tauri command in `ministr-app/src/components/surfaces/CloudPanel.tsx`. Federated bearer token minted through new `OAuthStore::issue_bearer_token` so existing scope middleware validates it unchanged.
  - [x] **OS keychain for token storage** (carry-over) — Tauri side migrates from plain JSON at `<data-dir>/cloud.json` to `keyring`/`security-framework` per OS.
  - [x] **Proper OS RNG for PKCE** (carry-over) — replace the current SHA-256-over-nanos in `ministr-app/src-tauri/src/commands_cloud.rs::cloud_authenticate` with `getrandom`.
  - **Validation:** click "Sign in with GitHub" → browser handshakes via PKCE → token lands in OS keychain → Tauri panel shows the GitHub avatar + email; restart the app and confirm the token survives.

- [x] **F1.4 Usage metering pipeline** *(depends on F1.2; blocks F1.5, F2.3)*
  - [x] `usage_events(tenant_id, kind, count, ts)` write path; kinds emitted: `corpus.indexed`, `index.minutes`, `query.served`, `atlas.queries`.
  - [x] Extend existing `record_activity` middleware (`ministr-daemon/src/activity.rs`) to also write a billable `usage_events` row alongside the in-memory activity ring.
  - [x] Aggregator cron rollup per day (Azure Container Apps Job) → daily `usage_rollups` table.
  - [x] `GET /api/v1/billing/usage` endpoint; Tauri panel + future `/billing` web UI consume it.
  - [x] Carry-over: App Insights cost/latency badges in the Tauri overview tile.
  - **Validation:** indexing a 1MB repo emits `corpus.indexed=1` + `index.minutes≈$measured`; 100 ministr_survey calls emit `query.served=100`; daily rollup matches the event sum within ±0.

- [x] **F1.5 Stripe customer/subscription scaffolding** *(depends on F1.4)*
  - [x] On sign-up, create a Stripe Customer (no subscription yet); store `users.stripe_customer_id` via `set_stripe_customer_id` from the GitHub callback when `upsert_github_user` reports `inserted=true` (Postgres `xmax=0` trick). Stripe credentials supplied via `MINISTR_STRIPE_SECRET_KEY`. Orgs deferred to F3.1 — `orgs.stripe_customer_id` column already exists.
  - [x] Use Stripe **Meters + meter events** — `StripeClient::report_meter_event` lands at `ministr-cloud/src/billing/stripe_api.rs`, form-encoded `POST /v1/billing/meter_events` with native `identifier` dedup (no `Idempotency-Key` header). One meter per `usage_events.kind`; no internal caller yet — F2.3 enforcement wires it in.
  - [x] Webhook receiver (`POST /webhooks/stripe`) in `ministr-cloud`; verifies signature; on `customer.subscription.updated`/`deleted` events updates `users.plan_id`/`orgs.plan_id`.
  - [x] No enforcement yet — wired and tolerant. Stripe call failures in the GitHub callback log + continue rather than blocking sign-in. Enforcement lands in F2.3.
  - **Validation:** in Stripe test mode, create a subscription via Checkout (the F2.4 path) → webhook fires → `users.plan_id` flips to `pro` → `Tenant.plan` resolves to `Pro` on the next request.

### F2 — Pro launch (first revenue moment)

> Deps: all of F1. This is when `ministr.ai/pricing` goes up and we accept money.

- [x] **F2.1 GitHub App for private repos** *(depends on F1.3)*
  - [x] Register a GitHub App (org-owned) — deployment step. Scopes: `contents:read` + `metadata:read`. Installable per-repo or org-wide. Credentials supplied via `MINISTR_GITHUB_APP_ID` + `MINISTR_GITHUB_APP_PRIVATE_KEY` (PEM contents).
  - [x] `ministr-cloud/src/github/app.rs` — `GitHubAppClient` mints **installation access tokens** (~1hr TTL, cached in-process with 10-min proactive eviction). RS256-signed JWT as the App (9-min lifetime + 60s `iat` backdate), exchange at `POST /app/installations/{id}/access_tokens`.
  - [x] `clone_repo` (`ministr-daemon/src/daemon.rs:474`) accepts an optional `github_installation_id` on `CloneRepoRequest`; when set + daemon's `AppState.installation_minter` is wired, the token is minted on demand and spliced into the URL as `https://x-access-token:<token>@github.com/...`. Self-hosted serve leaves the field `None` and the PAT-in-URL fallback remains. Open-core seam: `InstallationTokenMinter` trait in `ministr-api/src/github_app.rs` (MIT), concrete impl in `ministr-cloud` (proprietary).
  - [x] Tauri "Clone private repo" dialog (`CloudPanel.tsx`) — adds an optional "GitHub App installation ID" input that threads through `cloud_clone_repo` → daemon. Token never reaches the desktop.
  - **Validation:** unauth'd user clicks "Clone private repo" → bounced through GitHub App install → returns to the panel with a fresh installation ID → clone + index succeeds; the token is **not** persisted server-side — minted on demand per indexing job.

- [x] **F2.2 Fast indexing lane** *(depends on F1.1, F1.2)*
  - [x] `priority SMALLINT NOT NULL DEFAULT 0` column added to `indexer_jobs` (idempotent `ALTER TABLE ADD COLUMN IF NOT EXISTS` in `ministr-mcp/src/admin/jobs/postgres.rs`'s `ensure_schema`). `JobQueue::enqueue` signature gained a `priority: i16` parameter; the reindex handler reads `Tenant.plan` from request extensions and tags via the new `ministr_mcp::auth::queue_priority(Plan) -> i16` (moved into MIT so the open-core handler doesn't depend on `ministr-cloud`).
  - [x] Postgres `claim_next` orders by `priority DESC, created_at ASC`; covering index `idx_indexer_jobs_status_priority_created` matches. In-memory backend mirrors the same ordering. Team jumps Pro; Enterprise jumps both. Dedicated Enterprise pool (separate Container Apps Environment) is an F5.5 deployment step.
  - [x] Per-IP + per-tenant rate limits — `ministr-cloud/src/ratelimit/` ships a tiny SOLID-layered token-bucket: `TokenBucket` trait (ISP) + `InMemoryBucket` impl + `KeyExtractor` fn (DIP) + `RateLimitConfig` composition + axum `from_fn_with_state` middleware. Two layers stack on `daemon_write_router` in cloud mode: per-IP (20-burst, 0.5/s refill) and per-tenant (60-burst, 1/s refill). Self-hosted serve mounts neither. Returns 429 + `Retry-After`.
  - **Validation:** synthetic load — enqueue 20 Pro jobs + 1 Team job → Team job clears within 2 min; Pro queue p95 stays ≤2 min.

- [x] **F2.3 Quota enforcement middleware** *(depends on F1.4, F1.5)*
  - [x] Tower middleware in `ministr-cloud/src/quota/` (split SOLID-style across `caps.rs` + `probe.rs` + `rule.rs` + `middleware.rs`). Mounted on `daemon_write_router` AFTER the scope guard and BEFORE the F2.2 rate limit so 402 preempts 429 accounting.
  - [x] Reads `Tenant.plan` from request extensions and the live corpus count from `UsageProbe` (DIP). Today's `RegistryProbe` wraps the daemon's `CorpusRegistry`; Postgres-backed probe for queries/day + indexing-minutes slots in via the same trait when F4.2 daily usage rollups need enforcement.
  - [x] Soft-fail with **HTTP 402 + JSON `{ reason, upgrade_url }`** — `upgrade_url` carries `?from=<plan>` so the cloud landing page lands on the right pricing card. Unit tests assert the spec body byte-for-byte.
  - [x] Atlas access is implemented as `AtlasAccessRule` checking `plan ∈ { Pro, Team, Enterprise }`. Today all paid tiers admit (no free cloud per B3); the rule shape is in place for F2.6 to mount on `GET /atlas/*`.

F2.6 v0 query routes return `503 atlas_not_indexed_yet` for known slugs and `404 unknown_atlas_slug` for unknown ones; F4.2 wires the live read-router once the cron writes blobs.

#### F2 done criterion

A stranger lands on `ministr.ai/pricing`, clicks "Start Pro", completes Stripe Checkout, returns to the Tauri panel showing a Pro plan badge, signs in with GitHub, installs the GitHub App on a private repo, clones it, queries it, AND queries Atlas v0 — all unattended in under five minutes.

### F3 — Team launch (second revenue moment)

- [x] **F3.1 Orgs + members + invites** *(complete except deferred bounce handling)* — split into a/b/c. All core sub-chunks landed.
  - [x] **F3.1a Org CRUD + first-user-as-owner + member listing** *(depends on F1.2; greenfield — `grep "Org\|Team\|Workspace" ministr-mcp/src/auth/*.rs` is empty)*
    - [x] `ministr-cloud/src/orgs/` module — `repo.rs` (transactional `create_org` inserts `orgs` row + owner `org_members` row in one txn; `list_orgs_for_user` joins through `org_members`; `member_role` + `list_org_members` for membership checks) and `routes.rs` (axum 0.8 router behind `ministr:read`).
    - [x] `POST /api/v1/orgs` — caller from `Extension<Tenant>` becomes the `owner`; default `plan_id = "team"` (matches §3 tier). Returns the new org + the caller's `role`.
    - [x] `GET /api/v1/orgs` — lists orgs the caller is a member of, with their role. Filters strictly through `org_members` so cross-tenant orgs stay invisible.
    - [x] `GET /api/v1/orgs/{id}/members` — requires the caller to be a member; returns user_id/email/role rows. Non-members get 403, not 404 (the caller can't probe org existence anyway because the route is auth-gated).
    - [x] Mounted in `cmd_serve_http` only when `cloud_pool` is `Some` — self-hosted serve has no orgs surface.

    - [x] **F3.1b-i Invite-link generation + acceptance via GitHub callback** *(2026-05-20)*
      - [x] New migration `0004_org_invites.sql`: `org_invites(id, org_id, email, token_hash, role, invited_by, created_at, accepted_at, expires_at)` with partial indexes on `token_hash WHERE accepted_at IS NULL` (consume hot path) and `(org_id, created_at DESC) WHERE accepted_at IS NULL` (admin list).
      - [x] New module `ministr-cloud/src/orgs/invites.rs`: `create_invite` mints a 256-bit token (CSPRNG → base64url), stores only its SHA-256 hex digest, returns the raw token in `CreatedInvite` exactly once. `consume_invite` runs `SELECT … FOR UPDATE` → expiry check → `org_members` insert with `ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING` → mark `accepted_at` in one transaction.
      - [x] `POST /api/v1/orgs/{id}/invites` route (owner/admin authz via `member_role`). Body: `{email, role?}` (role defaults to `member`, restricted to `member|admin` — minting owners forbidden via this path). Returns `{invite_id, invite_url, role, expires_at}`. Email is validated (non-empty + contains '@') without round-tripping to Postgres on malformed inputs.
      - [x] `OrgsState::with_cloud_base_url` builder + `cmd_serve_http` wiring so the returned `invite_url` is absolute (`{cloud_base}/auth/github/start?invite={raw}`). Self-hosted serve omits the orgs router entirely.

The callback handler calls `consume_invite` AFTER `upsert_github_user` succeeds; unknown/expired/already-accepted invites log + proceed (sign-in still mints a bearer token — recipient can request a fresh link). Existing PKCE + state-CSRF guarantees stay intact.
      - [x] Four pure-Rust unit tests cover the token plumbing (entropy floor, alphabet, determinism of hash, collision rejection). Postgres-integration coverage of `create_invite` + `consume_invite` is gated on `MINISTR_TEST_PG_URL` per the existing convention; not exercised in default cargo test.

        - [x] New `MailSender` trait + `InviteMessage` struct in `ministr-api/src/mail.rs` (MIT open-core seam, fire-and-forget shape mirroring `AuditSink` / `UsageSink`). `InviteMessage` carries `to_email`, `invite_url`, `org_name`, `inviter_name`, `role`.
        - [x] `LogOnlyMailSender` in `ministr-cloud/src/mail.rs` — safe-default impl that logs the would-be send at info level WITHOUT the invite URL (URL is a bearer credential — logging it would let log-readers escalate to org membership). Recipient / org / role / inviter all logged for operator triage.

That tightening lands with the concrete provider (F3.1b-ii-b) because OOB-delivered links (the F3.1b-i shape) shouldn't be retroactively restricted — the URL was the bearer when the invite was minted.

Outcome enum distinguishes `NoSubscription` (org pre-Checkout), `AlreadyAtTarget` (idempotent re-sync), and `Updated { prior, new }`. Idempotency key `sync-seats-{sub_id}-q{N}` collapses retries.

    - [x] **F3.1c-iii Personal-Pro → org transfer** *(2026-05-21)*
      - [x] `StripeClient::cancel_active_subscription_for_customer(customer_id) -> CancelSubscriptionOutcome` lands in `ministr-cloud/src/billing/stripe_api.rs`. Two-call dance against the Stripe API: `GET /v1/subscriptions?customer=X&status=active&limit=1` finds the active sub; `DELETE /v1/subscriptions/{id}` cancels immediately. Outcome enum distinguishes `NoSubscription` (no-op idempotent re-call) from `Cancelled { subscription_id }` (Stripe state mutated). Stripe API doesn't natively support cross-Customer subscription transfer, so the path is cancel-then-recreate; the Stripe proration credit on cancel covers the unused portion of the user's Pro period.
      - [x] New module `ministr-cloud/src/orgs/transfer_personal.rs` — `transfer_personal_to_org(pool, stripe, user_id, _org_id) -> Result<TransferPersonalOutcome, TransferPersonalError>` orchestrator. Looks up `users.stripe_customer_id`, falls through to `NoPersonalCustomer` when NULL (deployment without `MINISTR_STRIPE_SECRET_KEY` or pre-F1.5 row); otherwise delegates to the Stripe cancel helper. Three outcomes: `NoPersonalCustomer` / `NoActiveSubscription` / `Cancelled { subscription_id }`. `org_id` parameter is informational; route handler verifies org membership before calling the orchestrator.
      - [x] `POST /api/v1/orgs/{id}/transfer-personal-sub` route in `orgs/routes.rs`. Authz: owner OR admin of the target org (mirrors F3.2-iv-a's transfer-handler — member-role callers can't accept incoming subscriptions). Response is wire-stable: `{ outcome: "cancelled" | "no_active_subscription" | "no_personal_customer", subscription_id?: string }` so the Tauri UI can render one of three messages without inspecting the optional id.
      - [x] F3.7 audit emission on the `Cancelled` arm only: `AuditEntry::new("personal_sub.cancelled", "{subscription_id}:->{org_id}").with_org(org_id).with_actor(user_id)`. `with_org` means F3.5 webhook fan-out routes to the org's subscribers — Slack channels get a "ci-prod owner moved a personal Pro into your org" event automatically. No-op outcomes (`NoActiveSubscription` / `NoPersonalCustomer`) don't emit audit so retries don't pollute the feed.
      - [x] **Honest scope choice — no Team-sub-mint half**. This chunk cancels the personal sub; the user then runs Checkout for the org's Team plan via the existing F2.4 flow (`POST /api/v1/billing/checkout` against the org's `stripe_customer_id`). Combining both steps into one "atomic transfer" endpoint would require a hosted Checkout redirect chain that the existing F2.4 UI doesn't compose with; keeping them separate matches Stripe's intended UX where the user re-confirms billing details on the new plan.
      - [x] **Honest scope choice — no Tauri UI**. Mirrors the F3.2-iv-a split: backend lands first; UI follows in a separate chunk. Manual smoke today is via `curl` against `mcp.ministr.ai/api/v1/orgs/{id}/transfer-personal-sub` with a Bearer token.

Postgres-integration coverage of the orchestrator gated on `MINISTR_TEST_PG_URL` per convention.
      - **Validation:** cargo workspace check + cargo test green (196 ministr-cloud tests, +6 new); cargo clippy `--pedantic -D warnings` clean. Live: an existing Pro user `POSTs` to `/api/v1/orgs/{id}/transfer-personal-sub` → owner/admin authz passes → personal sub cancels in Stripe test mode → response carries `{ outcome: "cancelled", subscription_id: "sub_..." }` → user then runs Checkout for the org's Team plan via F2.4. Deferred to next deploy + Stripe test-mode session.
      - [x] **F3.1c-iii UI** *(2026-05-21)* — Tauri "Move my Pro into this org" button + ConfirmDialog landed in `OrgUsageSection`.
        - [x] `cloud_transfer_personal_sub(org_id) -> CloudTransferPersonalResponse` Tauri command in `commands_cloud.rs` mirrors the F3.2-iv-b transfer-corpus pattern (`authed_client` + `CommandError`). Registered in `main.rs` `invoke_handler`.

    - [x] New migration `0005_cloud_corpus_acl.sql` — `cloud_corpus_acl(corpus_id TEXT, org_id UUID NULL, user_id UUID NULL, scope CHECK IN ('read','write'), granted_by, created_at)` with FK to `cloud_corpora.corpus_id` (TEXT key matches the live table; F1.2's UUID-keyed `corpus_acl` had no callers and is left untouched). Two partial-unique indexes (org / user) for fast hot-path lookup; one created_at-desc index for the admin list.
    - [x] New module `ministr-cloud/src/orgs/corpus_acl.rs` — `share_with_org` (UPSERT on `(corpus_id, org_id)`), `revoke_org_share` (idempotent DELETE), `list_acl` (admin enumeration), `corpus_owner_tenant` (authz lookup), `acl_grants_access` (join `cloud_corpus_acl ↔ org_members` for tenant access check).
    - [x] Three routes on the orgs router: `POST /api/v1/corpora/{id}/share` (owner-only authz + caller must be in target org; rejects non-`read` scope; admits `'write'` reserved for future); `DELETE /api/v1/corpora/{id}/share/{org_id}` (idempotent 204); `GET /api/v1/corpora/{id}/share` (owner-only list).
    - [x] `PostgresTenantCorpusFilter::allowed` (F2.x-b) extended: when direct ownership doesn't match, consult the same `cloud_corpus_acl × org_members` join. Single extra `query_opt` on the deny path; hot path (direct owner) unchanged.
    - [x] One serde round-trip test verifies the `AclEntry` wire shape. Full integration coverage gated on `MINISTR_TEST_PG_URL` per the existing convention.
    - **Validation:** cargo test workspace green; clippy pedantic clean. Live: owner POSTs share → member of granted org can `ministr_survey project=corpus_id` (admitted by the extended filter); owner DELETEs grant → next call denies via the typo-tolerance shape.

  - [x] **F3.2-iii Tenant + ACL-aware `GET /api/v1/corpora`** *(2026-05-20)*
    - [x] Surprise on entry: today's `list_corpora` returns EVERY in-memory corpus to EVERY authenticated tenant — both a UX gap (members of a shared org couldn't see the corpus) AND a tenant-isolation leak (cross-tenant existence visible to anyone). F3.2-iii closes both.
    - [x] New trait `TenantCorpusVisibility` in `ministr-api/src/tenant_filter.rs` (MIT open-core seam, mirrors `TenantCorpusFilter`). Default impl returns `Ok(None)` ⇒ "no filter, return everything" (self-hosted serve). `PostgresTenantCorpusFilter` (the existing F2.x-b struct in `ministr-cloud`) now implements both traits — single instance powers MCP gate AND daemon list.
    - [x] `AppState::with_corpus_visibility` builder + new `corpus_visibility` field. `list_corpora` handler reads `Extension<TenantId>` and the optional filter; when both present, it asks the filter for the visible-set, intersects with `registry.list()`, and returns the survivors. Storage errors fail-closed (empty list rather than cross-tenant leak).
    - [x] SQL: `(SELECT corpus_id FROM cloud_corpora WHERE tenant_id = $1) UNION (SELECT a.corpus_id FROM cloud_corpus_acl a JOIN org_members m ON m.org_id = a.org_id WHERE a.org_id IS NOT NULL AND m.user_id = $1::uuid)`. Both arms index-friendly via the F1.2 + F3.2-i indexes.
    - [x] Wired in `cmd_serve_http`: one concrete `Arc<PostgresTenantCorpusFilter>` cast to both `Arc<dyn TenantCorpusFilter>` (MCP) and `Arc<dyn TenantCorpusVisibility>` (daemon AppState). Same pool, identical semantics across both surfaces.
    - **Validation:** cargo test workspace green; clippy pedantic clean. Live: two tenants with their own corpora, share a corpus from tenant A to org X (containing tenant B); tenant B's `GET /api/v1/corpora` returns A's shared corpus, tenant C's (not in X) does not.
  - [x] **F3.2-iv Corpus transfer flow** *(personal → org owner change; complete)* — split into iv-a (backend) and iv-b (Tauri UI). Both landed.
    - [x] **F3.2-iv-a Backend transfer endpoint + helper** *(2026-05-21)*
      - [x] `transfer_corpus_to_org(pool, corpus_id, target_org_id, caller_user_id) -> Result<TransferOutcome, OrgError>` in `ministr-cloud/src/orgs/corpus_acl.rs`. Single transaction: `SELECT cloud_corpora FOR UPDATE` (serialises against concurrent share/transfer) → ownership check (caller's UUID must equal current `tenant_id`) → `UPDATE cloud_corpora SET tenant_id = org_uuid` → `INSERT cloud_corpus_acl` with `scope = 'write'` (ON CONFLICT DO UPDATE mirrors `share_with_org`).
      - [x] `TransferOutcome` enum distinguishes `Transferred { previous_tenant_id, new_tenant_id }`, `AlreadyOnTarget` (idempotent re-call, returns 200 + `transferred=false` so retries don't pollute the audit feed), and `NotOwner` (collapses "corpus missing", "tenant_id NULL", "tenant_id != caller" into one 403 — existence-leak-resistant, mirrors `assert_corpus_owner`).
      - [x] New route `POST /api/v1/corpora/{corpus_id}/transfer` on the orgs router. Authz: caller must be owner/admin of the target org (mirrors the F3.2-i share-handler check — member-role callers can't accept incoming corpora, only org owners/admins can). Returns 201 on first transfer with a `TransferResponse { corpus_id, previous_tenant_id, new_tenant_id, transferred }` body.
      - [x] F3.7 audit emission on the `Transferred` path only: `AuditEntry::new("corpus.transferred", "{corpus_id}:{prev}->{new}").with_org(new_tenant_id).with_actor(user_id)`. `with_org` means the F3.5 webhook fan-out routes to the receiving org's subscribers — Slack channels get a "ci-prod corpus moved into your org" event automatically.
      - [x] **Visibility — no filter rewrite needed.** The transfer's ACL insert means existing F3.2-iii visibility logic (`cloud_corpus_acl JOIN org_members`) surfaces the corpus to every member of the target org. The caller (who used to own it via direct `tenant_id` match) now sees it via the same ACL JOIN as any other org member. Bonus: a future transfer-back-to-user wouldn't strand the ACL row — it stays valid for the org's continuing access.
      - [x] **Honest scope choice — no transfer-back-to-user path** *(deferred)*. F3.2-iv-a only handles user → org. Once tenant_id is the org UUID, the caller isn't the owner anymore — they can't issue a second transfer. A future iteration can add an org-owner-can-transfer-back path; would need a different authz check (member_role on the source org).
      - [x] Two new unit tests cover the outcome enum's wire shape (variants distinguishable; `Transferred` carries both sides). Postgres-integration coverage of the actual transaction gated on `MINISTR_TEST_PG_URL` per convention.
      - **Validation:** cargo workspace test green (no FAILED entries); clippy `--pedantic -D warnings` clean. Live: owner POSTs to `/api/v1/corpora/{id}/transfer` with `{ org_id }` → corpus's `tenant_id` flips to the org UUID, `cloud_corpus_acl` gets a `scope='write'` row, audit event fires with `org_id=target_org`, F3.5 webhook fan-out delivers to subscribed channels. Deferred to next deploy.
    - [x] **F3.2-iv-b Tauri UI** *(2026-05-21)*
      - [x] `cloud_transfer_corpus_to_org(corpus_id, org_id) -> CloudTransferResponse` Tauri command in `commands_cloud.rs` mirrors the F3.2-ii share-command pattern (authed_client + CommandError). Registered in `main.rs` `invoke_handler`.
      - [x] `cloudClient.ts` exposes `CloudTransferResponse` type and `transferCorpusToOrg` wrapper.
      - [x] **UI surface choice — extended `ShareDialog`** instead of a separate dialog. The "Transfer ownership" section lives below the existing "Share with org" + "Current shares" sections, separated by a border. Org-picker is restricted to orgs where the caller is **owner or admin** (`o.role === "owner" || o.role === "admin"`) — the cloud rejects member-only callers with 403, so the dropdown mirrors what the server admits, avoiding a 403-feedback round-trip.
      - [x] **Two-step flow**: select org → click "Transfer…" → `ConfirmDialog` (danger tone) spells out the consequence ("Org members will be able to see it. You will still see it via your org membership but the org owns it.") → confirm fires the request. A stray click on the section header can't move a corpus by accident.

Both refresh the dialog state AND fire `onTransferred?.()` so the parent `CorporaSection` re-fetches the corpus list (the now-org-owned corpus reappears under its new tenant context via the F3.2-iii ACL × org_members visibility path).

Live: owner picks an org where they're owner/admin → Transfer… → ConfirmDialog → confirm → corpus disappears from the personal corpus list (re-renders as owned-by-org-via-ACL on next refresh) → F3.5 webhook subscribers get the `corpus.transferred` audit event. Today's partial rows render with `day=today (partial)` so the spreadsheet preserves the rolled-up vs. live distinction. Response carries `Content-Disposition: attachment; filename=org-<sanitised>-usage-<N>d.csv` so receivers that follow the header get a sensible default name.
    - [x] `usage_to_csv(&OrgUsageResponse) -> String` helper (pure, no I/O) with RFC-4180 quoting: any field containing `,`, `"`, `\n`, or `\r` is wrapped in double quotes and embedded quotes are doubled. `sanitize_for_filename` strips `../` and other non-alphanumeric punctuation; empty input collapses to `org` so the disposition header is never blank.

Returns the saved path or `None` on cancel. CSV never lands in the JS renderer — 50K-row finance exports don't bloat IPC.

    - [x] **Projection scope choice** — v0 surfaces unit projections only (queries, index min, atlas), no `$` amount. Per-meter overage prices live in Stripe's dashboard, not in our env; finance can multiply against the live invoice line items if they need a cost estimate. Tightening to fetch the meter prices from Stripe + display dollars is a follow-up if needed.
    - [x] **Honest scope choice** — projection denominator uses the lookback window (`range_days`) rather than the active Stripe billing cycle. Calendar-month alignment is fine for the 30-day default and avoids coupling the dashboard to per-tenant subscription anchors. Cycle anchoring lands if finance asks.

    - [x] **F3.4c-i Scopes-picker UI + backend validation** *(2026-05-21)*
      - [x] New `ALLOWED_API_KEY_SCOPES` const + `validate_scopes(&str) -> Result<String, String>` in `ministr-cloud/src/api_keys.rs`. The four-scope vocabulary (`ministr:read`, `ministr:write`, `ministr:bundle:read`, `ministr:bundle:write`) mirrors `OAuthConfig::default().scopes_supported`; an invariant test (`allowed_scopes_matches_default_signin_scope_set`) asserts lockstep with `DEFAULT_SIGNIN_SCOPE` so future drift between API-key scopes and IdP-minted-bearer scopes shouts in CI rather than silently producing keys the resolver can't honour.
      - [x] `validate_scopes` returns the canonical single-space-separated string on success (so tabs / double spaces collapse uniformly); on failure returns the first unknown token (or empty string for whitespace-only input). The handler maps these to `ApiKeysApiError::UnknownScope(token) -> 400 "unknown_scope: <token>"` and `ApiKeysApiError::InvalidInput("scopes must not be empty") -> 400` respectively.

    - [x] **F3.4c-ii Stale-key detection — audit event + UI badge** *(2026-05-21)*
      - [x] `flag_stale_api_keys(pool, threshold_days, sink) -> StaleApiKeysOutcome` in `ministr-cloud/src/api_keys.rs`. SQL uses `COALESCE(last_used_at, created_at) < now() - make_interval(days => $1::integer)` so never-used-but-old keys are also surfaced; excludes `revoked_at IS NOT NULL` rows. For each match, fires `AuditEntry::new("api_key.stale", key_id).with_actor(owner_user_id)` through the injected sink. Returns `flagged` count + elapsed wall-clock for the cron's structured-log dashboard.
      - [x] `DEFAULT_STALE_API_KEY_DAYS = 90` const matches ROADMAP §F3.4c language. An invariant test asserts the const stays at 90 so future drift must update the ROADMAP first.
      - [x] New `ministr api-keys flag-stale --threshold-days N` CLI subcommand mirrors the `ministr audit prune` shape (`ApiKeysAction::FlagStale`, `cmd_api_keys_flag_stale`). Reads `MINISTR_PG_URL`, opens cloud pool, constructs a `PostgresAuditSink`, calls the helper. Logs `flagged` + `elapsed_ms` + `threshold_days` so the Container Apps Job dashboard can alarm on a runaway pass. Idempotent across runs (deterministic SELECT) — re-running on an unchanged table emits the same set of audit events.
      - [x] **Honest scope choice** — `api_key.stale` events carry `actor = owner_user_id` and `org_id = None` (v0 keys are user-owned per F3.4a; org-owned keys are a future expansion). F3.5 webhook fan-out filters on `org_id IS NOT NULL`, so personal-account stale events won't ring a Slack channel — they land in the audit table for admin review. When F3.4 grows org-owned keys, attach `org_id` and fan-out flips on automatically.
      - [x] Container Apps Job entry (weekly cadence, e.g. `0 0 * * 1`) is a Pulumi deployment task — mirrors the F2.6 atlas-reindex + F3.7c audit-prune Job patterns.
      - [x] Tauri UI: `isStaleApiKey` helper computes staleness client-side using the same `COALESCE(last_used_at, created_at) < now() - 90d` rule the backend SQL uses. `ApiKeysTable` renders a small `stale` badge next to the key name when true; tooltip explains the rule + the weekly cron behavior. `STALE_API_KEY_THRESHOLD_DAYS = 90` const locks the value in lockstep with the backend.
      - [x] Three new backend unit tests: default-threshold matches roadmap, `StaleApiKeysOutcome` shape construction, and the audit-event wire shape (`action="api_key.stale"`, `actor=owner_id`, `org_id=None`). Postgres-integration coverage of the actual SELECT gated on `MINISTR_TEST_PG_URL` per convention.
      - **Validation:** cargo workspace test green; clippy `--pedantic -D warnings` clean; `tsc --noEmit` + `vite build` clean. CLI smoke: `ministr api-keys flag-stale --help` shows the `--threshold-days [default: 90]` flag wired correctly. Live: cron runs → stale keys land in `audit_events` with action=`api_key.stale`, actor=owner → next refresh of the desktop API keys panel shows the `stale` badge. Deferred to next deploy.

  - [x] **F3.5a Backend — table + dispatcher + CRUD + test endpoint** *(2026-05-20)*
    - [x] Migration `0007_webhook_subscriptions.sql` adds the table (id / org_id / url / secret / event_filter / created_by / created_at / last_delivered_at) + `idx_webhook_subs_org` for the per-org hot path.
    - [x] `ministr-cloud/src/webhooks.rs` single-file module: `WebhookSubscription` + repo helpers (`create_subscription`, `list_subscriptions`, `delete_subscription`, `subscription_secret`, `mark_delivered`) + `WebhookDispatcher`. Dispatcher signs payloads as `X-Ministr-Signature: sha256=<hex>` with a paired `X-Ministr-Timestamp` header; HMAC construction is `HMAC-SHA256(secret, timestamp + "." + body)` — same shape as the F1.5 Stripe-inbound verifier so customers can reuse a Stripe-receiver with only a header rename. 3 attempts at 0/5/30s backoff per delivery.
    - [x] Axum routes `POST /api/v1/orgs/{id}/webhooks` (returns `CreatedSubscription` with the one-time secret), `GET /api/v1/orgs/{id}/webhooks` (no secret in response), `DELETE /api/v1/orgs/{id}/webhooks/{wid}`, `POST /api/v1/orgs/{id}/webhooks/{wid}/test` (synthetic `ministr.test` payload — receivers branch on `event` to skip processing). All owner/admin-only.
    - [x] `cmd_serve_http` builds the dispatcher once + wires `WebhooksState` into the orgs-scope router behind `ministr:read`.
    - [x] 6 unit tests cover: HMAC determinism for fixed inputs; timestamp and secret each change the signature; the signature shape matches the F1.5 inbound construction byte-for-byte; minted secrets are url-safe + correct length; retry backoff is monotonic non-decreasing with 0s first attempt.

Live: owner POSTs subscription → receives one-time secret → POSTs to `/test` → receiver gets `ministr.test` JSON with `X-Ministr-Signature: sha256=<hex>` → recomputes HMAC → match.         - [x] Discovery: F3.6-b-ii's naive plan (demo-page fetches `http://localhost:<port>/api/v1/corpora/{id}/bridge/graph` directly) was blocked by the absence of any CORS plumbing in the workspace. Credentials NOT allowed — agents authenticate via `Authorization: Bearer …` rather than cookies; widening to credentials-included would expand the attack surface for no benefit.
        - [x] Layer mounted LAST in `cmd_serve_http` — wraps the final composed router for both OAuth-protected and dev-no-OAuth paths. Boots log `CORS enabled — Access-Control-Allow-Origin headers added` at info when configured, or skip silently when unset.

Correlated subquery (vs LEFT JOIN) avoids the Cartesian-product hazard when multiple symbols share `(file, name)` — overloaded methods, etc.

- [x] **F3.7 Audit-light — 90-day retention** *(2026-05-20, complete)* — split into a/b/c, all landed.
  - [x] **F3.7a Backend write path + list endpoint** *(2026-05-20)*
    - [x] `AuditSink` trait + `AuditEntry` struct in `ministr-api/src/audit.rs` (MIT seam, fire-and-forget shape mirroring `UsageSink`).
    - [x] `PostgresAuditSink` in `ministr-cloud/src/audit.rs` spawns one tokio task per call to INSERT into `audit_events`. Storage hiccup logs but never propagates to the handler.
    - [x] **Plan deviation from roadmap** — original spec said "extend `record_activity` middleware" but that middleware is scoped to `/api/v1/corpora/*` and doesn't see the F3.4a + F3.2-i + F3.1a + F3.1b write actions. F3.7a instead uses inline `audit_sink.record(...)` calls at each handler site. Each handler already knows its action + resource id; the inline approach is shorter and avoids coupling the middleware to per-route action mapping.
    - [x] Seven audit sites landed: `api_key.created` (POST /api_keys), `api_key.revoked` (DELETE /api_keys/{id}), `share.granted` (POST /corpora/{id}/share), `share.revoked` (DELETE /corpora/{id}/share/{org_id}, only on actual state change), `org.created` (POST /orgs), `invite.created` (POST /orgs/{id}/invites). `member.added` and `corpus.*` deferred to F3.7b (member.added needs a hook in the GitHub-callback invite-accept path; corpus.* needs the daemon write router to thread `Tenant`).
    - [x] `OrgsState` + `ApiKeysState` gain `Option<Arc<dyn AuditSink>>` + `with_audit` builders. Self-hosted serve leaves both as `None` so audit emission is a no-op.
    - [x] `GET /api/v1/orgs/{id}/audit` — owner / admin only (members get 403). Cursor pagination via `?before_id=N`; default limit 50, max 200. Mounted behind `ministr:read` scope alongside the orgs router.
    - [x] `cmd_serve_http` builds a single `Arc<dyn AuditSink>` and shares it across orgs + api_keys states; logs the wiring at info on boot.
    - [x] 4 new unit tests cover `AuditEntry` builder chains, `dyn` dispatch through Arc, `AuditListQuery` defaults, and `PostgresAuditSink` trait-impl shape. Postgres-integration coverage of `list_org_audit` gated on `MINISTR_TEST_PG_URL` per convention.
    - **Validation:** cargo test workspace green (2404 tests, 0 failed); clippy `--pedantic -D warnings` clean. Live: owner POSTs an invite + revokes a share → both events appear via `GET /api/v1/orgs/{id}/audit` with the correct actor + resource + ISO timestamp. Deferred to next deploy.
  - [x] **F3.7b Remaining audit sites + filters** *(2026-05-20)*
    - [x] `AppState` gains `audit_sink: Option<Arc<dyn AuditSink>>` + `with_audit_sink` builder, mirroring the established `with_usage_sink` pattern from F1.4.
    - [x] Three daemon handlers (`register_corpus`, `clone_repo`, `unregister_corpus` in `ministr-daemon/src/daemon.rs`) take `Option<Extension<TenantId>>` and call a new `audit_corpus_action` helper after the success branch. Resource = `corpus_id`; actor = `TenantId` when present (None on self-hosted serve). Five emission sites: cloud-mode + inline branches of `register_corpus` (`corpus.created`); cloud-enqueue + inline branches of `clone_repo` (`corpus.cloned`); successful arm of `unregister_corpus` (`corpus.deleted`).
    - [x] `GitHubSigninState` gains `audit: Option<Arc<dyn AuditSink>>` + `with_audit` builder. `handle_github_callback` emits `member.added` after `consume_invite` returns `Accepted`; resource = the new member's `user.id`, `org_id` from the outcome, actor = `user.id` (self-action — the user accepted their own invite).
    - [x] `AuditListQuery` extended with `action` / `actor` / `from_ts` / `to_ts` fields. `list_org_audit` signature changed to take `&AuditListQuery`; the SQL uses `COALESCE`-style nullable filter predicates so the query stays one statement regardless of which filters are set. Postgres optimiser handles `IS NULL` constants at plan time.
    - [x] `cmd_serve_http` wires `PostgresAuditSink` into the daemon state via `with_audit_sink`; `GitHubSigninState` receives the same `Arc<dyn AuditSink>` from the F3.7a orgs block. (Daemon-side sink is a separate `Arc` from the orgs/api_keys sink — both wrap the same pool and emit identical rows; minor duplication, functionally identical.)
    - [x] Two new unit tests cover the extended `AuditListQuery` shape (all-None defaults, serde round-trip of every filter field). Postgres-integration coverage of the filtered SQL gated on `MINISTR_TEST_PG_URL` per convention.
    - **`webhook.created` deferred** — F3.5 (Slack/Discord webhook) hasn't shipped yet; once it does, add one audit call alongside the new subscription insert.
    - **Validation:** cargo workspace check + clippy `--pedantic -D warnings` clean. cargo test workspace: 2272 pass, 0 failure attributable to F3.7b. Pre-existing flaky test `full_flow_survey_read_extract_via_call_tool` fails 1/5 vs 0/5 on main — claim-extraction race, unrelated to audit work (test uses MCP Arc path, bypassing daemon HTTP handlers).
  - [x] **F3.7c Retention pruning cron** *(2026-05-20)*
    - [x] `prune_audit_events(pool, retention_days) -> PruneOutcome` in `ministr-cloud/src/audit.rs`. Uses parameterised `make_interval(days => $1::integer)` so the retention number is strictly bound (never injected). Returns deleted-row count + elapsed wall-clock.
    - [x] `DEFAULT_AUDIT_RETENTION_DAYS = 90` const matches ROADMAP §3 Team-tier audit window. F5.3 immutable audit will retain forever and skip this cron.
    - [x] New `ministr audit prune --retention-days N` CLI subcommand (clap default 90) — mirrors `ministr atlas reindex` shape. `cmd_audit_prune` opens the cloud pool from `MINISTR_PG_URL`, calls the helper, logs `deleted` + `elapsed_ms` + `retention_days` for the cron's structured-log dashboard.

    - [x] Three new unit tests cover the default retention window, `PruneOutcome` shape stability, and the `AuditSink` trait impl. Postgres-integration coverage of the actual DELETE gated on `MINISTR_TEST_PG_URL` per convention.
    - **Validation:** cargo workspace check + clippy `--pedantic -D warnings` clean; cargo test workspace 2407 pass, 0 failed. CLI smoke: `ministr audit prune --help` shows the `--retention-days [default: 90]` flag wired correctly. Live: F3.7 done-criterion ("a row from 91 days ago is gone after the next prune") satisfied by the helper's `WHERE ts < now() - make_interval(days => 90)` clause.
  - **F3.7 done criterion:** an admin invite + accept + role change all appear in the audit feed with correct actor, resource, IP, UA; a row from 91 days ago is gone after the next prune.

#### F3 done criterion

A 3-seat team's owner invites two coworkers by email, all three accept, the owner shares an org-owned corpus, all three can query it, the dashboard shows per-seat query breakdowns matching the live Stripe invoice, a coherence event in the corpus fires a Slack webhook within 30s, and the bridge visualizer renders the corpus's cross-language graph in the web UI.

### F4 — Atlas at scale (the moat, made real)

> Deps: F2.6 (Atlas v0 plumbing). Parallel with F3. **Gated by G.1 legal review** before any expansion beyond the F2.6 pilot 50 repos.

- [ ] **F4.1 Curated 5K repo list + legal scrub** *(depends on G.1)*
  - [ ] **License filter (auto-include)**: permissive only — MIT, Apache-2.0, BSD-2/3, MPL-2.0, ISC, Unlicense, 0BSD. Repo's `LICENSE` file detected via SPDX-license-identifier or text-match against the OSI canonical list. Reject if ambiguous.
  - [ ] **Copyleft (require opinion)**: GPL-2/3, AGPL-3, LGPL — defer to G.1 opinion of counsel. Likely fine for retrieval purposes per the 2025 US fair-use ruling, but get the opinion before going live and document the conclusion in `LEGAL-ATLAS.md`.
  - [ ] **Opt-out registry**: `ministr.ai/atlas/opt-out` — any repo owner can submit their repo for permanent removal; we honor a robots.txt-style `User-agent: ministr-atlas` / `Disallow: /` in the repo's `robots.txt` at the root. Re-check on every weekly cron.
  - [ ] **Public manifest** at `ministr.ai/atlas/manifest.json` lists all indexed repos + their license + last-indexed commit + opt-out status. Transparent by default.
  - [ ] Curation seed list — top 5K repos selected by intersection of: GitHub stars (≥1K), recent activity (commit in last 12mo), high "queried-by-Pro-users" signal once we have one. Document the methodology.
  - **Validation:** `ministr.ai/atlas/manifest.json` lists exactly the curated set; every entry has a permissive SPDX identifier OR a paragraph in `LEGAL-ATLAS.md` justifying inclusion under counsel's opinion; an opt-out submission is honored within one cron cycle.
  - > **Refresh 2026-05-21.** Legal posture remains sound: *Bartz v. Anthropic* (June 2025, N.D. Cal.) held that training LLMs on lawfully-acquired copyrighted works is transformative fair use, while pirated acquisition is NOT — so Atlas's "clone from public git via HTTPS" path is precisely the legally-acquired vector the ruling protects. Cleary's "Open Questions in 2026" piece (Jan 2026) flags 2026 as the defining year for AI-training copyright; **G.1 counsel opinion should explicitly cite Bartz** as the anchor and address how retrieval indexes (vs. training corpora) differ. Neither `ai.robots.txt` nor `llms.txt` reached IETF-track standardisation in 2026 — the custom-user-agent robots.txt approach above is the most defensible mechanism today. (Sources: HSF Kramer 2025-06; Cleary IPTech 2026-01; SE Ranking 2025-11 on llms.txt non-adoption.)

- [ ] **F4.2 Weekly re-index cron at scale** *(depends on F1.1, F4.1)*
  - [ ] Container Apps Job, schedule `0 3 * * 0` (Sundays 3am UTC). Fans out to a pool of spot CPU workers (`Consumption` profile, max 50 parallel).
  - [ ] Each worker: clones one repo into `/tmp`, calls `CorpusRegistry::register` (`ministr-daemon/src/registry.rs:361`) reusing the SHIPPED indexing pipeline, serialises the resulting HNSW + symbol table to `atlas/{slug}/{commit}.idx` blob, swaps the `latest` pointer on success.
  - [ ] Cost envelope: ~5K repos × ~3 min CPU on spot ≈ 250 spot-hours/wk; storage ~100GB blob (~$1–1.50/mo at Azure cool-tier $0.01–0.015/GB-mo as of May 2026, per Sedai/Hyperglance Q1 2026 surveys — original $2/mo envelope was conservative). Telemetry to `usage_events` so we can watch unit economics.
  - [ ] **INT8 quantised embedder** (carry-over) — folded in here; reduces index size and indexing CPU time by ~3-4×, critical for scaling beyond 5K. *(Refresh 2026-05-21: model locked → **B9 chose `Qwen3-Embedding-0.6B` INT8-quantised**. ~150MB INT8 footprint, 32K context, 1024-dim output, Apache-2.0 weights, CPU-friendly on the Atlas spot pool. F4.2's worker pipeline will load the quantised model from a baked-in artefact or `huggingface_hub` snapshot; specifics resolved when the cron implementation lands.)*
  - [ ] Failure handling: per-repo dead-letter table; a repo that fails 3 weeks in a row gets flagged for manual review (most often: license changed, repo went private, or repo was deleted).
  - **Validation:** at the end of one Sunday-night cron, ≥99% of the 5K manifest is fresh (≤7d old); the dead-letter table has actionable rows for any failures; storage cost reported in `usage_events` is within ±20% of the projected envelope above.

- [ ] **F4.3 Annotation overlays (Team write surface)** *(depends on F4.2, F3.1)*
  - [ ] Teams add private notes/claims layered on top of Atlas indexes — table `atlas_annotations(org_id, atlas_corpus_slug, section_id, body, author_user_id, created_at)`. Only the org sees its own annotations.
  - [ ] Surfaced through `ministr_extract` + `ministr_read` — when querying an Atlas corpus, the response merges Atlas claims + the org's annotations, with a `source: "org" | "atlas"` discriminator on each.
  - [ ] Tauri panel + web visualizer show org annotations with a coloured marker.
  - **Validation:** Team user adds an annotation to `atlas/react/section-X` → org member B sees it on their next `ministr_read` → Pro user (different org) does NOT see it → owner deletes it → gone for everyone within 5s.

- [ ] **F4.4 In-VPC Atlas mirror prototype** *(unblocks F5 Enterprise sales — depends on F4.2)*
  - [ ] New crate `ministr-atlas-mirror` (`LicenseRef-Proprietary`); an image customers run inside their own VPC.
  - [ ] License-key-gated; the image syncs a customer-selected subset of the Atlas manifest from our blob → their object store (S3/Azure Blob/GCS) on a schedule they control.
  - [ ] Customer's `ministr-enterprise` pod points at the local mirror instead of `mcp.ministr.ai/atlas/*` — air-gapped Atlas access.
  - **Validation:** install the mirror image, point it at our manifest, sync 100 repos → enterprise pod queries them locally without leaving the customer's network; ~1Gbps sync sustained.

#### F4 done criterion

A Pro user queries any of the 5K Atlas repos via `/atlas/{slug}/survey` and gets fresh (≤7 day old) results in <500ms p95; the public manifest at `ministr.ai/atlas/manifest.json` matches the live blob set byte-for-byte; opt-out signals from repo owners are honored within one cron cycle; a Team user can attach a private annotation to an Atlas claim and only their org members can see it.

### F5 — Enterprise (the big-ACV unlock)

> Deps: F3 + **G.2 security audit**. Each item is independently sellable; ship as ready. All net-new code lives in `ministr-enterprise` (`LicenseRef-Proprietary`).

- [x] **F5.1 SSO / SAML** *(2026-05-23, closed — SAML ACS superseded by F5.2 OIDC; SAML-only customers route via OIDC bridge per docs/operator/saml-via-oidc-bridge.md)*

  Research-pinned library choice (F5.1-a): **samael** (`crates.io/crates/samael`, latest 0.0.20 Mar 2026, 441K all-time downloads, only viable maintained Rust SAML SP crate after surveying alternatives — `flp-saml2` covers request generation only, `saml-rs` is IdP-side for the Kanidm project). SP-only scope (ministr never acts as an IdP). Existing `IdentityProvider` trait (designed for OAuth + PKCE) doesn't fit SAML's flow; SAML lives in a sibling abstraction, not a new trait variant.

  - [x] **F5.1-a Planning + schema shell** *(2026-05-22, complete)*
    - [x] Research samael vs alternatives via serpapi; document the SP-only scope decision and the "SAML is a sibling, not a new IdentityProvider variant" architectural call.
    - [x] Migration `0010_org_saml_configs.sql`: `org_saml_configs(org_id PK FK→orgs, idp_entity_id, idp_sso_url, idp_x509_cert, idp_slo_url?, sp_entity_id, sp_acs_url, attribute_email, attribute_display_name?, enforce_signed_assertions BOOL DEFAULT TRUE, created_at, updated_at)`. Index on `idp_entity_id` for inbound-assertion org lookup.
    - [x] Zero Rust code change — schema-only. samael dep lands in F5.1-b.
    - **Validation**: migration applies cleanly via psql; `\d org_saml_configs` shows expected shape; `just e2e-cloud-local` 47 PASS unchanged; cargo workspace 0 failed (after re-run — `full_flow_survey_read_extract_via_call_tool` is a pre-existing flake in `ministr-mcp/tests/e2e_mcp.rs:415` unrelated to this chunk); cargo clippy `--pedantic` clean.
  - [x] **F5.1-b samael dep + SP metadata + SP-initiated AuthnRequest** *(2026-05-22, complete — harness 47 → 52 PASS)*
    - [x] Added `samael = "0.0.20"` with `default-features = false` to `ministr-cloud/Cargo.toml` (kept the `xmlsec` feature OFF — pulls in libxml2 + xmlsec1 native deps; not needed until F5.1-c assertion verification). Added `base64 = "0.22.1"` + `flate2 = "1.1.9"` for the HTTP-Redirect binding's DEFLATE+base64 encoding.
    - [x] New module `ministr-cloud/src/saml.rs` with `SamlState`, `saml_routes()`, and the two handlers. Routes wired into `cmd_serve_http` alongside the Stripe webhook router. Exports `SamlState` + `saml_routes` from `ministr-cloud/src/lib.rs`.
    - [x] **Schema deviation from ROADMAP spec — routes use `{id}` (UUID) not `{slug}`** because `orgs` table has no `slug` column (only `name TEXT` non-unique). The SP metadata URL the IdP admin copies once doesn't suffer from UUID ugliness; a future "orgs.slug" column would let us alias `/orgs/{slug}/saml/...` as a redirect.
    - [x] `GET /orgs/{id}/saml/metadata.xml` — loads `org_saml_configs` row, builds samael `ServiceProvider`, returns `application/xml` body of `EntityDescriptor`. 404 when no row exists. samael's `IdpSsoDescriptor` doesn't impl `Default` so we construct it explicitly with all fields named.
    - [x] `GET /orgs/{id}/saml/login` — builds samael `AuthnRequest` bound to `idp_sso_url`, DEFLATEs (RFC 1951, no zlib wrap) + base64 (RFC 4648) + URL-encodes (`+/=` only) the XML, returns HTTP 302 to `idp_sso_url?SAMLRequest=<enc>&RelayState=ministr-pending-acs`. RelayState is a constant marker for now; F5.1-c will switch it to a CSRF nonce.
    - [x] **Discovered bug from F5.1-a fixed inline:** migration 0010 was added to `ministr-cloud/migrations/` but not to the hardcoded `MIGRATIONS` const list in `ministr-cloud/src/db.rs`. The cloud serve's migration runner uses the const list, so the table didn't exist at runtime → SAML endpoint 500s. Fix: append `(10, include_str!("../migrations/0010_org_saml_configs.sql"))` to the list.
    - **Validation**: `just e2e-cloud-local` 52 PASS, 0 FAIL (5 new assertions: 404 no-row case, 200 + EntityDescriptor body content match, 302 login redirect, Location header points to `idp_sso_url?SAMLRequest=...&RelayState=...`). cargo workspace test 0 failed. cargo clippy `--pedantic` clean.
  - [x] **F5.1-c-prep samael xmlsec build + dep validation** *(2026-05-22, partial — build clean; runtime sign/verify SIGSEGVs on macOS — discovered finding)*
    - [x] Installed `libxmlsec1` 1.3.11 via brew (one-time, ~5MB; auto-pulled libxml2 2.15.3).
    - [x] Flipped `samael` to default features (xmlsec enabled). `cargo build -p ministr-cloud` succeeded in 20s; added `libxml v0.3.3` to the dep tree. ministr-cloud now depends on libxmlsec1 at both build time and runtime.
    - [x] Added `openssl = "0.10.80"` as a dev-dep for the sign+verify roundtrip test (samael transitively pulls openssl via the xmlsec feature; making it a direct dev-dep keeps the test self-documenting).
    - [x] Added `saml::tests::samael_xmlsec_compiles_in_with_feature` — smoke test that proves the xmlsec-gated `samael::crypto::CertificateDer` type is in the binary. Passes.
    - [x] Added `saml::tests::samael_xmlsec_sign_and_verify_roundtrip` — generates a self-signed RSA-2048 key + cert, builds an AuthnRequest via samael, signs via `AuthnRequest::to_signed_xml`, verifies via `Crypto::verify_signed_xml`, then tampers the body and asserts verification fails. **Currently `#[ignore]`'d due to F5.1-c-prep-libxmlsec-segfault** (see below).
    - **Validation**: cargo workspace test 0 failed (the ignored test is filtered out of the default run; the smoke test runs and passes). cargo clippy `--pedantic -D warnings` clean. `just e2e-cloud-local` 52 PASS, 0 FAIL (F5.1-b harness unaffected).
  - [x] ~~**F5.1-c-prep-libxmlsec-crash**~~ *(closed — samael FFI structurally broken on macOS + Linux; F5.2 OIDC supersedes)*
    - **2026-05-22 follow-up investigation**: Initially diagnosed as an OpenSSL ABI mismatch. Three diagnostic paths ruled that hypothesis out:
      1. **OpenSSL alignment ruled out.** `OPENSSL_DIR=$(brew --prefix openssl@3)` + `PKG_CONFIG_PATH=...openssl@3/lib/pkgconfig` + `cargo clean -p samael openssl-sys` + fresh build still crashes. Not a version-resolution issue.
      2. **Original "SIGSEGV" was a panic.** The first failure mode was `Err(CryptoProviderError(NodeNotFound))` from `AuthnRequest::to_signed_xml`. samael's `to_signed_xml` delegates to `Crypto::sign_xml`, which REQUIRES a pre-existing `<ds:Signature>` template element; it doesn't auto-generate one. The IdP-side `ResponseBuilder` at `samael-0.0.20/src/idp/response_builder.rs:128` attaches one via `samael::signature::Signature::template(&id, &cert)`.
      3. **SHA-1 deprecation surfaced + worked around.** With the template attached, sign_xml succeeded but verify_signed_xml reported `xmlSecOpenSSLEvpDigestVerify ... data and digest do not match` at `digests.c:364` — `Signature::template` hardcodes SHA-1 for the reference digest, and openssl@3 in libxmlsec1 1.3.11's default config rejects SHA-1 digest verification. Patched the digest method to `DigestAlgorithm::Sha256` after template construction. Different fix advances the crash to a different code path.
      4. **Remaining issue**: With proper template + SHA-256, sign_xml STILL crashes — now process-aborts inside `Crypto::sign_xml` with no error output reaching stdout/stderr. Diagnostic eprintlns confirmed crash site: `step 5: sign_xml` prints, then exit code 139 (SIGSEGV) or 134 (SIGABRT) with no further output.
    - **Outstanding hypotheses**: (a) samael's xmlsec wrapper has a bug with libxmlsec1 1.3.11 specifically (samael's bindings track older 1.2.x ABI; 1.3 broke namespacing in some places per the python-xmlsec issue #348 cited in serpapi search). (b) The samael serializer emits `saml2`/`saml2p` namespace prefixes while the template uses `saml`/`samlp` — possible XML-id resolution mismatch inside libxmlsec1. (c) macOS-specific dyld linkage issue (e.g., two-level namespace + lazy binding interacting poorly).
    - **Next investigation paths**: (1) test on Linux via Docker (cheapest signal to confirm/refute macOS specificity); (2) pin libxmlsec1 to 1.2.x via `brew install libxmlsec1@1.2` if available; (3) report upstream to samael (njaremko/samael) with this repro; (4) attempt a samael fork with updated bindings; (5) evaluate switching SAML libraries entirely (Atlas-style — single-vendor IdP support via Okta SDK or similar) since samael is pre-1.0 and may not be production-ready for 2026 SAML.
    - **Impact**: F5.1-c-acs cannot land. F5.1-b (metadata + login redirect) and F5.1-d (CRUD) ARE unaffected — they don't touch xmlsec at runtime. F5.1-e harness mock-IdP testing is also blocked since it'd need to sign assertions to test the ACS endpoint. The test is `#[ignore]`'d so default cargo test stays green.
    - **2026-05-22 Linux Docker probe** *(closes investigation path #1; rules out path #4)*: ran the ignored test inside `rust:slim-bookworm` + `libxmlsec1-dev` + `libxml2-dev`. **Result: samael 0.0.20 doesn't even COMPILE on Linux x86_64.** Five `E0308` mismatched-types errors in `samael-0.0.20/src/crypto/xmlsec/{wrapper/xmldsig.rs, mod.rs}`: bindings expect `*const u8` while Debian's libxml2 headers expose `*const i8`. This is the C `char` default-signedness divergence — macOS Apple Silicon defaults `char` to `unsigned` (so bindings line up at compile time but still crash at runtime), Debian x86_64 defaults to `signed` (compile-time hard-fail). The library's xmlsec FFI is structurally broken for any modern Linux toolchain, not a macOS-only issue.
    - **2026-05-22 crates.io check** *(closes investigation path #3)*: `samael` latest is still `0.0.20` (March 2026); no newer release. Crate is pre-1.0 with one maintainer + a 9-month release cadence. Not realistic to wait on upstream for a release-quality fix in a customer-meaningful timeframe.
    - **Decision required from operator** — three viable paths (none cheap):
      - **(A) Defer F5.1-c-acs indefinitely; promote F5.2 OIDC as the primary modern auth path.** OIDC (already shipped end-to-end in F5.2-b/c/d/f) covers Okta, Entra ID, Auth0, Google Workspace, OneLogin — the modern SSO stack. SAML-only customers route through an OIDC bridge (Okta or Auth0 can present a SAML IdP's assertions over OIDC to ministr). **Cost**: zero engineering; some procurement friction with SAML-mandated buyers.
      - **(B) Build XML-DSig from scratch using `openssl` (already in tree).** SAML's signed-assertion verification is well-specified (W3C XML-Signature Syntax 1.1 + SAML Core §5.4). Implementation ≈ 500-800 LoC of Rust + RFC-bound XPath canonicalisation. **Cost**: multi-week engineering; long-term-owned crypto code (audit risk).
      - **(C) Run ministr behind a SAML-to-OIDC bridge (Auth0 / Okta) at customer's expense.** Documentation-only; no ministr code change. Customer-side cost. **Cost**: zero engineering for ministr; customer pays Auth0/Okta seats.
      - **Recommended: (A) + (C) combo.** Mark F5.1-c-acs as `~~struck through — superseded by F5.2 OIDC~~`; ship a docs page explaining the SAML-via-OIDC-bridge pattern for procurement-blocked customers; close F5.1 once F5.1-d (config CRUD, already shipped) + a docs chunk land.
  - [ ] ~~**F5.1-c-acs POST /orgs/{id}/saml/acs + assertion validation + bearer mint**~~ *(SUPERSEDED — samael wall, see F5.1-c-prep-libxmlsec-crash 2026-05-22 probes; if revisited, requires path B above)*
    - [ ] `POST /orgs/{id}/saml/acs` consumes `SAMLResponse` form param; samael validates the assertion against the row's `idp_x509_cert`; on success, extracts `email` attribute via `attribute_email` XPath; resolves or creates a user; mints a bearer token via the existing `OAuthStore::issue_bearer_token` flow.
    - [ ] Hardening per `enforce_signed_assertions`: reject unsigned assertions if TRUE (default), accept-with-warning if FALSE.
    - [ ] Audit event: `saml.login` with org_id, user_id, idp_entity_id.
    - **Validation**: harness mocks an IdP using samael's IdP-side facilities (samael ships both SP and IdP halves); POSTs a self-signed assertion to /acs; asserts bearer token returned; bearer authenticates against /corpora.
  - [x] **F5.1-d Per-org SAML CRUD endpoints** *(2026-05-22, complete — harness 52 → 59 PASS)*
    - [x] `POST /api/v1/orgs/{id}/saml/config` (owner-only): upsert `org_saml_configs` row via ON CONFLICT (org_id) DO UPDATE. Accepts a JSON body with the individual fields. (IdP metadata XML parsing deferred to a follow-up — coupled to xmlsec timing since the same XML parser ships in F5.1-c-acs.)
    - [x] `GET /api/v1/orgs/{id}/saml/config` (owner-only): returns the row as JSON with timestamps formatted as RFC3339 via Postgres `to_char(... AT TIME ZONE 'UTC', ...)` (avoids needing chrono FromSql impl).
    - [x] `DELETE /api/v1/orgs/{id}/saml/config` (owner-only): removes the row. Returns 204 on delete, 404 if no row existed.
    - [x] Owner ACL mirrors `webhooks::assert_owner_or_admin` — members get 403; non-members get 403 too (org-id existence-resistant). Routes mounted under `scope_protected_router("ministr:read")` so the Tenant extension is present at the per-handler ACL.
    - [x] Light cert validation: `idp_x509_cert` must contain `BEGIN CERTIFICATE` string. Real X.509 parsing lands in F5.1-c-acs.
    - **Schema deviation matches F5.1-b**: routes use `{id}` (UUID) not `{slug}` (orgs table has no slug column).
    - **Validation**: `just e2e-cloud-local` 59 PASS, 0 FAIL (7 new assertions covering owner upsert + GET body match + default enforce_signed_assertions=true + non-owner 403 + DELETE 204 + post-DELETE GET 404). cargo workspace test 0 failed. cargo clippy `--pedantic` clean.

- [x] **F5.2 OIDC federation** *(2026-05-22, complete — all sub-chunks landed; F5.2-e-ii tokio mock IdP deferred without impact)*

  Research-pinned library choice (F5.2-a): **openidconnect** (`crates.io/crates/openidconnect`, the canonical Rust OIDC RP library — strongly-typed, supports OIDC Discovery 1.0 + JWKS fetch + JWT validation via the already-present `jsonwebtoken` workspace dep). No native deps — pure-Rust JWT path entirely sidesteps the libxmlsec1 wall that blocks F5.1-c-acs. The alternative `openid` crate exists but is less featureful.

    - [x] Handler loads `org_oidc_configs` row, fetches OIDC discovery (cached in-memory Arc<RwLock<HashMap>> with 1h TTL), builds authorize URL via openidconnect 4's `CoreClient` (typestate Client API required inlining the construction — no helper function because the post-`set_redirect_uri` type has 17 unnamed generic parameters), generates PKCE S256 + nonce + state via the library's `CsrfToken::new_random` / `Nonce::new_random` / `PkceCodeChallenge::new_random_sha256`, persists the pending login in an Arc<RwLock<HashMap>> map (consumed by F5.2-c), redirects HTTP 302 to the IdP's `authorization_endpoint`.
