  - [x] **F5.2-b-harness-flake** *(2026-05-22, resolved — never reproduced after fresh run + harness instrumentation; real bug was an OIDC issuer mismatch in the mock IdP, surfaced once the harness ran end-to-end)*
    - **What actually broke**: not the migrations. F5.2-b's 3 harness assertions failed because the mock IdP at `scripts/e2e-oidc-mock-idp.py` served its discovery doc with `issuer: http://localhost:8090` while the harness configured `org_oidc_configs.issuer_url = http://127.0.0.1:8090`. openidconnect-rs's `CoreClient::from_provider_metadata` enforces OIDC Discovery 1.0 §4.3 (`issuer` must match the URL prefix used to discover it byte-for-byte), so the handler returned `discover_async: Validation error: unexpected issuer URI 'http://localhost:8090' (expected 'http://127.0.0.1:8090')` → 500 `not_found`. Fix: change the mock IdP's `base` to `http://127.0.0.1:{port}` so the discovery `issuer` matches the harness's `issuer_url`.
    - **About the "no migrations / no log lines" original diagnostic**: not reproducible from clean. The KEEP=1 inspection at this session showed migrations DID run (`\dt` lists 22 tables including `users` / `schema_migrations`) — the original "schema_migrations doesn't exist" report was likely a transient cargo-lock or rebuild artefact from F5.2-b code landing while the harness was running. The "no log lines for migrations" half is explainable: `tracing::info!` in `ministr-cli/src/commands.rs` emits with target `ministr::commands` (the binary name from `[[bin]] name = "ministr"`), and the default filter `ministr_core=info,ministr_mcp=info,ministr_daemon=info,ministr_cli=info,warn` doesn't include `ministr=info`, so info-level logs from the binary crate fall through to `warn` and are silenced. That's logging hygiene, not a correctness bug.
    - **Harness hardening shipped**: `mint_token` now captures stderr to a temp file and surfaces it on non-zero exit instead of silencing with `2>/dev/null`. A future regression of the original "zero log lines on failure" shape will carry its own diagnostic.
    - **Files touched**: `scripts/e2e-oidc-mock-idp.py` (issuer fix), `scripts/e2e-cloud-local.sh` (mint_token stderr capture).
  - [x] **F5.2-c GET /orgs/{id}/oidc/callback + token exchange + ID-token validation + bearer mint** *(2026-05-22, complete — harness 62 → 67 PASS)*
    - [x] `ministr-cloud/src/users.rs` — new `upsert_oidc_user(pool, email) -> UserRow` keyed on the `email` UNIQUE INDEX. `ON CONFLICT (email) DO UPDATE` with `plan_id = users.plan_id` + `github_id = users.github_id` self-assignments preserves billing's authoritative column AND any pre-existing GitHub-side identity. **v0 limitation documented inline**: the users table has no `(issuer, subject)` column, so two IdPs claiming the same email federate into one ministr user. Acceptable for v0 because enterprise customers run ONE IdP per org and the per-org `org_oidc_configs` row is the trust boundary, not the user row.
    - [x] `ministr-cloud/src/oidc.rs::handle_callback` — full SP callback flow. Consumes `?code=&state=` from the IdP redirect, pops the `PendingLogin` by state up-front (single-use; replay-resistant), reconstructs the `CoreClient` from cached discovery + per-org config, exchanges code via `client.exchange_code(...).set_pkce_verifier(...).request_async(&http_client)`, extracts the `id_token`, validates claims via `id_token.claims(&client.id_token_verifier(), &nonce)` (signature against JWKS + `iss` + `aud` + `nonce`), enforces `email_verified` when `enforce_email_verified` is set, upserts the user, mints bearer via the same `OAuthStore` the GitHub callback uses (`DEFAULT_OIDC_SIGNIN_SCOPE = "ministr:read ministr:write"`), emits `oidc.login` audit event, returns 200 + `{token, user_id, plan_id}` JSON.
    - [x] `OidcState` gained `with_oauth_store` + `with_cloud_base_url` + `with_audit` builders. `cmd_serve_http` wires all three; the cloud base URL is read from `MINISTR_CLOUD_BASE_URL` so the `redirect_uri` the IdP sees matches what's registered for the Relying Party.
    - [x] `scripts/e2e-oidc-mock-idp.py` rewritten end-to-end: added `GET /authorize` (auto-approve — immediately 302s to `redirect_uri?code=<code>&state=<state>` and stores `code -> {nonce}` in-process so /token can echo the right nonce into the JWT), `POST /token` (form-encoded code exchange returning RS256-signed ID token), and a `GET /jwks.json` body that includes the public key's `n`/`e` instead of an empty stub. RSA signing shells out to `openssl dgst -sha256 -sign` against a keypair the harness generates via `openssl genrsa` (no Python cryptography dep needed).
    - [x] `scripts/e2e-cloud-local.sh` — generates the keypair, extracts the modulus as base64url-encoded JWK `n` (via a one-liner Python helper that strips the leading 0x00 byte openssl sometimes emits for top-bit-set moduli), exports `OIDC_*` env vars to the mock IdP, and runs 5 new assertions: (1) /authorize redirect to cloud callback with `code` + `state`, (2) callback 200, (3) JSON body carries non-empty token + user_id, (4) the OIDC-minted bearer authenticates against `/api/v1/corpora`, (5) `audit_events` table contains an `oidc.login` row.
    - **Honest finding — macOS BSD awk doesn't honour `BEGIN{IGNORECASE=1}`**. The cloud's existing F5.1-b/F5.2-b Location-header extractor happens to work because axum emits lowercase headers, but Python's `BaseHTTPRequestHandler` emits `Location:` with capital L — F5.2-c's awk pattern rewritten to `tolower($1)=="location:"` so it's portable. Pre-existing patterns left alone (they work by accident; documented inline).
    - **Honest scope choice — response is JSON, not a redirect**. F5.2-c v0 returns `{token, user_id, plan_id}` directly so the harness can assert end-to-end without a loopback receiver. A future iteration can mirror the GitHub flow's 302 to a `MINISTR_CLOUD_BASE_URL/auth/done?token=…` page when the desktop integration arrives.
    - **Validation**: cargo workspace test 0 failed; cargo clippy `--pedantic -D warnings` clean; `just e2e-cloud-local` 67 PASS 0 FAIL. Live cross-env validation pending the next deploy with a real IdP (Keycloak / Auth0).
  - [x] **F5.2-d Per-org OIDC CRUD endpoints** *(2026-05-22, complete — harness 67 → 76 PASS)*
    - [x] `ministr-cloud/src/oidc.rs` gained 11 new symbols: `REDACTED_CLIENT_SECRET = "[REDACTED]"` sentinel, `oidc_config_routes(state) -> Router` (POST/GET/DELETE on `/api/v1/orgs/{id}/oidc/config`), `OidcConfigError` (with `IntoResponse` mapping to 401/403/404/400/500), `OidcConfigUpsertBody`, `OidcConfigView`, `assert_oidc_owner_or_admin`, `validate_oidc_upsert`, and the three handlers (`handle_oidc_config_upsert` / `_get` / `_delete`). Exact mirror of F5.1-d's SAML CRUD shape; the only differences are the column set + the redaction sentinel.
    - [x] `POST` upserts `org_oidc_configs` via `ON CONFLICT (org_id) DO UPDATE`. Validates non-empty `issuer_url` / `client_id` / `client_secret` and rejects an `issuer_url` missing `http(s)://`. Default claim mappings (`groups` / `email` / `name`) apply when absent. **client_secret never appears in the RETURNING clause** — the handler hardcodes `REDACTED_CLIENT_SECRET` in the response view so even an inadvertent log of `row` can't leak it.
    - [x] `GET` reads the row, also hardcodes `REDACTED_CLIENT_SECRET` in the response.
    - [x] `DELETE` removes the row, returns 204; absent row returns 404 (same shape as F5.1-d).
    - [x] Owner-only ACL: each handler calls `assert_oidc_owner_or_admin` which delegates to `crate::orgs::repo::member_role`. **Duplicated rather than shared with F5.1-d's `assert_owner_or_admin`** because sharing would require lifting the error enum to a parent type — the body is two lines, the duplication saves more than it costs. A future cleanup chunk can extract `orgs::repo::assert_owner_or_admin` returning a generic `OrgRoleError`.
    - [x] Wired in `cmd_serve_http` behind `scope_protected_router("ministr:read")` right after the F5.1-d SAML config block. Self-hosted serve has no `cloud_pool` so this block doesn't run.

The DB-ground-truth check is the load-bearing security assertion — proves the redaction is HTTP-only, not a DB-side scrubbing bug.
    - **Honest scope choice — `group_role_map JSONB` column NOT added in this chunk**. Per the ROADMAP spec ("defer until F5.2-d actually needs it") + the principle that the CRUD itself doesn't consume it. F5.2-c's callback already reads `enforce_email_verified` / `groups_claim` / `email_claim` / `name_claim` from the existing schema; F5.2-d exposes all of those for configuration. Group → role mapping lands the chunk that actually consumes the JSONB (likely after F5.2-c grows beyond email-only sign-in into role-driven access).

  - [x] **F5.2-f group_role_map JSONB → org_members inference** *(2026-05-22, complete — harness 76 → 85 PASS)*
    - [x] Migration `0012_org_oidc_group_role_map.sql` adds `group_role_map JSONB NOT NULL DEFAULT '{}'::jsonb` to `org_oidc_configs`. Wired into `ministr-cloud/src/db.rs` MIGRATIONS const at index 12. Default `{}` means existing rows keep the F5.2-c shape (no role inference, no `org_members` writes).
    - [x] CRUD shape extended (F5.2-d's POST/GET): `OidcConfigUpsertBody` + `OidcConfigView` carry `group_role_map: serde_json::Value`. POST validates the value is a JSON object whose values are `"owner"`, `"admin"`, or `"member"` — non-object → 400, invalid role → 400. SQL includes the column in INSERT / ON CONFLICT / RETURNING + SELECT paths.
    - [x] Callback consumption: `apply_group_role_map(pool, org_id, user_id, &cfg, jwt)` orchestrates the inference. Re-parses the validated JWT payload via `base64::URL_SAFE_NO_PAD` + `serde_json::from_slice` to access the configured `groups_claim` — the openidconnect-rs surface only exposes the standard claim accessors without a custom `AdditionalClaims` type parameter, and the type cascade through every Client/Verifier instantiation would have been invasive. Safe because the library has already verified the JWT's signature + iss + aud + nonce up-thread; re-parsing the same bytes can't introduce tampering. The helper picks the **highest-power** role from matching groups (`owner > admin > member` via `role_rank`).
    - [x] **Bootstrap-safe owner protection**: `apply_group_role_map` reads the existing `org_members.role` first; if it's `"owner"` and the target role is anything else, it returns `Unchanged` without touching the row. Prevents an over-broad `{"all-employees": "member"}` mapping from accidentally locking the customer out of their own org. F5.2-f's harness assertion proves this end-to-end: directly promote the OIDC user to owner via psql, POST a downgrade-attempting mapping, run the callback, confirm the row is still `owner`.
    - [x] Audit emission: existing `oidc.login` PLUS new `member.added` (first insert) or `member.role_updated` (existing row mutated). Action-name-only differentiation — `AuditEntry`'s schema is intentionally metadata-free, the role is reconstructable from the next-step `org_members` read. Matches the F3.7b `member.added` shape so the audit feed stays uniform.
    - [x] Mock IdP `scripts/e2e-oidc-mock-idp.py` gained `OIDC_FIXED_GROUPS` env (comma-separated). When non-empty, the signed JWT carries a `groups` claim with the configured list. Empty / unset → no groups claim, preserves the F5.2-b/c/d assertion paths unchanged.
    - [x] Harness `scripts/e2e-cloud-local.sh` adds 9 F5.2-f assertions covering the full grant + callback flow (group_role_map saved + retrieved + applied), psql verification of `org_members.role`, audit row check, bootstrap-safe downgrade-prevention, and two input-validation negative cases.
    - [x] Pure unit tests in `oidc.rs::group_role_tests` cover `extract_groups_from_jwt` (malformed JWT, string-array, custom claim name), `pick_role_from_groups` (highest-power wins, empty/non-object map), `role_rank` (owner > admin > member > garbage). 212 ministr-cloud tests pass.
    - [x] `docs/operator/oidc-real-idp.md` updated: `group_role_map` is now documented in the field table + the claims-read-at-callback note. The earlier "reserved for future" placeholder removed.
    - **Honest scope choice — action-name-only audit**. `AuditEntry`'s schema has no free-text `message` field; my first draft fabricated `with_message` calls that don't exist. Reverted to action-name differentiation (`member.added` vs `member.role_updated`) which matches the existing F3.7b emission shape.
    - **Honest scope choice — re-parse the JWT instead of custom AdditionalClaims**. The openidconnect-rs idiomatic path requires parameterizing `CoreClient` + `IdToken` + the verifier with a custom `AdditionalClaims` struct. That's a wide type cascade through every instantiation. Re-parsing the post-validated payload sidesteps it; documented inline with the safety argument (validation already happened).
    - **Validation**: cargo workspace test 0 failed; cargo clippy `--pedantic -D warnings` clean; `just e2e-cloud-local` 76 → 85 PASS, 0 FAIL.

  - [x] **F5.3-a Tier-aware audit retention** *(2026-05-22, complete — harness 85 → 90 PASS)*
    - [x] `ministr-cloud/src/audit.rs::prune_audit_events` WHERE clause gained a tier-skip predicate: `(org_id IS NULL OR NOT EXISTS (SELECT 1 FROM orgs o WHERE o.id = ae.org_id AND o.plan_id = $2))` with `$2` bound to a new `ENTERPRISE_PLAN_ID` const. Rows whose `org_id` resolves to an Enterprise org survive forever; non-Enterprise + NULL-org rows continue to prune at 90d.
    - [x] **Policy choice — NULL-org rows DO prune**. The Enterprise "infinite retention" promise covers actions tied to an Enterprise org via `org_id`; user-level audit events on personal accounts (sign-up flows, personal API-key actions) fall outside the promise. Documented inline in the `prune_audit_events` doc comment so future maintainers don't widen the rule by accident.
    - [x] New `ENTERPRISE_PLAN_ID = "enterprise"` const locked to the lowercase form `ministr_mcp::auth::store::parse_plan_id` normalizes to. Unit test (`enterprise_plan_id_matches_parse_plan_id_lowercase`) regression-guards the case so a future refactor can't silently break the SQL match.

    - **Honest scope choice — synthetic fake-org_id for the non-Enterprise case**. First version inserted a real second org but hit `set -e` fragility around docker/psql exit codes; switched to a synthetic UUID that doesn't exist in `orgs`. The SQL's `NOT EXISTS` treats missing-org as "not Enterprise" — same observable outcome with less seed surface area.

  - [x] **F5.3-b Runtime-role REVOKE for immutability** *(SQL landed; Pulumi deploy deferred)* — migration + harness simulation complete.
    - [x] **F5.3-b-sql Migration + constrained role + harness simulation** *(2026-05-22, complete — harness 153 → 159 PASS)*
      - [x] Migration `0015_audit_events_revoke_runtime_role.sql` creates `ministr_audit_runtime` NOLOGIN role, REVOKEs ALL on `audit_events`, GRANTs only INSERT + SELECT. Sequence `audit_events_id_seq` gets USAGE (without it, INSERT would fail with "permission denied for sequence" — a confusing failure mode the cloud would hit on first audit emission).
      - [x] **Per-partition grants required** — pre-flight empirical test confirmed PG does NOT cascade parent grants to existing child partitions (`has_table_privilege('role', 'audit_events_y2026q2', 'INSERT')` returned `false` after `GRANT INSERT ON audit_events`). Migration walks `pg_inherits` via a DO block + `format()` + `EXECUTE` to apply per-partition grants.
      - [x] **`USAGE ON SCHEMA public` grant** — PG 15+ removed the implicit USAGE-to-PUBLIC grant on the public schema. Without an explicit grant the SET ROLE'd session sees "relation audit_events does not exist" rather than "permission denied" (PG hides every table the role can't see).
      - [x] Harness adds 6 assertions: role exists, DELETE under SET LOCAL ROLE → "permission denied for table audit_events", UPDATE under SET LOCAL ROLE → "permission denied", SELECT under SET LOCAL ROLE → succeeds with row count, child partition `audit_events_y2026q2` has DELETE revoked, child partition has INSERT granted.
      - **Honest finding — `set -euo pipefail` killed the script on first run**. psql exits non-zero on any per-statement error even with `ON_ERROR_STOP=0` (that flag controls processing continuation, not exit status). Fixed by trailing each `$(docker compose exec psql)` capture with `|| true` and inspecting the captured stderr.
      - **Honest finding — F5.3-c-ii-boot's `ensure_audit_partitions` doesn't apply the new role's grants** to partitions it creates at runtime. Production future partitions would have INSERT denied for the runtime role. Tracked as a follow-up in F5.3-b-deploy scope.
      - **Honest scope choice — production cutover deferred**. Today the dev cloud connects as the superuser `ministr` user; REVOKE doesn't apply to superusers, so the immutability check is via SET LOCAL ROLE simulation in the harness. F5.3-b-deploy lands the Pulumi work (CREATE LOGIN role with managed password, rotate cloud connection string).
      - **Validation**: cargo workspace test 0 failed (247 ministr-cloud tests, unchanged); cargo clippy `--pedantic -D warnings` clean; `just e2e-cloud-local` 153 → 159 PASS, 0 FAIL.

      - [ ] Pulumi `azure-native:dbforpostgresql:Configuration` or equivalent: provision `ministr_audit_runtime` with LOGIN + Pulumi-managed password.
      - [ ] Update cloud `MINISTR_PG_URL` to connect as `ministr_audit_runtime`. Pruner CLI uses a separate `MINISTR_PG_PRUNER_URL` env var pointing at the superuser/admin role.
      - [ ] Extend `ensure_audit_partitions` to GRANT INSERT, SELECT on each newly-created partition so future partitions inherit the same RBAC posture.
  - [x] **F5.3-c Quarterly partitioning + cold-partition archive** *(complete except Pulumi blob backend)* — all code landed.
    - [x] **F5.3-c-i Partition `audit_events` by quarter** *(2026-05-22, complete — harness 90 → 92 PASS)*
      - [x] Migration `0013_audit_events_partitioned.sql` converts `audit_events` to `PARTITION BY RANGE (ts)` via create-new + copy + atomic-swap. Composite PK `(id, ts)` because PG partition keys must be part of the PK. Hardcoded 16 quarterly partitions covering 2024-Q1 through 2027-Q4 via a `DO` block + `generate_series('2024-01-01', '2027-10-01', '3 months')` loop emitting `CREATE TABLE … PARTITION OF audit_events_new FOR VALUES FROM (start) TO (start + 3 months)`. F5.3-c-ii will add the boot-time `ensure_audit_partitions(lookahead)` helper that extends the forward edge dynamically.
      - [x] **Sequence preservation across the swap**: `audit_events_id_seq` is detached from the old column via `ALTER SEQUENCE … OWNED BY NONE` BEFORE the `DROP TABLE audit_events`, so the sequence survives. Re-bound to the new column via `ALTER SEQUENCE … OWNED BY audit_events.id` in the final step. Existing rows are copied with explicit `id` values so the sequence's `last_value` doesn't drift; subsequent `nextval` calls produce ids past the previously-seen max.
      - [x] Indexes from migration 0001 (`idx_audit_events_org_ts` partial on `(org_id, ts DESC) WHERE org_id IS NOT NULL`; `idx_audit_events_ts` on `(ts DESC)`) are recreated on the new partitioned parent. PG 11+ propagates parent indexes to every current + future partition automatically.
      - [x] **Honest finding — index name collision**. First migration draft tried to create `idx_audit_events_org_ts` directly on `audit_events_new` while the old table still held that index name. PG index names are schema-scoped (not table-scoped), so the CREATE crashed with `relation "idx_audit_events_org_ts" already exists`. Fixed by creating the new indexes with `_new` suffix, then `ALTER INDEX … RENAME` back to the canonical names AFTER the old table drops. Documented inline in the migration so a future schema author doesn't repeat the gotcha.
      - [x] Harness adds 2 assertions: `count(pg_inherits WHERE inhparent = 'audit_events'::regclass) == 16` (locks in the partition count) + `pg_class.relkind == 'p'` (locks in that the parent is a partitioned table, not a regular one). All 90 prior assertions survive — F5.3-a's prune, F5.2-* CRUD, every audit-row INSERT path still works against the partitioned table.
      - **Honest scope choice — no boot-time helper this chunk**. The hardcoded 2024-2027 range is a 2.5-year runway from current time; F5.3-c-ii will add `ensure_audit_partitions(pool, lookahead_quarters)` so the forward edge auto-extends without manual migrations. Sized to fit one /roadmap pass.
      - **Validation**: cargo workspace test 0 failed (213 ministr-cloud tests, unchanged from F5.3-a); cargo clippy `--pedantic -D warnings` clean; `just e2e-cloud-local` 90 → 92 PASS, 0 FAIL.
    - [x] **F5.3-c-ii Cold-partition archive + boot-time partition extension** *(complete)* — boot + FS archive + read endpoint all landed.
      - [x] **F5.3-c-ii-boot Boot-time `ensure_audit_partitions`** *(2026-05-22, complete — harness 92 → 97 PASS)*
        - [x] New `ministr_cloud::ensure_audit_partitions(pool, lookahead_quarters) -> EnsurePartitionsOutcome` in `audit.rs`. Lists existing partitions via `pg_inherits` + `pg_class`, parses names via the pure `parse_audit_partition_name` helper, asks Postgres for the current (year, quarter) via `extract(year/quarter FROM now() AT TIME ZONE 'UTC')`, then walks the full `[current..target]` range inclusive with `CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS … PARTITION OF audit_events FOR VALUES FROM … TO …`. Returns `(existing, created, target_end_year, target_end_quarter)`.
        - [x] **Gap-fill semantics** (load-bearing): the helper walks the full target range and skips quarters already in a `HashSet<(year, quarter)>` of existing partitions. Earlier draft used `next_quarter(highest_existing)` as the walk start — that path CAN'T fill gaps when a future partition exists past a hole. Harness assertion proves the new shape end-to-end: `DROP TABLE audit_events_y2027q4` (creates a gap), run the helper, partition is restored.
        - [x] `cmd_serve_http` boot calls `ensure_audit_partitions(pool, DEFAULT_PARTITION_LOOKAHEAD_QUARTERS=8)` right after migrations apply. Failure logs `warn` but doesn't crash boot — the partition surface degrades gracefully (writes fail only past the highest seeded partition).
        - [x] New CLI subcommand `ministr audit ensure-partitions --lookahead-quarters N` mirrors `audit prune`'s shape. Useful for operator-driven catch-up + external cron jobs that don't want to restart serve to extend the forward edge.
        - [x] 5 new pure unit tests cover `parse_audit_partition_name` (valid + 8 rejection cases), `next_quarter` (Q4 → next year Q1), `quarter_start_literal` (matches migration 0013 bounds byte-for-byte), and `DEFAULT_PARTITION_LOOKAHEAD_QUARTERS == 8` regression guard.
        - [x] 5 harness assertions: relaxed F5.3-c-i's hardcoded `== 16` partition-count to `>= 16` (the boot helper extends dynamically), then DROP one future partition, run the CLI, verify count restored + 2027_q4 re-created, run again to verify idempotency.

          - [x] New `archive_audit_partition_to_dir(pool, partition_name, archive_dir) -> ArchiveOutcome { rows, bytes_on_disk, file_path }` in `audit.rs`. Verifies the partition exists in `pg_inherits` before opening a transaction. SELECT casts id/org_id/actor/ip to text + ua column + ts via `to_char(... AT TIME ZONE 'UTC', 'YYYY-MM-DD"T"HH24:MI:SS.US"Z"')`. Serializes each row as one JSON line, gzips via `flate2::write::GzEncoder` (explicit `finish()` flushes the trailer), writes to `<archive_dir>/<partition_name>.jsonl.gz`. `ALTER TABLE DETACH PARTITION` + `DROP TABLE` inside the same transaction.

          - [x] New `S3JsonlCredentials` struct (3 required: `access_key_id`, `secret_access_key`, `region`; 1 optional: `endpoint_url_override` for `MinIO` / Cloudflare R2 / Backblaze B2 / other S3-compatible providers). `#[serde(default)]` on the optional field; `#[allow(dead_code)]` on it with a comment pointing at F5.3-d-iii-b-dispatch as the future reader.

          - [x] `PerOrgSiemDispatcher`'s s3_jsonl arm logs a LOUD `warn` (`"s3_jsonl row found but dispatch not yet wired (F5.3-d-iii-b-dispatch will add the aws-sdk-s3 PUT path)"`) — distinct from the unknown-kind arm so ops can distinguish "kind we recognise but haven't wired" from "kind we don't know".
          - [x] 6 new pure unit tests: validator admits the happy path; rejects `http://` scheme; rejects non-JSON token; rejects token missing `access_key_id`; rejects empty `region`; `validate_s3_credentials_shape` admits the optional `endpoint_url_override`.
          - [x] 7 new harness assertions: POST happy-path s3_jsonl config → 200 + kind echoed + token redacted; reject https:// (cross-kind scheme mismatch); reject non-JSON token; reject token missing required field; reject empty `region`.
          - **Honest scope choice — no `aws-sdk-s3` dep yet**. Dispatch lands in F5.3-d-iii-b-dispatch. Customers configuring `s3_jsonl` rows today see audit events land in Postgres but NOT in S3 until the next chunk ships. The `warn` log surfaces the gap.
          - **Validation**: cargo workspace test 0 failed (246 ministr-cloud tests, +6 new); cargo clippy `--pedantic -D warnings` clean; `just e2e-cloud-local` 138 → 145 PASS, 0 FAIL.
        - [x] **F5.3-d-iii-b-dispatch aws-sdk-s3 PUT path** *(2026-05-22, complete — harness 145 → 153 PASS)*
          - [x] Added `aws-sdk-s3` + `aws-credential-types` + `aws-config` workspace deps (pinned to "1" major). Compile cost: ~30s on a clean build.
          - [x] New `civil_from_unix_secs(u64) -> (i32, u32, u32)` — Howard Hinnant's algorithm in pure integer arithmetic. Avoids a `chrono` / `time` dep. Localized clippy `#[allow]` for the mathematically-bounded casts; 7-known-date unit test (epoch, end-of-day, day boundary, 2024-01-01, leap-day 2024-02-29, this session 2026-05-22, centennial non-leap 2100-01-01).
          - [x] New `dispatch_s3_jsonl(endpoint, token_json, entry)` helper. Parses `s3://bucket/prefix` (with `split_once('/')`-style bucket/prefix split + trailing-slash trim), deserializes the token via `S3JsonlCredentials`, builds an `aws-sdk-s3` `Client` with static `Credentials::new` + region from token + optional `endpoint_url_override` (forces path-style addressing when set). Key format: `<prefix>/year=YYYY/month=MM/day=DD/<unix_ms>-<getrandom_nonce_u64_hex>.json`. Body = serde JSON of the flattened audit fields + ts_unix_secs. PUT call wrapped in a 10s `tokio::time::timeout` matching the other dispatchers.
          - [x] `PerOrgSiemDispatcher`'s s3_jsonl arm switched from the "not yet wired" warn to the real `dispatch_s3_jsonl` call.
          - [x] New `scripts/e2e-siem-s3-receiver.py` — stdlib http.server accepting PUT at any path, JSONL-records `{method, path, auth, content_type, body}`. Returns 200 OK with empty body (real S3 returns 200 + ETag header; SDK tolerates the missing ETag). Skips SigV4 validation since the harness doesn't need it.
          - [x] 8 new harness assertions: POST per-org s3_jsonl config (with `endpoint_url_override` → fake S3) → 200, audit triggers, fake S3 got ≥1 PUT, method is PUT, path matches the Hive-partitioned shape (`/<bucket>/<prefix>/year=…/month=…/day=…/*.json`), Authorization carries AWS4-HMAC-SHA256 SigV4 signature, body[`.action`] == invite.created, body[`.org_id`] == ORG_ID_A.
          - **Honest finding — civil_from_unix_secs unit test failed on first run** because the hardcoded epoch for 2026-05-22 was off by 5 days. Recomputed: 56yr * 365 + 14 leap days + 141 day-of-year = 20 595 days × 86 400 = 1 779 408 000. Fixed inline with a `Why:` comment showing the math.
          - **Honest finding — harness path assertion failed on first run** because `aws-sdk-s3` URL-encodes `=` to `%3D` AND appends `?x-id=PutObject` query string. Both are expected SDK behaviors; the assertion was too strict. Relaxed glob to `/ministr-audit-bucket/audit/year*month*day*.json*` so it survives encoding-policy churn.
          - **Honest finding — clippy fired 6 lints on the date-math casts** (`cast_possible_wrap`/`sign_loss`/`truncation`/`bool_to_int_with_if`) plus `too_many_lines` on dispatch_s3_jsonl. All silenced with localized `#[allow]` + a comment explaining the algorithm-bound nature of the casts.
          - **Validation**: cargo workspace test 0 failed (247 ministr-cloud tests, +1 new); cargo clippy `--pedantic -D warnings` clean; `just e2e-cloud-local` 145 → 153 PASS, 0 FAIL.
      - [x] **F5.3-d-iii-c syslog/CEF** *(2026-05-22, complete — harness 125 → 133 PASS)*
        - [x] Extended `ALLOWED_SIEM_KINDS` from `["splunk_hec", "datadog_logs"]` to include `"syslog_cef"`. New `TOKENLESS_SIEM_KINDS = ["syslog_cef"]` const — syslog auth happens at the network layer (mTLS / VPN / source-IP allowlist) so the per-event bearer is unused; the validator skips its empty-token check for these kinds.
        - [x] `validate_siem_upsert` gained per-kind scheme branching: `syslog_cef` requires `tcp://`; `splunk_hec` + `datadog_logs` require `http(s)://`. Cross-kind mismatch is now a 400 — catches "I reused the Datadog URL pattern" as a common operator mistake.
        - [x] New `dispatch_syslog_cef(endpoint, entry)` free helper. Parses `tcp://host:port`, opens a `tokio::net::TcpStream` with a 10s timeout, writes one newline-terminated CEF v0 line, flushes. Failures log `warn` but never propagate.
        - [x] New `format_cef_line(entry)` + `cef_escape(value)` helpers. CEF v0 header: `CEF:0|ministr|ministr-cloud-audit|1|<action>|<action>|5|`. Extension carries standard CEF labels (`src=`, `suser=`, `requestClientApplication=`) plus custom (`orgId=`, `resource=`). `cef_escape` uses `Cow<str>` for the zero-alloc fast path on metachar-free strings; escapes `|`, `\`, `=` per CEF spec; collapses `\n` / `\r` to spaces because they'd otherwise terminate the syslog message mid-payload.
        - [x] `PerOrgSiemDispatcher`'s kind-branch is now 3-arm: `splunk_hec → dispatch_splunk_hec`, `datadog_logs → dispatch_datadog_logs`, `syslog_cef → dispatch_syslog_cef` (token bound but unused on this arm).
        - [x] New harness `scripts/e2e-siem-syslog-receiver.py` — `socketserver.ThreadingTCPServer` that JSONL-records each received line `{line, peer}`. Spawn-readiness probe uses bash's `/dev/tcp` open-and-close since TCP collectors don't expose `/healthz`.
        - [x] 8 new harness assertions: POST per-org `syslog_cef` config (empty token + tcp:// endpoint) → 200, response carries `kind=syslog_cef`, audit triggers, collector got new line, CEF v0 header matches, Signature (field 5) carries the audit action, `orgId=ORG_ID_A` extension present, standard `suser=` CEF label present.
        - [x] 8 new pure unit tests: ALLOWED_SIEM_KINDS lockstep, TOKENLESS_SIEM_KINDS lockstep, validator admits `syslog_cef` + empty token, validator rejects cross-kind scheme mismatch (`syslog_cef` with `http://`, `splunk_hec` with `tcp://`), `cef_escape` three metachar cases (passthrough, `|\=`, newline collapse), `format_cef_line` header + extension shape.
        - **Honest scope choice — TCP only**. UDP syslog is deferred; most production syslog deployments use TCP for reliability anyway. *(Followed up in F5.3-d-iii-c-udp below.)*
        - **Honest scope choice — no TLS layer for the TCP connection**. Production deployments wrap with stunnel or use TLS-syslog (RFC 5425) at the collector edge. F5.3-d-iii-c-tls can land later if needed.
        - **Validation**: cargo workspace test 0 failed (238 ministr-cloud tests, +8 new); cargo clippy `--pedantic -D warnings` clean; `just e2e-cloud-local` 125 → 133 PASS, 0 FAIL.
      - [x] **F5.3-d-iii-c-udp UDP transport fallback for syslog/CEF** *(2026-05-22, complete — harness 133 → 138 PASS)*
        - [x] Refactored `dispatch_syslog_cef` from the all-in-one TCP impl into a scheme-router that calls `dispatch_syslog_cef_tcp` (existing logic, renamed) or `dispatch_syslog_cef_udp` (new). Both maintain the 10s timeout + fire-and-forget posture.
        - [x] `dispatch_syslog_cef_udp` uses `tokio::net::UdpSocket`: binds an ephemeral local socket (`0.0.0.0:0`), sends one datagram via `send_to(line.as_bytes(), host_port)`. **No trailing newline** — each datagram IS one syslog message per RFC 3164 / RFC 5424 §A.2.
        - [x] Validator's `syslog_cef` arm now admits `tcp://` OR `udp://`. Error message updated to enumerate both schemes.
        - [x] 2 new pure unit tests: validator admits `udp://` for `syslog_cef`; validator rejects `udp://` for `splunk_hec` (the inverse cross-kind case mirroring the tcp:// case from F5.3-d-iii-c).
        - [x] New `scripts/e2e-siem-syslog-udp-receiver.py` — `socketserver.ThreadingUDPServer` + `BaseRequestHandler`. Records each datagram as `{line, peer}` JSONL. Spawn-readiness probe is just `kill -0` + 200ms sleep since UDP has no connection handshake.
        - [x] 5 new harness assertions: POST per-org config (`udp://` endpoint) → 200, audit triggers, UDP collector got ≥1 datagram, CEF v0 header matches, `orgId=ORG_ID_A` extension present.
        - **Honest scope choice — no TLS-wrap layer**. UDP-syslog naturally has no TLS option (datagrams are unencrypted). Customers needing both UDP transport + encryption use a TLS-aware syslog proxy (rsyslog / syslog-ng) at their network edge.
        - **Validation**: cargo workspace test 0 failed (240 ministr-cloud tests, +2 new); cargo clippy `--pedantic -D warnings` clean; `just e2e-cloud-local` 133 → 138 PASS, 0 FAIL.
  - **Validation (full F5.3)**: delete attempted on a row via psql as the runtime role → permission denied; the event appears in the customer's Splunk within 60s; a 6-month-old row is still queryable from the archive partition.

    - [x] **F5.4-e-audit Issuance audit log** *(2026-05-22, complete — CLI-only; harness unchanged at 181 PASS)*
      - [x] `mint-license` gained an optional `--audit-log PATH` flag. When set, appends one JSON line per successful mint with `{ts_iso, ts_unix, enterprise_id, seat_count, valid_days, exp, jwt_id_hash}`. `jwt_id_hash` is the first 16 hex chars of `sha256(jwt)` — unique identifier without storing the bearer material. Audit-log write happens BEFORE the JWT is printed/written so a crash in between doesn't leave an orphan issuance.
      - [x] New `ministr cloud list-licenses --audit-log PATH [--format json|table]` subcommand. Table view (default) is sorted ts_unix descending; JSON re-emits the JSONL verbatim (pipeable to jq). Malformed lines from partial writes skipped with a warn.
      - [x] Updated `docs/operator/license-mint.md` with an "Audit log" section covering both commands + storage guidance ("stash alongside your license private key").
      - [x] **Smoke-tested**: minted 2 licenses for acme-corp (50 seats, 365 days) + beta-co (10 seats, 90 days); audit log captured both lines with distinct jwt_id_hashes; table view sorted descending + json view re-emitted both.
      - **Honest scope choice — JSONL file, no DB**. JSONL append is POSIX-atomic for writes ≤ 4 KB (each line is well under); concurrent multi-host writes would interleave half-lines — documented as a single-operator-host limitation. **F5.4-e-audit-db** (landed 2026-05-23, harness 215 → 220 PASS) closed this: new `license_issuances` table + `mint-license --pg-url` dual-write + `list-licenses --pg-url` readback. JSONL stays the local truth; PG becomes the multi-operator-visible mirror.
      - **Honest scope choice — ISO-8601 formatter duplicated** from `ministr-cloud::audit::civil_from_unix_secs` because that helper is module-private; lifting it to a public re-export for one caller wasn't worth the API surface change. Future cleanup chunk can hoist both copies to a shared workspace helper.
      - **Honest scope choice — no harness assertion**. Operator CLI smoke-tested manually like F5.4-e-mint.
      - **Validation**: cargo workspace test 0 failed (252 ministr-cloud tests, unchanged); cargo clippy `--pedantic -D warnings` clean; harness state unchanged at 181 PASS.
    - [x] **F5.4-e-revoke Revocation list** *(2026-05-22, complete — harness 186 → 192 PASS)*
      - Shipped as JSONL revocation list mirroring the F5.4-e-audit log discipline (operator append-only, opt-in env var). `license_jwt_id_hash` moved from CLI-private into `ministr-cloud::license` as `pub fn` so the mint audit, revoke CLI, and boot check all hash identically. New `RevocationRecord` struct + `is_revoked_by_file` helper + `LicenseError::Revoked { hash, reason }` variant + `LicenseError::RevocationListUnreadable`.
      - `validate_license_from_env` extended to consult `MINISTR_LICENSE_REVOCATIONS` env var when set + non-empty; revocation hit returns `Err(Revoked)` so boot logs surface the explicit "license revoked at gate" reason rather than a generic JWT failure.
      - CLI: `ministr cloud revoke-license --jwt PATH | --jwt-id-hash hex --enterprise-id ID --reason "..." --revocation-list PATH`. Hash-only form supports revoking against the audit log when the JWT file is gone.
      - Operator runbook (`docs/operator/license-mint.md`) extended with a "Revocation flow" section covering both forms + Helm/Compose env-var wiring.

      - [ ] `license_revocations` table the serve checks on each boot; offline-cached grace window for graceful degradation when ministr's portal is unreachable.
    - [x] **F5.4-e-revoke-mid-flight-graceful** *(2026-05-23, complete)*
      - [x] `RevocationShutdownHandle` struct in `ministr-cloud/src/revocation_fetch.rs` — `Arc<AtomicBool>` revoked flag + `Arc<Notify>` shutdown signal. `trigger()` sets the flag + notifies; `is_revoked()` reads the flag.
      - [x] `spawn_refresh_task` gains `shutdown_handle: Option<RevocationShutdownHandle>`. On revocation: when handle is `Some`, triggers graceful signal and returns (task exits cleanly). When `None`, falls back to `process::exit(1)` for backward compat.
      - [x] `cmd_serve_http` creates the handle when URL-based revocation is configured, wires `axum::serve(...).with_graceful_shutdown(handle.shutdown.notified())`. After graceful drain completes, exits with code 1 so the orchestrator restarts. In-flight requests finish rather than getting connection-reset.

Existing harness F5.4-e-revoke-mid-flight assertions (229→231 PASS) continue to hold — the behavior difference (drain vs instant exit) isn't observable from the harness's perspective since the exit code is still 1.

      - [ ] Internal webapp surfacing the F5.4-e-mint flow with templated email distribution + audit-log browser + revocation toggle.
    - [x] **F5.4-e-rotate Key rotation tooling** *(2026-05-22, complete — harness 192 → 199 PASS)*
      - Shipped `ministr cloud rotate-license-keys --audit-log PATH --revocation-list PATH --new-private-key PATH --out-dir DIR --new-audit-log PATH --valid-days N`. Reads the existing audit log, dedupes by `enterprise_id` keeping the latest `ts_unix`, filters out revoked hashes via `load_revoked_hashes` and naturally-expired records (`exp <= now`), then re-mints one fresh JWT per surviving enterprise via the existing `sign_license_jwt` helper. Writes `<safe_enterprise_id>-<short_hash>.jwt` per license to `--out-dir`; appends each re-issuance to `--new-audit-log` so the rotation cycle is itself auditable.
      - `enterprise_id` filename sanitisation strips everything outside `[a-zA-Z0-9._-]` to `_` — prevents path traversal from a typo or hostile audit-log injection.
      - `valid_days` is operator-supplied uniformly; preserving each license's original remaining lifetime would be marginal value at higher cost (need per-record math + would surprise the operator). The "extend or shorten the cycle uniformly" posture is what most rotation playbooks need.
      - New `pub fn load_revoked_hashes(path) -> HashSet<String>` in `ministr-cloud::license` — batch sibling to `is_revoked_by_file` for the rotate flow's O(1) revocation check. 2 new unit tests.
      - Operator runbook (`docs/operator/license-mint.md`) extended with a "Key rotation flow" 5-step section walking through generate-new-keypair → rotate → distribute → customers paste → retire old key. Includes the rotation summary stdout format + an explicit "what this does NOT do" list (no automatic emails, no signature verification of old JWTs, no per-customer horizons).
      - Honest scope choice — no email distribution; operators still copy reissued JWTs to their CRM by hand. F5.4-e-ui (deferred) would close that with a webapp.
      - 7 new harness assertions: keypairs generated, 2 licenses minted, alpha revoked, rotation summary line ("1 re-issued, 1 skipped (revoked)"), exactly 1 JWT in out-dir, filename starts with `rotate-beta-`, new audit log carries exactly 1 record for `rotate-beta`.
  - **Validation (full F5.4):** customer runs `helm install ministr/enterprise -f values.yaml` with a fresh license key → pod boots, accepts SAML logins, indexes a private repo, mirrors Atlas — never reaches `mcp.ministr.ai` except for license-revocation checks (which fall through to a cached grace window if our side is unreachable).

    - [x] **F5.5-b-sla-skeleton** *(2026-05-22, complete — harness 199 → 204 PASS)* — unauthenticated `GET /sla` endpoint on the public admin router returning `{status, version, uptime_secs, started_at_iso}` JSON. Foundation for the eventual `status.ministr.ai` dashboard + richer load-balancer probes that want more than `/healthz`'s binary up/down. Boot timestamp captured via `Instant::now()` in `AdminState`'s constructors; ISO formatter is a local copy of the Howard Hinnant civil-from-unix-secs algorithm (the cloud-side helper is module-private; lifting to a workspace-shared helper is a separate cleanup chunk). Unit tests cover epoch zero + 2026-05-22 + leap-day (2024-02-29) round-trips. Honest scope: latency percentiles (p95) and cross-pod persistent metrics are explicitly out of this chunk — separate `F5.5-b-latency` and `F5.5-b-persist` follow-ups.
    - [x] **F5.5-b-latency** *(2026-05-23, complete — harness 204 → 207 PASS)* — `LatencyTracker` (Arc/Mutex over `VecDeque<u32>` microseconds, default cap 1024) + `record_latency_middleware` axum function + `/sla.latency` JSON field carrying `{count, p50_ms, p95_ms, p99_ms}` (None until first sample). Mounted on the final composed router INSIDE the CORS layer (CORS wraps it) so the rolling window stays a true measure of in-process request handling. Sample units stored in micros (u32 covers ~71 minutes/sample); rendered at the JSON seam in milliseconds because the SLA contract is in ms. 6 unit tests cover empty / single-sample / known-distribution p50=50/p95=95/p99=99 / rolling-window-drops-oldest / zero-capacity-clamps-to-1 / clone-shares-backing-buffer. Live harness sees p95=8ms over 93 samples — well under the contract target of 200ms. Honest scope: no per-route bucketing (every request lands in one pool), no cross-pod aggregation (restart drops the buffer — that's `F5.5-b-persist`'s job).
    - [x] **F5.5-b-persist** *(2026-05-23, complete — write + read + retention all landed)* — restart drops the in-memory percentile history; periodic flush + DB-backed query + cron-style prune give durable historical evidence. Split into write/read/retention; full track shipped in one conversation.
      - [x] **F5.5-b-persist-write** *(2026-05-23, complete — harness 207 → 210 PASS)* — migration `0016_request_latency_snapshots.sql` (id BIGSERIAL, ts_unix, sample_count, p50/p95/p99 INTEGER µs, idx on ts_unix DESC); new `ministr-cloud::sla::persist_snapshot` pure async fn; `cmd_serve_http` spawns a tokio task when `cloud_pool` is `Some` that ticks every `MINISTR_SLA_FLUSH_SECS` (default 60s) and flushes the current `LatencyTracker` snapshot. First tick swallowed so no zero-row lands at boot; snapshot-is-None skip so no zero-sample row ever. Self-hosted serve (no `cloud_pool`) leaves the task unspawned — historical p95 isn't a self-hosted concern. Harness sets `MINISTR_SLA_FLUSH_SECS=2` so multiple rows land in a single run; live: 8 rows after 30s of harness traffic, p95=6.8ms on the most recent. Storage cost: ~50 bytes × 1440 flushes/day × 30 days ≈ 2 MB/pod/month.
      - [x] **F5.5-b-persist-read** *(2026-05-23, complete — harness 210 → 212 PASS)* — `SlaWindowStore` trait in `ministr-api` (MIT) with one async method `max_p95_since(since_ts_unix: i64) -> Option<u32>` + `PostgresSlaWindowStore` in `ministr-cloud` (single `SELECT MAX(p95_us) ... WHERE ts_unix >= $1` hitting the F5.5-b-persist-write index). `AdminState::with_sla_window_store` builder mirrors the existing `with_api_key_resolver` / `with_plan_resolver` pattern; `/sla.latency` gains a `window_30d_max_p95_ms: Option<u64>` field rendered from microseconds. Self-hosted serve leaves the store `None` and the field renders as `null`. Resolver errors log at warn and fall back to `null` so a transient backend blip never breaks the `/sla` probe that load balancers depend on. Live: `9ms` historical max vs `8ms` current p95 — rolling-max monotonicity holds. 4 unit tests (object-safe, canned/none/error stub behaviour); 2 new harness assertions (numeric ms field, max ≥ current monotonicity).
      - [x] **F5.5-b-persist-retention** *(2026-05-23, complete — harness 212 → 215 PASS)* — `ministr-cloud::sla::delete_snapshots_older_than(pool, cutoff_ts_unix)` pure async fn + new `ministr cloud sla-prune-snapshots --older-than-secs SECS` CLI subcommand. Operator wraps in cron / Azure Container Apps Job with `--older-than-secs $((30 * 86400))` for the canonical 30-day retention. CLI-only (no in-process tokio task) so retention cadence is policy that doesn't require a serve restart to tune. Defensive: `--older-than-secs 0` refuses with a clear error so the most common operator typo doesn't nuke the table. 1 integration test gated on `MINISTR_TEST_PG_URL` (writes 2 rows with old + new ts, prunes between them, asserts only the new survived). 3 harness assertions (CLI exits 0, row count drops 9→1, defensive-0 refuses).
    - [x] **F5.5-b-page** *(skeleton landed; dashboard deferred)* — split into skeleton + dashboard.
      - [x] **F5.5-b-page-skeleton** *(2026-05-23, complete — Next.js page builds clean)* — new `/status` route at `docs-next/app/(home)/status/page.tsx` (server component, `revalidate: 30`). #### F5 done criterion

An enterprise customer installs ministr via Helm in their own VPC, federates to their Entra ID for SSO, indexes a private repo, mirrors a 100-repo subset of Atlas into their VPC, sees immutable audit events streamed to their Splunk, rotates their CMK via Azure Key Vault, and operates fully under the SLA — all gated by a license key our portal issued.

### F6 — Stickiness (cross-cutting; ships continuously throughout F1–F5)

> These are the agent-specific superpowers that make ministr's per-agent API surface the integration moat. Once an agent has integrated against `ministr_compress` + persistent sessions + cross-corpus search, switching out has real engineering cost.

- [x] **F6.1 Persistent agent sessions** *(2026-05-21, complete)* *(moves shipped in-memory primitives to durable state)* — split into a/b/c/c-followup/d/e/f, all landed.
  - [x] **F6.1-a SessionStorage trait + PostgresSessionStorage + migration** *(2026-05-21)*
    - [x] New `SessionStorage` trait + `SessionSnapshot` struct in `ministr-api/src/session_storage.rs` (MIT seam, mirrors the `ApiKeyResolver` boxed-future shape because reads need return values). v0 snapshot fields: `session_id`, `tenant_id`, `corpus_id?`, `opened_at`, `last_seen_at`, `budget_used`, `coherence_score`. **Honest scope choice**: snapshot is intentionally narrow — claims / drops / invalidated sections / memory tracker are recomputed lazily on resume from the corpus, not persisted. Persisting them would multiply storage cost without obvious agent-visible benefit.
    - [x] Migration `0008_agent_sessions.sql` adds the `agent_sessions` table with PK `(tenant_id, id)` so two tenants can use the same session id without colliding. Indexes on `(tenant_id, corpus_id)` (list-sessions hot path) and `last_seen_at` (future stale-session prune).
    - [x] `PostgresSessionStorage` impl in `ministr-cloud/src/session_storage.rs`. Four methods: `save` (UPSERT on PK, preserves `opened_at` across re-saves, advances `last_seen_at`), `load` (single PK query, returns `Option<SessionSnapshot>`), `touch` (cheap `last_seen_at = now()` update), `delete` (idempotent).
    - [x] Four unit tests in ministr-api (save/load round-trip, unknown-session returns None, save upserts on PK, delete idempotent). Plus a compile-time dyn-compatibility check in ministr-cloud. Postgres-integration coverage of the SQL paths gated on `MINISTR_TEST_PG_URL` per convention.
    - [x] Migration registered in `db.rs` MIGRATIONS list at index 8.
    - [x] **No wiring into SessionRegistry yet** — that's a "when to checkpoint" decision (every mutation? periodic? on close?) the user should drive. F6.1-b will pick a checkpoint strategy and wire the snapshot-on-write hook.
    - **Validation:** cargo workspace test green (one pre-existing flaky test `full_flow_survey_read_extract_via_call_tool` in ministr-mcp — documented in F3.7b's note as a claim-extraction race unrelated to backend changes; passes on re-run; my changes don't touch its path); clippy `--pedantic -D warnings` clean. Live: a future F6.1-b will call `save` after each mutation; this iteration ships the seam ready to accept that wiring.
  - [x] **F6.1-b SessionRegistry storage plumbing** *(2026-05-21)*
    - [x] Added `ministr-api` as a dep of `ministr-core` (peer-foundation crate; ministr-mcp + ministr-daemon already follow the same layering). Required for SessionRegistry to hold an `Option<Arc<dyn SessionStorage>>` without re-declaring the trait.
    - [x] `SessionRegistry::with_storage(Arc<dyn SessionStorage>)` builder + `storage: Option<Arc<dyn SessionStorage>>` field. Default `None` so self-hosted serve and pre-F6.1 cloud deployments stay in-memory.
    - [x] `persist_snapshot(&self, snapshot: SessionSnapshot)` method — fire-and-forget `tokio::spawn` → `storage.save`. Failures log at warn level but never propagate; a storage hiccup must not break a live tool call. Collapses to a no-op when no storage backend is wired so callers can invoke unconditionally.
    - [x] **Honest scope choice — no caller-site invocation yet**. The "when to checkpoint" decision (every mutation vs periodic vs on-close) stays open. F6.1-c will pick the choke point (likely `MinistrServer::ensure_session_mut` post-handler, or the UsageTracker's consume path) and wire `persist_snapshot` calls there. Bundling it with lazy-restore in F6.1-c means the round-trip is provable end-to-end in one chunk.
    - [x] Three new unit tests: `registry_storage_defaults_to_none` (no-op without backend), `with_storage_attaches_backend` (builder), `persist_snapshot_fires_through_storage` (stub-backed end-to-end with `#[tokio::test]` + yield loop). Plus the existing 25 tests continue to pass — no regressions to the in-memory path.
    - **Validation:** cargo workspace test green; clippy `--pedantic -D warnings` clean.
  - [x] **F6.1-c-followup — UsageTracker pre-seed + budget restore** *(2026-05-21)*
    - [x] New `PRIOR_CONSUMPTION_CONTENT_ID = "__ministr_restored_prior__"` sentinel const in `ministr-core/src/session/window.rs`. The `__ministr_*` prefix is reserved for internal sentinels — agent content_ids are user-derived and shouldn't start with that prefix.
    - [x] `WindowEstimator::record_prior_consumption(token_count) -> Vec<String>` records a synthetic entry against the sentinel id. Returns evicted ids (mirrors `record`); empty when the snapshot is well-formed (`budget_used ≤ capacity`).
    - [x] `UsageTracker::seed_prior_consumption(token_count) -> Vec<String>` proxies through to the window. The caller is `SessionRegistry::try_restore`.
    - [x] `try_restore` now seeds the restored budget after creating the shell, with three guard layers: (a) `i64 → usize` via `try_from` (collapses to 0 on negative / oversized rows), (b) skip when `budget_used == 0` (so a never-delivered session doesn't accumulate a phantom zero-cost row), (c) clamp to `capacity - 1` for overlarge corrupted rows (keeps the synthetic prior in the window rather than triggering immediate eviction that would silently zero the budget).
    - [x] **Coherence-score restore deferred** — Session's coherence model doesn't have a single scalar to set; `coherence_score` in the snapshot stays as an informational field that hydrates via a future refactor. Today's value: budget pressure resumes correctly across pods, which is the load-bearing fidelity for the F6.1 done criterion's "budget preserved exactly" half.
    - [x] Two new tests: `try_restore_seeds_budget_used_into_in_memory_tracker` (500-token snapshot through a 1000-cap registry → tracker reports tokens_used = 500), `try_restore_clamps_overlarge_budget_to_capacity` (9M-token corrupted snapshot → tracker clamps to within capacity rather than evicting the seed).
    - **Validation:** cargo workspace test green (no flake this run); clippy `--pedantic -D warnings` clean. F6.1's "budget preserved across pods" half now passes end-to-end through the StubStorage round-trip. The remaining F6.1-d (drops ledger persistence) is the last fidelity piece.
  - [x] **F6.1-c Lazy-restore on first access** *(2026-05-21)*
    - [x] New `SessionRegistry::try_restore(id, tenant_id, budget_config, access_mode) -> Option<SessionSnapshot>` async method. Decision tree: in-memory shadow → `None`; no storage backend → `None`; storage miss → `None`; storage hit → materialise a fresh `SessionEntry` shell via the same path as `create_session` and return the loaded snapshot. Storage errors log at warn level and collapse to `None` so a Postgres hiccup falls through to fresh creation rather than hard-failing the request.
    - [x] **Honest scope choice — partial fidelity**. The returned `SessionSnapshot` carries the persisted `budget_used` and `coherence_score`, but the freshly-created in-memory `SessionEntry` does NOT yet have those values seeded — `UsageTracker` doesn't expose a pre-seed constructor today. v0's value is "the session shell exists on this pod" (so the audit-feed / activity counters that key on session continuity work) rather than "full state restored". A future iteration adds `UsageTracker::with_consumed` + a coherence-restore path and stitches the persisted values through.
    - [x] **No caller-site wiring yet**. F6.1-c-followup will wire `MinistrServer::ensure_session_mut` to `await registry.try_restore(...)` before falling through to `get_or_create`. That requires the MCP server to thread `tenant_id` through the resolve path, which is non-trivial; the present iteration keeps the wiring choice separate so the seam doesn't carry a half-finished implementation.
    - [x] Five new tests: `try_restore_returns_none_when_session_already_in_memory` (in-memory shadow), `..._when_no_storage` (no-op without backend), `..._when_storage_misses` (graceful miss), `..._hydrates_shell_when_storage_hits` (round-trip the snapshot back), `persist_then_restore_round_trips_through_storage` (full pod-1 → pod-2 simulation: a second registry sharing the same StubStorage hydrates what the first persisted). The StubStorage's `load` was strengthened to actually return saved snapshots so the round-trip is provable end-to-end through the trait.
    - **Validation:** cargo workspace test green (one pre-existing flake `full_flow_survey_read_extract_via_call_tool` in ministr-mcp — claim-extraction race documented in F3.7b's note; passes on re-run; my changes don't touch its path); clippy `--pedantic -D warnings` clean.
  - [x] **F6.1-d Drops ledger persistence** *(2026-05-21, complete)* — split into d-a (trait + impl + migration), d-b (registry plumbing + restore hook), d-c (tool-handler-level append wiring), all landed.
    - [x] **F6.1-d-a `DropsLedger` trait + `PostgresDropsLedger` + migration** *(2026-05-21)*
      - [x] New `DropsLedger` trait + `DropEntry` struct in `ministr-api/src/drops_ledger.rs` (MIT seam, mirrors `SessionStorage`'s boxed-future shape). Two methods: `append` (fire-and-forget eviction event; the in-memory drop already happened, the ledger row is a durability layer) and `list_for_session` (async read used by `try_restore` to hydrate evicted-content awareness).
      - [x] **Separated from `SessionStorage`** deliberately. Snapshot semantics are "tell me where the session is right now" (occasional, full state); drops semantics are "log this eviction event" (every drop, append-only). Mixing them would force snapshot writes to bloat with every drop OR force drops to wait for snapshot cadence. Two traits compose cleanly at the call site (Session will fire both).
      - [x] Migration `0009_session_drops.sql` adds `session_drops(id BIGSERIAL, session_id TEXT, tenant_id UUID, claim_id TEXT, evicted_at TIMESTAMPTZ)`. BIGSERIAL key gives chronological ordering for replay. Two indexes: `(tenant_id, session_id, id)` (hot-path lookup, covering for SELECT id) and `(evicted_at)` (future retention cron).
      - [x] **Wall-clock policy** — `evicted_at` is captured client-side rather than `DEFAULT now()` because the eviction happened in-process before the ledger append; recording the persist time would lie about when the agent actually lost the claim. Documented in the SQL comment so a future maintainer doesn't "simplify" by switching to `DEFAULT now()`.
      - [x] `PostgresDropsLedger` impl in `ministr-cloud/src/drops_ledger.rs`. Single INSERT for `append`, single ORDER BY id ASC SELECT for `list_for_session`. Cheap clone via `Arc<Pool>`.
      - [x] 3 unit tests in ministr-api (append→list round-trip, tenant + session filtering, empty for unknown session). Compile-time dyn-usability check in ministr-cloud. Postgres-integration coverage of the SQL paths gated on `MINISTR_TEST_PG_URL` per convention.
      - [x] Migration registered in `db.rs` MIGRATIONS list at index 9.
      - **Validation:** cargo workspace test green; clippy `--pedantic -D warnings` clean.
    - [x] **F6.1-d-b SessionRegistry drops plumbing + restore hook** *(2026-05-21)*
      - [x] Added `drops_ledger: Option<Arc<dyn DropsLedger>>` field + `with_drops_ledger` builder on SessionRegistry (mirrors the F6.1-b storage shape).
      - [x] New `record_drops(&self, tenant_id, session_id, claim_ids: &[String])` helper: captures a single `evicted_at` wall-clock for the batch (drops from the same record_tokens call are semantically simultaneous), spawns one tokio task per claim through `ledger.append`. Failures log at warn level but never propagate. No-op when no ledger is wired so callers can invoke unconditionally.
      - [x] Renamed `try_restore`'s return type from `Option<SessionSnapshot>` to `Option<RestoredSession { snapshot, drops }>` so a single call returns both the snapshot and the ledger's drop list. Existing 5 try_restore tests updated to match the new shape (each was a 4-line tweak, no semantic regression).
      - [x] `try_restore` now consults the ledger via `list_for_session` AFTER the snapshot load. Empty vec on miss / error keeps the caller's match arm simple; a real ledger outage doesn't block the restore.
      - [x] Inlined `iso8601_now` + `format_iso8601` helpers in registry.rs (civil-calendar math borrowed from `ministr_mcp::task::iso8601_now`'s shape; a future cleanup can extract a shared helper).
      - [x] **Honest scope choice — no tool-handler-level append wiring**. The MCP server's tool handlers (which know tenant_id from auth middleware and session_id from request context) need to call `record_drops` after `record_tokens` returns non-empty evicted ids. That requires changes in `ministr-mcp` that are easier to scope independently. Today's registry exposes the helper; ministr-mcp wires it next.
      - [x] 6 new tests: default-None field, builder, batch-of-3 fires 3 entries, empty list is no-op, try_restore includes drops when ledger wired, try_restore returns empty drops when no ledger. 42 registry tests total (5 prior try_restore tests updated to new return type).
      - **Validation:** cargo workspace test green (no flake this run); clippy `--pedantic -D warnings` clean. The F6.1 done criterion's "drops preserved across pods" half now works end-to-end through the StubLedger round-trip; tool-handler-level append wiring closes the production path.
    - [x] **F6.1-d-c Tool-handler-level drops append wiring** *(2026-05-21)*
      - [x] New `emit_section_drops(reg, session_id, evicted_ids)` helper in `ministr-mcp/src/server/session.rs`. Reads `crate::tenant_scope::current()` and calls `reg.record_drops(...)` when both the tenant scope is present and the eviction list is non-empty. Factored into a free function (rather than inlined) so the wiring is independently testable without a full `MinistrServer` fixture.

Lock is still held — `record_drops` only spawns fire-and-forget tasks, so holding it across the call is cheap.

  - [x] **F6.1-e Tool-handler-level snapshot checkpoint** *(2026-05-21)*
    - [x] New `emit_session_snapshot(reg, session_id, status)` helper in `ministr-mcp/src/server/session.rs`. Reads `tenant_scope::current()`, builds a `ministr_api::SessionSnapshot` from the live `UsageStatus` (`budget_used` via `i64::try_from(status.tokens_used)` saturating to `i64::MAX` for the impossible-but-defensive overflow case), and calls `reg.persist_snapshot(snapshot)`. Helper is a no-op when no tenant is scoped (mirrors `emit_section_drops`'s posture).
    - [x] Called from `record_section_delivery` right after `emit_section_drops`, inside the same lock window. Same NLL release point — `entry` borrow has already ended at the `status` capture so `reg` is freely usable as `&SessionRegistry` for the fire-and-forget `persist_snapshot`.

    - [x] Promoted `ministr_mcp::task::iso8601_now` from private to `pub(crate)` so the new helper can format timestamps consistently with how `PostgresSessionStorage`'s `to_char` emits them.   - [x] **F6.1-f Tool-handler-level try_restore wiring** *(2026-05-21)*
    - [x] New `try_restore_session(reg, session_id)` free async helper in `ministr-mcp/src/server/session.rs`. Reads `tenant_scope::current()` and delegates to `reg.try_restore(session_id, &tenant_id, None, AccessMode::ReadWrite).await`. Short-circuits when no tenant is scoped (stdio / self-hosted serve can't lookup by `(tenant_id, session_id)` PK anyway). `try_restore` itself is idempotent — already-in-memory sessions short-circuit there — so the helper is safe to invoke unconditionally before `ensure_session_mut`.
    - [x] Wired into BOTH `ensure_session_mut` callers: `record_section_delivery` (line 87) and `build_response_with` (line 230). Insertion point is right after `self.registry.lock().await` and before the `ensure_session_mut` call — the await on storage.load happens while holding the tokio mutex, which is appropriate for `tokio::sync::Mutex` (designed for this; yields while blocked). Calling on every request is cheap after the first hit because `try_restore` returns `Some` on the first hit + `None` on subsequent in-memory short-circuits.
    - [x] Extended the F6.1-e `StubStorage.load` to actually return saved snapshots by `(tenant_id, session_id)` PK so round-trip tests can pre-seed via direct push into `saves`. Matches the registry.rs F6.1-c `StubStorage` shape.
    - [x] Four new tokio tests in `session.rs::tests`: `try_restore_session_hydrates_when_storage_hits` (pre-seed a snapshot, scope a tenant, helper materialises the shell), `..._skips_when_no_tenant_scope` (stdio / self-hosted no-op), `..._is_noop_when_already_in_memory` (registry's own idempotency works through the helper), `..._is_noop_when_no_storage` (registry-storage=None branch).
    - [x] **Honest scope choice — shell hydration only**. The lazy-restore materialises the SessionEntry shell + seeds `budget_used` (via F6.1-c-followup's `UsageTracker::seed_prior_consumption`). Coherence-score restoration remains deferred per F6.1-c-followup. The shell-only contract is enough to close the F6.1 done criterion: a resumed session shows the same budget pressure as before the pod restart.
    - **Validation:** cargo workspace test green (0 failed); cargo clippy `--pedantic -D warnings` clean. F6.1's full done criterion is now reachable end-to-end: pod 1 calls `record_section_delivery` → `emit_section_drops` persists drops + `emit_session_snapshot` persists budget → pod 2 calls any handler → `try_restore_session` rehydrates from `PostgresSessionStorage` + `PostgresDropsLedger`. Live validation pending the next deploy (cloud `cmd_serve_http` wires `PostgresSessionStorage` + `PostgresDropsLedger` via `SessionRegistry::with_storage` + `with_drops_ledger`).

  - [x] **F6.2-a Session bundle export backend (tar)** *(2026-05-21)*
    - [x] New `ministr-mcp/src/sessions/{mod,export}.rs` module with `SessionBundleManifest` serde struct (schema_version=1; session_id / opened_at / exported_at / budget_used / delivered_count / total_delivered_tokens / pressure_level) + `build_session_bundle(session_id, &SessionEntry) -> Result<Vec<u8>, String>` helper. Archive layout: `manifest.json` + `delivered.jsonl` (one `DeliveredItem` per line, sorted by `turn_delivered` ascending for stable diff-able replays).
    - [x] **Archive format choice — tar, not zip.** Matches the existing `.ministr-index` corpus-bundle convention so no new compression dep lands; the workspace already pins `tar = "0.4"`. The roadmap's `.session.zip` extension becomes `.session.tar` in v0 — a future chunk can swap to zip if downstream tooling demands it.

Wired in `cmd_serve_http` behind `ministr:read` scope on the OAuth path; mounted unconditionally so self-hosted users can also export sessions for debugging.

    - [x] Promoted `ministr_mcp::task::iso8601_from_secs` to `pub(crate)` so the manifest can derive `opened_at` from `Session::elapsed()` (the live struct holds a monotonic `Instant`, not wall-clock; the derivation is approximate but stable enough for inspector display).

StubDropsLedger mirrors the F6.1-d-b pattern.

  - [x] **F6.2-c Blob storage + signed URL** *(2026-05-21)*
    - [x] New `SessionBundleStore` trait + `SignedBundleUrl` / `SessionBundleStoreError` types in `ministr-api/src/session_bundle_store.rs` (MIT seam, mirrors `DropsLedger`'s boxed-future shape). Two methods: `put_and_sign(tenant_id, session_id, bytes)` + `verify_and_get(blob_path, token)`. Three stub-backed unit tests cover the dyn-dispatch contract.
    - [x] `CloudSessionBundleStore` in `ministr-cloud/src/session_bundle_store.rs` — Azure Blob upload at `sessions/{tenant}/{session_id}/{ts}.tar` + HMAC-SHA256-signed URLs `?expires={unix}&sig={hex}`. `DEFAULT_SIGNED_URL_TTL_SECS = 24 * 60 * 60` matches the spec; per-store override via `with_ttl_secs`. Min 32-byte secret enforced at construction; constant-time signature compare via `subtle` (reuses the same crate the F1.5 Stripe-inbound verifier and F3.5 webhook dispatcher use). 9 unit tests cover sign/parse/verify shape, secret-length floor, blob-path format, and `Debug` doesn't leak the secret.
    - [x] `build_session_bundle_store_from_env(cloud_base_url)` factory in the same module — keys on `MINISTR_BLOB_STORE_KIND=azure` + existing `MINISTR_BLOB_AZURE_ACCOUNT` + new `MINISTR_SESSION_BUNDLE_SIGNING_SECRET` (operator generates via `openssl rand -base64 32`) + new `MINISTR_SESSION_BUNDLE_CONTAINER` (default `ministr-session-bundles`). Returns `None` when any are missing so self-hosted serve falls through to inline tar.
    - [x] `SessionExportState::with_bundle_store(Arc<dyn SessionBundleStore>)` builder + `bundle_store: Option<...>` field. `handle_export` upgraded — when both store + tenant scope are present, uploads the bundle and returns JSON `SignedBundleUrl { url, expires_at }`; on store error logs at warn and rebuilds the bundle for the inline-tar fallback; otherwise (self-hosted / no-scope) ships the F6.2-a/b inline-tar shape unchanged.
    - [x] New `GET /api/v1/sessions/bundles/{*path}?expires=…&sig=…` handler — calls `store.verify_and_get(blob_path, raw_query)`. Returns 200 + `application/x-tar` on success, 403 on `InvalidToken`, 404 on `NotFound`, 500 on `Storage`. Mounted unconditionally so the URL scheme stays opaque (404 when no store wired, never "this deployment doesn't have a store" leak).
    - [x] `cmd_serve_http` wires `CloudSessionBundleStore` when the env is set; logs `session bundle store wired — uploads to blob + returns signed URL` at info on boot, or `disabled — handle_export streams inline tar` at debug otherwise. Self-hosted serve unaffected.
    - [x] Tauri `cloud_fetch_session_bundle` upgraded — branches on `Content-Type` header. `application/json` ⇒ parse `SignedBundleResponse`, follow the URL with a bare GET (no bearer; signature is in the query), parse the resulting tar. `application/x-tar` ⇒ parse inline directly. Same `CloudSessionBundle` payload reaches the React inspector in both shapes — UI unchanged.
    - [x] Promoted `ministr_mcp::task::iso8601_from_secs` from `pub(crate)` to `pub` so the cloud-side `expires_at` field stays byte-identical to the in-bundle `opened_at` / `exported_at` strings the manifest emits (the inspector sorts on these lexically).
    - [x] **Honest scope choice — no direct Azure SAS**. The official Azure Rust SDK v1 (GA'd May 2026) doesn't yet expose user-delegation SAS minting. Production pods authenticate via Managed Identity and don't have the account key for shared-key SAS. Self-signed HMAC tokens served by our own download route avoid the entire SAS-vs-MI mismatch, give us hooks for metering / audit in a future iteration, and keep the bytes flowing through the same TLS termination as the rest of the API. Bundle sizes are KB-scale so the proxy hop is cheap. When the SDK grows user-delegation SAS, the trait's `put_and_sign` can swap implementations without touching the route or the Tauri command.
    - [x] **Honest scope choice — store error falls back to inline tar**. If the blob upload fails after we've successfully built the bundle, the handler rebuilds the bundle inside a fresh registry lock and ships it inline. The user still receives a usable export rather than a 500; the operator sees the warn log. Costs a second build pass — acceptable for the rare-failure path.
    - [x] Four new tests in `sessions::export::tests` (`put_and_sign_round_trips_through_dyn_store`, `put_and_sign_error_surfaces_to_caller`, `with_bundle_store_attaches_backend`, `verify_and_get_validates_token`) + 12 existing tests still pass = 16 total.
    - **Validation:** cargo workspace test green (0 failures); cargo clippy `--pedantic -D warnings` clean; ministr-app `tsc --noEmit` + `vite build` clean. Live: `POST /api/v1/sessions/{id}/export` with the bundle-store env populated → returns `{"url":"https://mcp.ministr.ai/api/v1/sessions/bundles/sessions/{tenant}/{id}/{ts}.tar?expires=…&sig=…","expires_at":"…"}`; the URL is fetchable for 24h without a bearer. Deferred to next deploy.
