    - [x] **F6.2-e-followup Tenant filter on /api/v1/sessions** *(2026-05-21)* — closes the cross-tenant leak F6.2-e shipped with. Four layers: (1) new `tenant_id: Option<String>` field on `SessionEntry` in `ministr-core/src/session/registry.rs` (existing `parent_session_id` / `client_name` hint-stamping pattern), defaults to `None` in `create_session`; (2) `try_restore` stamps `entry.tenant_id = Some(snapshot.tenant_id.clone())` so restored shells carry the right identity across pod recycles; (3) `ministr-mcp`'s `ensure_session_mut` stamps from `tenant_scope::current()` the first time a session is touched on a cloud request; (4) `handle_list` reads the scope once per request, admits all when `None` (self-hosted), admits only `tenant_id == Some(scope)` entries when `Some(t)`. Pre-stamping legacy entries with `tenant_id = None` are invisible to scoped callers — safe-by-default; they leak nothing. Two new tests: `session_entry_default_tenant_id_is_none` + `list_endpoint_filters_by_tenant_scope` (covers self-hosted, two-tenant isolation, unknown-tenant-sees-nothing including unstamped). **Validation:** cargo workspace test green (11 sessions tests + one pre-existing flake passing on retry); cargo clippy `--pedantic -D warnings` clean.
    - [x] **F6.2-e-followup-ii Tenant ownership check on /api/v1/sessions/{id}/export** *(2026-05-21)* — closes the second leak (export-by-id was still ungated). Three layers: (1) extracted `admit_session_for_scope(scope, entry_tenant)` helper with full doc-comment matrix; (2) `handle_export` applies the predicate post-lookup and returns **404** (not 403) on cross-tenant access so existence isn't leaked across tenants (mirrors the "session not found" shape so attackers can't enumerate id space); (3) renamed the prior filter test to `list_endpoint_filter_subsets_via_admit_helper` and added a 4-corner `admit_session_for_scope_matrix` unit test as a regression guard both endpoints share. **Validation:** cargo workspace test green (12 sessions tests); cargo clippy `--pedantic -D warnings` clean. Live: a scoped caller `POST /api/v1/sessions/<other-tenant-id>/export` → 404 "session not found"; same caller's own id → 200 + tar bytes. Deferred to next deploy.
    - [x] Two new unit tests in `sessions::export::tests`: `session_summary_from_entry_carries_live_fields` (deliveries + budget reflected correctly); `session_summary_serde_round_trip` (wire-shape regression guard for the TS mirror).
    - **Validation:** cargo workspace test green (9 sessions tests now); cargo clippy `--pedantic -D warnings` clean; ministr-app `tsc --noEmit` + `vite build` clean. Live: authenticated user sees the inspector dropdown populated with live sessions → picks one → clicks Fetch → sees the trace. Deferred to next deploy.
  - **Validation:** export a 30-minute session → tar contains a deterministic `manifest.json` + per-event JSON-lines; opening in the inspector renders the full trace; signed URL expires at exactly 24h. *All five sub-bullets landed; live cross-env smoke test pending the next deploy with `MINISTR_SESSION_BUNDLE_SIGNING_SECRET` populated.*

- [x] **F6.3 Cross-corpus search** *(2026-05-21, complete)* *(Pro+ feature; depends on F2.6)* — split into a/b, both landed.
  - [x] **F6.3-a Backend fan-out + `source_corpus` discriminator** *(2026-05-21)*
    - [x] New `source_corpus: Option<String>` field on `ministr-core::service::SurveyResult` (with `#[serde(skip_serializing_if = "Option::is_none")]` so existing wire shape is preserved); mirrored on `ministr-api::query::SurveyResult`; propagated through `ministr-daemon::convert::survey_result` and `ministr-mcp::backend::convert::api_survey_to_service`.
    - [x] New `corpus_ids: Option<Vec<String>>` parameter on `SurveyParams` in `ministr-mcp/src/server/types.rs`. When `Some(non-empty)`, takes precedence over `project`.
    - [x] Free helper `cross_corpus_survey(backend, tenant_subject, corpus_ids, query, top_k, exclude_ids)` in `ministr-mcp/src/server/mod.rs` — sequential per-corpus `backend.survey_with_exclude` calls; per-corpus errors log + skip rather than fail the whole fan-out; propagates the last error only when EVERY per-corpus call failed.
    - [x] Pure `merge_cross_corpus_results(per_corpus, top_k)` helper extracted from the orchestrator — tags each result with its source corpus, sorts by score descending (stable), truncates to `top_k`, sums `deduplicated_count`. Six unit tests cover tagging, sort order, truncation, dedup summation, empty input, and pre-existing-tag overwrite semantics.
    - [x] Survey handler branches on `is_cross_corpus`; cross-corpus path SKIPS the existing elicitation re-run (the disambiguation heuristic is single-corpus framed and the merge distorts the "spread" prompt).
    - [x] **Honest scope choice — sequential, not parallel**. `tokio::join_all` across N corpora deferred to F6.3-b/c after auditing the registry's `ensure_present` for parallel-safety. Cross-cloud-corpora calls hit Postgres + blob lazy-restore; the cache lock contention pattern needs validation before going parallel.
    - [x] **Honest scope choice — content_id namespace collisions**. Two corpora can produce identical `content_id` strings (e.g. both contain `docs/index.md#root`). The same `exclude_ids` set is applied across all corpora; the session machinery sees same-content-id hits as same delivery. Agents can disambiguate via the new `source_corpus` field, but the dedupe collision is documented. The fix lands when session tracking learns to namespace by `(corpus_id, content_id)`.
    - **Validation:** cargo workspace test green (0 failed); clippy `--pedantic -D warnings` clean; ministr-app `tsc --noEmit` + `vite build` clean. Live: a Pro user calls `ministr_survey` with `{"query": "useEffect", "corpus_ids": ["my-app", "atlas/react"]}` → response carries top-k hits sorted by score across both corpora, each tagged with `source_corpus`. Deferred to next deploy.
  - [x] **F6.3-b `corpus_boost` ranking parameter** *(2026-05-21)*
    - [x] New `corpus_boost: Option<HashMap<String, f32>>` parameter on `SurveyParams` — per-corpus score multipliers keyed by `corpus_id`. Absent corpora default to 1.0 (unboosted); only consulted when `corpus_ids` is set.
    - [x] New `sanitise_boost(raw: f32) -> f32` helper + `MAX_CORPUS_BOOST = 10.0` const in `ministr-mcp/src/server/mod.rs`. Clamps `[0.0, 10.0]`; falls back to 1.0 on NaN/±∞ so a malformed entry can't silently zero a corpus.
    - [x] `cross_corpus_survey` orchestrator takes `corpus_boost: Option<&HashMap<...>>` and forwards to the pure `merge_cross_corpus_results` helper, which applies `score *= sanitise_boost(boost)` in-place before sort + truncate. The boosted score REPLACES the raw score in the returned struct — agents read the effective ranking directly.
    - [x] 9 new unit tests: above-1 floats a corpus above higher raw scores, 0.0 suppresses, absent corpus defaults to 1.0, negative clamps to 0, runaway clamps to ceiling, NaN safe-fallback, ±INF safe-fallback, None-map regression-equal to F6.3-a, plus a 7-cell `sanitise_boost` matrix.
    - **Validation:** cargo workspace test green (0 failed); clippy `--pedantic -D warnings` clean; ministr-app `tsc --noEmit` + `vite build` clean. Live: `{"query":"useEffect","corpus_ids":["my-app","atlas/react"],"corpus_boost":{"my-app":2.0}}` → my-app's hits score-doubled before merge → own repo's `useEffect` outranks React's. Deferred to next deploy.
  - **Validation:** Pro user creates `["my-app", "atlas/react", "atlas/postgres"]` survey → result set includes hits from all three, with `source_corpus` discriminator on every hit; ranking is sane (own repo's `useEffect` should beat React's `useEffect` for the user's own files).

- [ ] **F6.4 MCP federation (align with MCP-AX draft)** *(depends on F6.3)*
  > NOTE (refresh 2026-05-23): MCP-AX is still at `draft-abbott-mcp-ax-00` (May 4 2026) with no revisions. No known implementations. Watch but don't implement until at least `-01`. **Meanwhile, MCP 2026-07-28 RC shipped 3 days ago with a stateless protocol core** — F7 below handles that migration, which is more urgent than MCP-AX federation.
  - [ ] Implement the IETF **MCP-AX draft** (`draft-abbott-mcp-ax-00`, published 4 May 2026) — hierarchical aggregation protocol that lets one MCP URL aggregate many corpora into a single tool surface for the agent. Track the draft; align as it stabilises.
  - [ ] Per-tenant federation endpoint at `mcp.ministr.ai/mcp/federated` — one URL, all of (own corpora ∪ Atlas reads ∪ org corpora) reachable through a single namespaced tool surface.
  - [ ] Fallback to ad-hoc namespaced tool prefix (`survey_<corpus_slug>`) if MCP-AX doesn't stabilise on a timeline we can wait for.
  - **Validation:** an agent configures one URL → sees `tools/list` returning a unified tool surface namespaced per corpus → calls resolve to the right backing corpus; matches MCP-AX hierarchical conformance once the draft is final.

### F7 — MCP 2026-07-28 spec migration *(urgent — RC published 2026-07-25, blocks next rmcp update)*

> **Discovered 2026-05-23 via /roadmap-refresh.** The MCP specification 2026-07-28 release candidate makes the protocol **stateless at the core layer**: no `initialize` handshake, no `Mcp-Session-Id` header, no resumable streams. Extensions framework replaces the old capability-negotiation dance. Two official extensions ship: **MCP Apps** (server-initiated UI) and **enhanced OAuth** (hardened auth flow). Sources: [blog.modelcontextprotocol.io](https://blog.modelcontextprotocol.io/posts/2026-07-28-release-candidate/), [mcp.directory analysis](https://mcp.directory/blog/mcp-2026-07-28-release-candidate), [PipeLab security analysis](https://pipelab.org/blog/what-stateless-mcp-means-for-agent-runtime-security/).
>
> **Impact on ministr:** The F-Test-3b-fix-1 tenant-capture-on-`initialize` pattern (our `tenant_id_hint` populated from `context.extensions` during `ServerHandler::initialize`) breaks when clients stop sending `initialize`. The fork-per-connection model (`server_factory` calling `fork_for_new_session`) needs rethinking. rmcp will update to the new spec; our pinned version will hold temporarily but we need to migrate before the ecosystem moves.

- [ ] **F7.1 Audit current MCP surface against 2026-07-28 RC** — read the RC spec; enumerate every `initialize`-dependent code path in `ministr-mcp`; produce a migration plan. No code changes.
- [ ] **F7.2 Stateless tenant resolution** — replace the `initialize`-captured `tenant_id_hint` with a per-request resolution path that works without `initialize`. The OAuth bearer token already carries the tenant; the question is how rmcp exposes it in the stateless world.
- [ ] **F7.3 Session continuity without `Mcp-Session-Id`** — the spec removes the session header. ministr's session machinery (F6.1) uses it for session binding. Evaluate: client-provided session ID in tool params vs. server-side session inference from the bearer token.
- [ ] **F7.4 Extensions framework adoption** — register ministr's capabilities as MCP extensions rather than the old `initialize`-negotiated features. Evaluate whether MCP Apps (server-initiated UI) is relevant for the bridge visualizer or session inspector.
- [ ] **F7.5 OAuth hardening alignment** — the RC hardens the OAuth flow. Audit our existing OAuth 2.1 + DCR + PKCE implementation against the new spec requirements.
- [ ] **F7.6 rmcp version bump** — update to the rmcp release that targets 2026-07-28. This is the integration chunk; everything above informs it.
- **Validation:** `just e2e-cloud-local` passes with the updated rmcp; multi-tenant MCP tool calls work without `initialize`; existing Tauri + CLI clients continue to function.

### F-Test — Local cloud e2e testing infrastructure *(2026-05-21, new track)*

> Cross-cutting: builds the local equivalent of `azure-smoke` so multi-tenant cloud correctness, ACL semantics, API-key authn parity, session-tenant-scoping, webhook fan-out, and billing webhooks are all exercisable on a laptop without an Azure deploy. Today's `scripts/demo-local.sh` covers ONE tenant's happy path; the F-items above ship with Postgres-integration tests gated on `MINISTR_TEST_PG_URL` and unit coverage, but no e2e proof that ties them together end-to-end. F-Test fills that gap. Each chunk extends the harness in place — there's only one command to remember (`just e2e-cloud-local`) regardless of which scenario it ends up covering. Mirrors the `azure-smoke` extension policy from `justfile`.

- [x] **F-Test-1 Multi-tenant harness + first scenarios** *(2026-05-21)*
  - [x] `scripts/e2e-cloud-local.sh` lands — spawns Postgres + cloud serve, mints TWO bearer tokens via the new `ministr cloud mint-test-bearer` subcommand, runs 14 PASS/FAIL assertions, tears down on exit. KEEP=1 leaves the stack running; PORT=... overrides default 8088. Persistent `/tmp/ministr-e2e-data` keeps the embedding-model cache across runs (Candle's HF download is flaky and re-downloading on every run wastes a cache miss).
  - [x] `just e2e-cloud-local` recipe wired in `justfile`. CI-friendly exit code (non-zero on any FAIL).
  - [x] `ministr cloud mint-test-bearer --github-id N --email E` CLI subcommand lands — upserts a `users` row via the same `upsert_github_user` path the GitHub callback uses, then mints a bearer via `OAuthStore::issue_bearer_token` bound to the UUID subject. Required because the OAuth self-issuer's DCR mints non-UUID `client_id`s which break the cloud schema's UUID-typed tenant lattice (discovered finding — see below).
  - **14 assertions PASS** today: `/healthz` alive + status; `/atlas/manifest.json` reachable + count==50; tenant A POST /corpora + corpus_id captured; tenant A GET /corpora returns 200; **tenant isolation** (tenant B does NOT see A's corpus); tenant A POST /orgs (201) + role==owner; tenant B GET /orgs returns 200; **org isolation** (tenant B does NOT see A's org); tenant A POST /api_keys (201) + mst_pk_ prefix.
  - **2 remaining FAILs** are real cloud bugs surfaced by the harness, captured below as F-Test-1-discovered findings. The harness exits with FAIL_COUNT so CI can gate, but the F-Test track's first chunk's value is in *building the scaffold + finding the bugs* — the fixes layer into subsequent chunks.
  - **Honest scope choice — no GitHub OAuth callback exercise**. Real-callback flows need a registered OAuth App + browser handshake; F-Test-1 stays inside the self-issuer surface (which Tenant resolution treats identically once the bearer lands).
  - **Honest scope choice — no Stripe exercise**. Requires `stripe-cli` forwarding + a registered product. Deferred to F-Test-4.
  - **Validation:** cargo workspace test 0 failed; cargo clippy `--pedantic -D warnings` clean. Live: `just e2e-cloud-local` exits non-zero today because 2 assertions FAIL — the cloud bugs surfaced (visibility filter + API-key resolver) are real and tracked as discovered findings below.

##### F-Test-1 discovered findings (2026-05-21)

These are real cloud bugs the harness surfaced. Each is a candidate follow-up chunk:

- **DCR client_id vs UUID schema mismatch.** The OAuth self-issuer's DCR mints 22-char base64url `client_id`s like `uTdHkFkzSxwo1_JfflD0Ng`, but the cloud schema's `users.id` / `org_members.user_id` / visibility-filter `$1::uuid` cast all assume UUID-shaped tenant subjects produced by the GitHub callback. Three downstream failures cascade from this one mismatch — tenant_id stamping silently NULLs, the visibility filter rejects all rows, and orgs creation 500s. **Workaround**: the new `ministr cloud mint-test-bearer` subcommand uses the same `upsert_github_user` path as the GitHub callback so the resulting bearer has a UUID-shaped subject. **Fix candidate**: make the DCR handler mint UUID-shaped client_ids when cloud-mode is detected, OR disable the DCR path when `MINISTR_PG_URL` is set.
- [x] **tokio-postgres `$X::uuid` parameter-inference bug.** *(fixed inline)* — When SQL has `WHERE col = $1::uuid` or `VALUES ($1::uuid, ...)`, PG infers `$1` as UUID directly (not TEXT), and tokio-postgres rejects `&String` → UUID binds at the Prepare phase with "error serializing parameter 0". Surfaced by both orgs creation (500) and visibility-filter query (silent empty). Fix: prepend `::text` to force TEXT inference first, then the trailing `::uuid` server-side cast accepts the TEXT value. Sweep of 19 cloud SQL files (59 occurrences) lands in this chunk. The pattern was already in use in `audit.rs` (`CASE WHEN $1::text IS NULL THEN NULL ELSE $1::uuid END`) — the rest of the codebase didn't follow it, presumably because the gated `MINISTR_TEST_PG_URL` integration tests had never been successfully run (Rustls CryptoProvider panic blocks them from the standard `cargo test` path).
- [x] **Visibility filter `cloud_corpora.tenant_id` is TEXT, not UUID** *(fixed inline in F-Test-1-followup)*. The F-Test-1 sweep applied `$X::uuid → $X::text::uuid` uniformly, but migration 0003 declared `cloud_corpora.tenant_id TEXT` (the outlier among tenant_id columns — `usage_events`, `usage_rollups`, `agent_sessions`, `session_drops` are all UUID). For the TEXT column, the cast became `tenant_id (TEXT) = $1::text::uuid (UUID)` which PG rejected with SQLSTATE E42883 "operator does not exist: text = uuid". Diagnosed by extending `map_err` in tenant_filter.rs to surface the Debug-form of tokio-postgres errors (the bare Display only said "db error"). Fix: two-line revert — `tenant_filter::visible_corpus_ids` first arm and `orgs::corpus_acl::transfer_corpus_to_org` UPDATE both back to bare `$1`.
- [x] **API-key bearer authn returns 401 — `validate_scope_middleware` pre-checks `validate_token` (OAuth-only) BEFORE the api-key fall-through.** *(fixed inline in F-Test-1-followup)* The middleware short-circuits with 401 for `mst_pk_…` tokens before ever reaching `resolve_tenant_with_scope`'s api-key path. Predates F3.4a and was never updated when the resolver landed. Fix: replace the pre-check with `resolve_tenant` (which walks both OAuth + api-key paths), then keep the `resolve_tenant_with_scope` call for the 401-vs-403 disambiguation. One-file change in `ministr-mcp/src/auth/middleware.rs`. Surfaced by F-Test-1's "API key bearer can GET /corpora" assertion (was returning 401, now returns 200).
- [x] **Cloud-mode `list_corpora` doesn't surface pending registrations** *(2026-05-21, closed)*. Originally documented in F-Test-1-followup; deferred twice as "architectural"; closed in F-Test-pending-merge by a smaller seam than the original `register_pending` proposal. Approach taken: extended `ministr_api::TenantCorpusVisibility` with a `pending_corpora_for_tenant` method (default impl returns empty for self-hosted) + `CorpusRegistrationView` minimal struct; `PostgresTenantCorpusFilter` queries `cloud_corpora WHERE tenant_id = $1` (TEXT column — the F-Test-1-followup lesson held). The daemon's `list_corpora` handler now unions the in-memory CorpusInfo list with synthesised CorpusInfo entries for any direct-ownership cloud_corpora rows not yet in-memory. Synthesis uses `IndexingStatus::Idle` + zero counts (the in-memory entry, when it lands later, has the live progress + real counts — pre-empts the synthesised version because `known: HashSet<id>` skip-list keeps duplicates out). Harness's previously-NOTE'd "tenant A sees own corpus" assertion converted to a real PASS (uses `.id` not `.corpus_id` — the existing `.corpus_id` filter was a latent bug that silently always returned 0 because CorpusInfo's serde field is `id`).

###### F-Test-1-followup *(2026-05-21, complete)* — harness fully green at 19 PASS, 0 FAIL

- [x] `tenant_filter::visible_corpus_ids` SQL: TEXT-column `cloud_corpora.tenant_id` reverts to bare `$1`; UUID-column `org_members.user_id` keeps `$1::text::uuid` (landed).
- [x] `orgs::corpus_acl::transfer_corpus_to_org` SQL: TEXT-column assignment reverts to bare `$1` (landed).
- [x] `auth::middleware::validate_scope_middleware`: replace `validate_token` pre-check with `resolve_tenant` so API-key bearers reach the resolver (landed). Same fix posture as the no-scope `validate_token_middleware` which was already correct.
- [x] `auth::store::resolve_api_key`: add `tracing::debug!` to distinguish "resolver not installed" / "token not in api_keys" / "scope missing" paths — three previously-silent failure modes (landed). Surfaced by F-Test-1-followup's RUST_LOG-driven diagnostic.
- [x] `tenant_filter::map_err`: surface the Debug form of tokio-postgres errors alongside Display so future "db error" failures don't require manual instrumentation (landed).
- [x] Harness `scripts/e2e-cloud-local.sh` adds `psql_user_id` + `psql_count` helpers; the "tenant A sees own corpus" assertion converted to a data-layer ownership check via psql (works around the cloud-registry gap above) (landed).
- **Validation:** `just e2e-cloud-local` exits 0 with 19 PASS, 0 FAIL. cargo workspace test 0 failed. cargo clippy `--workspace --all-targets -- -D warnings -W clippy::pedantic` clean.

- [x] **F-Test-2 Webhook fan-out e2e** *(2026-05-21, complete)*
  - [x] `scripts/e2e-webhook-receiver.py` — stdlib `http.server` receiver, 60 LoC. Listens on `RECEIVER_PORT` (default 8089), appends every POST (path + lowercased headers + body) to a JSONL record file, 200 OKs the cloud's dispatcher so retry-storms don't fire (landed).
  - [x] `scripts/e2e-cloud-local.sh` extension: spawns the receiver after serve is up; trap-driven cleanup kills it on EXIT/INT/TERM; new `python3` precondition check in the early `for cmd` loop (landed).
  - [x] Five new assertions in the harness:
    1. `POST /api/v1/orgs/{org_id}/webhooks` returns 201 with secret.
    2. The one-time HMAC secret is present in the response.
    3. `POST /api/v1/orgs/{org_id}/invites` returns 201 (audit event fires).
    4. Receiver records an `invite.created` delivery within 6s (poll loop using `jq fromjson` on `.body` — the JSONL `.body` is a JSON-encoded string of the actual payload).
    5. HMAC-SHA256(secret, ts + "." + body) computed by `openssl dgst -sha256 -hmac` matches the `X-Ministr-Signature` header byte-for-byte.
  - **Validation:** `just e2e-cloud-local` exits 0 with 24 assertions green. The fan-out path triggered TWO deliveries (`org.created` from F3.7a's org-create hook + `invite.created` from F3.7a's invite-create hook) — both arrive within 6s; the harness asserts on `invite.created` because the org-create one races with the webhook-subscription-create call.
  - **Honest finding:** the `event_filter:"*"` value admits all events; tightening to `event_filter:"invite.created"` would isolate the assertion path. For F-Test-2 v0, the wildcard is fine — the jq+fromjson polling already selects only invite.created.

- [x] **F-Test-3 Session bundle round-trip e2e** *(2026-05-21, complete — a + b both landed; parent flag was stale)*
  - [x] **F-Test-3a Session-list tenant isolation + cross-tenant 404** *(2026-05-21)* — closes the F-Test-1-pinned count=1 NOTE.
    - [x] Harness asserts tenant A /sessions returns empty (no leaked bootstrap session), tenant B /sessions returns empty (isolation), both tenants' `POST /api/v1/sessions/{synthetic-uuid}/export` return 404 (F6.2-e-followup-ii existence-resistance).
    - [x] **Real cloud bug fixed:** `scope_tenant` middleware was missing from `session_export_router`. `handle_list` reads `tenant_scope::current()` to filter unstamped/legacy entries; without the layer the task-local was always None and `admit_session_for_scope` admitted every entry. Both tenants saw the bootstrap `ministr-<hash>` session (generated by `infra.rs::generate_session_id` from config `corpus_paths`). Fix: layer added to session_export_router at construction. Harness's prior `count=1 NOTE` upgraded to a PASS.
    - **Validation:** `just e2e-cloud-local` 34 PASS, 0 FAIL. cargo workspace test 0 failed. cargo clippy `--pedantic` clean.
  - [x] **F-Test-3b Full session bundle round-trip via MCP `/mcp` call** *(landed 2026-05-21; harness 39 PASS, 0 FAIL)*
    - [x] Drive an MCP Streamable HTTP JSON-RPC handshake from bash (`initialize` → extract `Mcp-Session-Id` header → `notifications/initialized` → `tools/call ministr_survey`) so `ensure_session_mut` stamps a real tenant-scoped session in the in-memory registry. Implemented as `mcp_initialize_and_call` helper in scripts/e2e-cloud-local.sh.
    - [x] Assert the session shows up in `GET /api/v1/sessions` for tenant A with poll loop (up to 30s — accounts for survey latency during concurrent indexing). Tenant B's GET stays empty (isolation).
    - [x] `POST /api/v1/sessions/{real-id}/export` for tenant A → 200 + tar bytes; `tar -tf` confirms `manifest.json` entry (F6.2-a wire shape).
    - [x] Tenant B POST `.../export` of tenant A's real session id → 404 (existence-resistant; tighter variant of the synthetic-id check from F-Test-3a).
    - [x] **Real harness bug discovered + fixed:** bash's `${3:-{}}` parameter-expansion default parses as `${3:-{}` + literal `}`, appending an extra `}` to whatever value `$3` is. The args_json gained a trailing `}`, the JSON body became invalid, and rmcp returned 415 Unsupported Media Type (which masquerades as "did not arrive"). Fix: explicit `if [[ -z "${3:-}" ]]` branch. Worth remembering: any `${X:-{...}}` pattern in bash is broken; nested closing braces inside the default aren't tracked by the parser.
    - **Validation:** `just e2e-cloud-local` 39 PASS, 0 FAIL. cargo workspace test 0 failed. cargo clippy `--pedantic` clean.

##### F-Test-3b-fix-2 (2026-05-21, complete) — sweep all tenant_scope::current() sites in tool handlers to use the hint-fallback helper

F-Test-3b-fix-1 only patched `ensure_session_mut`'s tenant_id stamping path. The other 13 `crate::tenant_scope::current()` call sites scattered across `ministr-mcp/src/server/mod.rs` tool handlers were still silently getting `None` on the cloud `/mcp` dispatch path — affecting default-corpus selection (F2.x-c), cross-corpus survey tenant lookups (F6.3-a), per-tenant audit emission, ministr_read/extract/related/symbols/etc.

- **Added helper**: `MinistrServer::current_tenant_subject() -> Option<String>` in `builders.rs`. Walks `tenant_scope::current()` → `self.tenant_id_hint`. Replaces the same inline fallback chain that was in `session.rs::ensure_session_mut` (which now delegates to the helper too).
- **Swept 13 call sites** in `mod.rs` via `Edit replace_all`: every `let tenant_subject = crate::tenant_scope::current();` became `let tenant_subject = self.current_tenant_subject();`. All sites consume the result the same way (`.as_deref()` or `.clone()` on Option<String>) so no further callsite adjustments were needed.
- **Result**: 0 remaining `tenant_scope::current()` calls in mod.rs (was 13). On the cloud /mcp path, all 13 handlers now correctly recover the calling tenant subject via the hint that initialize captured from `context.extensions`. Self-hosted / stdio / in-process tests still see `None` (no scope mounted, no hint captured) — pre-fix-1 behavior preserved.
- **Files touched**: `ministr-mcp/src/server/builders.rs` (helper + doc), `ministr-mcp/src/server/mod.rs` (13 sweep), `ministr-mcp/src/server/session.rs` (ensure_session_mut delegates to helper).
- **Validation**: `just e2e-cloud-local` 39 PASS, 0 FAIL (unchanged — the harness doesn't yet exercise the other 13 tool handlers, so this is "future-proofing" verification: the path was provably broken before; it's now provably fixed via the same mechanism F-Test-3b proved end-to-end). cargo workspace test 0 failed. cargo clippy `--pedantic` clean.

##### F-Test-3b-fix-1 (2026-05-21, complete) — capture-on-initialize via context.extensions

The F-Test-3b-blocker hypothesis (rmcp's dispatcher spawns the tool-handler on a task that doesn't inherit tokio task-locals) was confirmed AND a path through it was found in one chunk:

- **Probe**: a temporary `tracing::info!` in `MinistrServer::initialize` showed `tenant_scope::current()` returns `None` even inside `initialize` (not just `tools/call`) — so the task-local is lost before any ServerHandler method runs. BUT `context.extensions.get::<axum::http::request::Parts>()` returned `Some(parts)`, and `parts.extensions.get::<Tenant>()` returned the calling tenant. rmcp 0.14's `streamable_http_server/tower.rs:326` injects the axum request's `Parts` (with full `extensions`) into rmcp's `RequestContext::extensions` — survives the spawn boundary.
- **Fix shipped**: new `tenant_id_hint: Arc<std::sync::Mutex<Option<String>>>` on `MinistrServer`; `initialize` captures via the `context.extensions → Parts → Tenant` chain and stores; `ensure_session_mut` falls back to the hint when `tenant_scope::current()` is None. Mirrors the existing `client_name_hint` and `parent_session_id_hint` patterns. Three construction sites in `builders.rs` updated + `fork_for_new_session` resets the hint per-fork (so a future fork-per-connection fix doesn't carry a stale tenant id forward).
- **Live verification**: manual MCP handshake + `tools/call ministr_survey` as tenant A; `GET /api/v1/sessions` for tenant A now returns the stamped session (`{"session_id":"ministr-<hash>", "budget_used":0, …}`); tenant B's GET returns `[]`.
- **Honest scope choice — shared-bootstrap remains**: `server_factory` still uses `server.clone()` rather than `server.fork_for_new_session()`. Switching to fork-per-connection was attempted in this chunk and broke `tools/call` (fresh-UUID `active_session_id` has no corpus-resolution path and the survey hung). So all `/mcp` connections currently share the same bootstrap `active_session_id` → SessionEntry; the first tenant to make a call stamps it, subsequent tenants' calls observe `tenant_id.is_some()` and skip stamping. This means tenant B's tool-call activity gets filed under tenant A's SessionEntry — a real cross-tenant gap WORTH ITS OWN CHUNK (see F-Test-3b-fix-1-shared-bootstrap below). The capture-on-initialize fix is necessary but not sufficient for full multi-tenant /mcp correctness.
- **Files touched**: `ministr-mcp/src/server/mod.rs` (struct field + initialize), `ministr-mcp/src/server/session.rs` (ensure_session_mut fallback chain), `ministr-mcp/src/server/builders.rs` (3 construction sites + fork_for_new_session reset).
- **Validation**: cargo workspace test 0 failed. cargo clippy `--pedantic` clean. `just e2e-cloud-local`: 34 PASS, 0 FAIL (harness doesn't yet exercise MCP; that's F-Test-3b proper).

##### F-Test-3b-fix-1-shared-bootstrap (2026-05-21, complete) — fork-per-connection + panic-site fixes

Closed by switching `server_factory` to `server.fork_for_new_session()` after first making the 5 `get_session(...).expect("active session exists")` panic sites resilient via `ensure_session_mut`.

**The real cause of the prior "hung tool call":** root-causing the F-Test-3b-fix-1 hung-survey hypothesis turned out to be wrong. The hang wasn't about corpus resolution; it was about a silent tokio task panic. Five handler/prompt sites assumed the bootstrap session was pre-created and called `.expect("active session exists")`. With the fork giving each /mcp connection a fresh uuid_v4 active_session_id, the session didn't exist on first read. The panic crashed the rmcp handler task silently; rmcp's SSE stream stayed open with no data flowing; curl hit `--max-time` and reported a timeout that LOOKED like a hang. The original F-Test-3b-fix-1 close report misattributed this to corpus resolution.

**Phase A (panic-site fixes)**: 5 sites swept to use `ensure_session_mut` instead of `get_session(...).expect(...)`:
- `ministr-mcp/src/server/mod.rs:997` (ministr_survey exclude_ids read)
- `ministr-mcp/src/server/mod.rs:1668` (elicitation eviction)
- `ministr-mcp/src/server/mod.rs:2778` (session-summary prompt)
- `ministr-mcp/src/server/mod.rs:2847` (what-next prompt)
- `ministr-mcp/src/server/resources.rs:168` (read_status_resource — also needed a borrow-checker shape change: snapshot entry's fields into owned values BEFORE accessing `reg.session_count()/session_ids()` so the &mut reg borrow ends in time)

**Phase B (server_factory)**: `move || Ok(server.clone())` → `move || Ok(server.fork_for_new_session())` in `ministr-cli/src/commands.rs`. The fork's existing `tenant_id_hint` reset (landed in F-Test-3b-fix-1) means tenant A's captured subject doesn't carry over to tenant B's connection.

**Harness assertions (3 new, 39 → 42 PASS)**:
- tenant B drives MCP call → /sessions count >= 1 (fork gives B its own SessionEntry)
- tenant B's session_id != tenant A's (no shared-bootstrap contamination)
- tenant A's /sessions still returns only A's session after B's call (no shared shadow mutation)

**Validation**: harness 42 PASS, 0 FAIL. cargo workspace test 0 failed. cargo clippy `--pedantic` clean. F6.2 export tar for tenant A now genuinely cannot contain tenant B's deliveries (different SessionEntry).

##### F-Test-3b-blocker (2026-05-21, resolved by F-Test-3b-fix-1) — rmcp task-local-loss across the cloud /mcp dispatch boundary

Investigating F-Test-3b's prerequisite "MCP tool call populates a tenant-scoped session" surfaced a real architectural bug that's bigger than one /roadmap chunk.

- **Symptom**: tenant A drives `POST /mcp` initialize + `tools/call ministr_survey`, then `GET /api/v1/sessions` returns `[]` (empty). Expected: count=1 with the rmcp-assigned session id and `tenant_id == tenant_A_uuid`.
- **Confirmed via temporary debug log in `ensure_session_mut`**: `tenant_scope::current()` returns `None` during the tool-call handler. Both observed `session_id` values are the bootstrap `ministr-<hash>` (from `infra.rs::generate_session_id`), not the rmcp-forked id — suggesting `fork_for_new_session` doesn't run on the cloud HTTP path either, OR the per-request fork loses the task-local during construction.
- **Root cause hypothesis**: `cmd_serve_http` mounts `scope_tenant` middleware as a layer over rmcp's `StreamableHttpService` (line ~433). The middleware DOES set the task-local on the outer request future, but rmcp's internal dispatcher spawns the tool-handler on a separate tokio task that doesn't inherit tokio task-locals across `tokio::spawn`. So every `tenant_scope::current()` call inside tool handlers — there are 12+ in `ministr-mcp/src/server/mod.rs` — silently returns `None`.
- **Impact (broader than just session stamping)**: F2.x-c default-corpus selection (`default_corpus_for_tenant(tenant_subject)` called with `None` → falls back to empty default service); F6.3-a cross-corpus survey tenant lookups; F6.2-e session bundle export tenant filtering; per-tenant audit emissions from tool handlers. Multi-tenant correctness on the /mcp path is silently broken.
- **Why F-Test-1/2/5/3a didn't catch it**: those tests exercise `/api/v1/*` daemon/orgs/api_keys/webhooks routes, which run the handler IN-PROCESS in the same axum task that set the scope_tenant task-local. The `/mcp` path is the only one that dispatches through rmcp, which is where the boundary is crossed.
- **Fix candidates** (none trivial, all warrant their own chunk):
  1. **Capture tenant on initialize, store on `MinistrServer`** — mirror the `client_name` capture pattern: read `tenant_scope::current()` in the rmcp `initialize` handler, store it on the per-request server, have `ensure_session_mut` read from the server instead of the task-local. Risk: initialize might also run in the post-spawn task (need to verify).
  2. **Custom rmcp service wrapper** — wrap `StreamableHttpService` with a per-request fork that re-enters the task-local scope before invoking the inner service. Higher invasiveness.
  3. **Switch from task-local to request-extension** — store the Tenant in axum request extensions all the way down and have tool handlers read from `RequestContext<RoleServer>::extensions` (if rmcp 1.5 supports). Most idiomatic but depends on rmcp surface.
  4. **Pin rmcp version + patch upstream** — submit a PR to rmcp to propagate task-locals across the dispatcher boundary, or expose a hook for callers to inject context.
- **Workaround in the meantime**: tool handlers that genuinely need the tenant subject can read it from `MinistrServer.tenant_id` (after fix candidate #1 lands). Until that lands, the multi-tenant filtering on /mcp falls through to the permissive default for every cloud caller.
- **Documented inline** at `ministr-mcp/src/server/session.rs::ensure_session_mut` so future maintainers see why the stamp is silently dropping. F-Test-3b stays blocked until one of the fix candidates lands.

- [x] **F-Test-4 Stripe webhook flip e2e** *(2026-05-22, complete — 5 new assertions, harness 42 → 47 PASS)*
  - [x] **Scope simplification vs original spec:** the chunk was originally written as "requires stripe-cli + stripe listen forwarding". After implementing, that turned out to be unnecessary — the cloud's webhook handler at POST /webhooks/stripe is purely a signature-verifier + Postgres-updater that doesn't care whether the event came from Stripe's edge or directly from curl. The harness constructs fixture event JSON, signs it with openssl HMAC-SHA256 mirroring Stripe's v1 scheme, and POSTs directly. Zero Stripe API contact, zero `stripe login` required, zero monetary risk per user's explicit constraint.
  - [x] Set `MINISTR_STRIPE_WEBHOOK_SECRET=whsec_e2e_test_only_localhost_no_money` in the harness's serve env (mounts the route).
  - [x] `stripe_sign_header` bash helper — `t=<ts>,v1=<HMAC_SHA256(secret, ts+"."+body)>`. Mirrors the existing X-Ministr-Signature helper pattern (openssl dgst -sha256 -hmac).
  - [x] UPDATE tenant A's user row pre-flip: set `stripe_customer_id = 'cus_e2e_test_<runid>'` + reset `plan_id = 'free'` (F-Test-5 had pre-emptively upgraded to pro; a stuck-at-pro test wouldn't prove the upgrade path).
  - [x] customer.subscription.updated with `lookup_key=pro` → POST signs → 200 → poll users.plan_id flips from free to pro within 5s.
  - [x] customer.subscription.deleted → POST → 200 → poll plan_id falls from pro to free within 5s.
  - [x] Attacker-signed body (wrong secret, same payload) → POST → 400 (signature rejected — covers the security boundary).
  - **Validation:** `just e2e-cloud-local` 47 PASS, 0 FAIL. cargo workspace test 0 failed. cargo clippy `--pedantic` clean. End-to-end Stripe webhook semantics + HMAC verification validated locally with no external service contact.
  - **stripe-cli IS installed locally** (brew, one-time) — preserved for future operator-mode tests that may want `stripe listen` forwarding, but the unit / e2e tests don't need it. The original "operator-only" framing dissolves in favour of a CI-friendly pure-local test.

- [x] **F-Test-5 Quota / paywall enforcement e2e** *(2026-05-21, complete)*
  - [x] New `PostgresCorporaProbe` in `ministr-cloud/src/quota/probe.rs`: `SELECT count(*) FROM cloud_corpora WHERE tenant_id = $1` (TEXT column, no cast — same lesson as F-Test-1-followup). Tenant-scoped. Exported through `ministr_cloud::PostgresCorporaProbe`.
  - [x] `cmd_serve_http` quota wiring: when `cloud_pool` is Some, wires `PostgresCorporaProbe` as the `UsageProbe`; self-hosted serve keeps `RegistryProbe`. Boots log `PostgresCorporaProbe wired — quota counts cloud_corpora per-tenant` at info.
  - [x] Harness adds 4 assertions: tenant A registers 9 more corpora at Pro cap (loop with unique sample dirs); 11th attempt returns HTTP 402; paywall `reason == "corpus_quota_exceeded"`; `upgrade_url == "https://ministr.ai/billing/upgrade?from=pro"` (byte-for-byte spec match).
  - **Validation:** `just e2e-cloud-local` exits 0 with 28 assertions green; cargo workspace test 0 failed; cargo clippy `--pedantic -D warnings` clean.
  - **Honest finding fixed by this chunk:** the F2.3 `RegistryProbe` counts `registry.list()` length pod-wide (admitted in the code's doc comment: "counts every corpus on the pod, regardless of tenant_id"). On cloud mode that count was almost always 0 (in-memory registry stays empty until indexing) AND not per-tenant — so a Pro tenant could register unlimited corpora without ever hitting the 10-cap. `PostgresCorporaProbe` fixes both: cloud_corpora is the source of truth, and the WHERE tenant_id = $1 filter is per-tenant. The pre-existing `RegistryProbe` still works correctly on self-hosted serve where there's effectively one tenant.

#### F-Test done criterion

`just e2e-cloud-local` covers all five chunks and exits 0 on a clean checkout against a fresh `dev-cloud-up` Postgres. CI runs it on every push and turns red on any FAIL; engineering's "should I ship this PR?" answer becomes a single command rather than a multi-step DEMO.md walkthrough.

### G — Governance (interleaved gates)

- [ ] **G.1 Atlas legal review** *(gates F4.1 public launch beyond F2.6's pilot 50)*
  - [ ] Engage IP counsel; deliverable is a written opinion documenting:
    - Indexing + embedding generation under permissive licenses (MIT/Apache/BSD/MPL/ISC) is safe for redistribution as a service (cite the 2025 US fair-use ruling on training).
    - Copyleft (GPL/AGPL/LGPL) — opinion on whether retrieval indexes are derivative works; if not, include; if yes, exclude until 4.1 supports filtered scrub.
    - Opt-out mechanism (`ai.robots.txt`-style + manifest submission) is sufficient legally and reputationally.
  - [ ] Conclusion documented at `LEGAL-ATLAS.md` (repo root); auditable by buyers.

- [ ] **G.2 Security audit** *(gates F5 Enterprise sales)*
  - [ ] Third-party pen test of the cloud surface — OAuth flow, tenant isolation, SAML/OIDC handshakes, on-prem image escape resistance.
  - [ ] Findings remediated before any Enterprise contract signs. Customer-facing summary published.

- [ ] **G.3 SOC2 Type 1** *(needed for most Enterprise procurement; runs during F5)*
  - [ ] Adopt Drata or Vanta as the GRC platform (~$5–10K/yr); first Type 1 audit follows in ~14–22 weeks; ~$15–35K all-in for the first cycle.
  - [ ] Trust Center at `trust.ministr.ai` publishes the report (under NDA) plus active sub-processor list, security policies, and uptime stats.
  - [ ] Type 2 follows naturally once we have 6+ months of operating evidence — sequenced AFTER F5 lands.

## 5. Dependency DAG

```
                    F0 — license flip (MIT)  [done]
                                │
                                ▼
                            ┌── F1.1 ──┐  [done]
                            │           │
                            ▼           ▼
                          F1.2 ─────► F1.4 ─────► F1.5
                            │
                            ├── F1.3 ──────┐
                            │               ▼
                            │             F2.1
                            │               │
                            └────► F2 (.2 .3 .4 .5 .6 .7) ◄── revenue moment #1
                                            │
                            G.1 legal       │
                            review  ◄──── gate F4
                                            │
                                ┌───────────┴───────────┐
                                ▼                       ▼
                          F3 (.1–.7)               F4 (.1–.4)
                          (revenue #2)             (the moat scaled)
                                │                       │
                                └───────────┬───────────┘
                                            ▼
                            G.2 security audit ◄── gate F5
                                            │
                                            ▼
                                       F5 (.1–.6) ◄── revenue moment #3
                                            │
                            G.3 SOC2 Type 1  │
                            (concurrent) ────┤
                                            │
                                       Trust Center

         F6 (.1–.4 — Stickiness)  ────────  ships continuously across F1–F5
```

**Critical-path observations:**
- **F0 is a paper change** but it gates the entire open-core narrative — do it first.
- **F1.2 is the joint-bottleneck:** persistence + tenancy + bridge between MCP and daemon registry — three problems solved as one project (intentional).
- **F3 ∥ F4** is the genuine parallelism — once F2 ships, the team-launch track and the Atlas-scale track don't depend on each other.
- **F6 is decoupled by design** — Stickiness items absorb into the most relevant adjacent F-item rather than waiting for their own dedicated phase. F6.1 lands during F1.2 (durable session state). F6.2 lands during F2.6 (session export plumbing). F6.3 lands during F2.6 (cross-corpus is just multi-Atlas survey). F6.4 lands when MCP-AX stabilises.
- **G.1 must complete before F4.1 (5K expansion);** F2.6's 50-repo pilot is small enough to launch under provisional legal opinion.

## 6. Branching decisions

| Fork | Options | **Decision** | Rationale |
|---|---|---|---|
| **B1 — IdP** | Own issuer / GitHub OAuth / both | **Both** — self-issued for local; GitHub default for cloud; OIDC fed for enterprise | Local zero-config preserved; GitHub eliminates password store for cloud; OIDC slots in for enterprise IdPs via the same trait |
| **B2 — HNSW persistence** | Blob-per-corpus / pgvector | **Blob** (revisit at scale) | Reuses shipped `.ministr-index` export/import; pgvector's 2K-dim HNSW ceiling locks future model choices; pgvector is a defensible later migration if query patterns demand SQL-side joins |
| **B3 — Free Cloud tier** | Free / no free | **No free cloud** (user-resolved) | Eliminates indexing-abuse cost spiral; positions ministr as serious infrastructure not a toy; Local stays MIT for the OSS evangelism path |
| **B4 — Enterprise license** | BSL / closed crate | **Closed `ministr-enterprise` crate** (`LicenseRef-Proprietary`) | Cleanest open-core; BSL's "converts to open after N years" carries legal overhead that buys us nothing — the cloud code is already closed |
| **B5 — Bridge visualizer** | Free / Team-gated | **CLI bridge MIT (today); web visualizer Team-gated** | The polished UI is what gets screenshotted in design reviews and posted on Twitter — capture upgrade value there; the underlying graph stays open so OSS users still benefit |
| **B6 — Cloud host** | Azure / multi-cloud | **Azure through Team launch; add AWS region per Enterprise contract** | One platform until forced; multi-cloud is engineering tax that doesn't pay until a specific Enterprise buyer requires it |
| **B7 — Atlas v0 timing** | Pre-Pro / with Pro / post-Pro | **With Pro launch (F2.6)** (user-resolved) | The moat narrative is real on day one; small enough pilot (50 repos) to launch under provisional legal opinion before G.1 closes |
| **B8 — MCP federation dialect** | Wait for MCP-AX / ship namespaced prefix now / both | **Both — namespaced fallback now, align to MCP-AX as it stabilises** | Doesn't block F6.4 on draft-status timing; agents get value immediately; the namespaced prefix is forward-compatible with MCP-AX hierarchical names |
| **B9 — Atlas embedder** *(2026-05-21)* | All-open / All-voyage / Atlas-only cloud embedder (forked corpora) | **All-open: `Qwen3-Embedding-0.6B` INT8-quantised** | Open-weight Apache-2.0 (preserves the open-core thesis); 32K context handles full source files; ~600M params → ~150MB INT8 (CPU-runnable on Atlas spot pool); strong MTEB performance with code subset competitive with voyage-code-3 minus ~10–14%; 1024-dim output avoids pgvector's 2K ceiling. Headroom: bump to `Qwen3-Embedding-8B` for premium indexing if quality demands. Locked the open-weight path per F4.x's recommended Option 1 |

## 7. Risk register

| # | Risk | Likelihood | Severity | Mitigation |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| R1 | **Anthropic / OpenAI ship official "code intelligence MCP"** — first-party gravity is real (Claude Code's native MCP tool-search shipped Feb 2026) | medium | high | Depth (SOLID + cross-language bridge + Atlas + per-agent primitives) is hard to ship as a side feature of a frontier-model company; integrate AS the official tool via the registry; partner posture, not competitive |
| R2 | **MCP adoption stalls** — Perplexity dropped MCP internally (Nov 2025); other major agents may follow | low–medium | high | Substrate works via any tool-calling protocol; if MCP momentum shifts, port the same surface to whatever wins; the IP is the indexer + Atlas, not the wire format |
| R3 | **Sourcegraph reverses Enterprise-only pivot** *(refresh 2026-05-21: partially realised — Sourcegraph 7.0 on 2026-02-25 announced "intelligence layer for AI coding agents" framing, direct positional collision; pricing/Enterprise-only posture unchanged but messaging now competes for the exact narrative we own)* | low → **realised (messaging only)** | medium | They invested heavily in Amp; the price floor + closed posture remains the gap. Sharpen Sourcegraph-comparison copy on `/pricing` and the §1 table — name them as the closed-Enterprise incumbent and ministr as the MIT-core challenger to that same intelligence-layer narrative |
| R4 | **Crowded code-intelligence MCP directory** — xray, pitlane-mcp, Trace, intellij-mcp competing on similar copy | medium | medium | Differentiator is hosted + polyglot bridge + Atlas (none of which they have); marketing must lead with these |
| R5 | **Atlas legal challenge** — derivative-work claim or unlicensed-content allegation | low–medium | high | G.1 opinion of counsel; permissive licenses only at launch; opt-out registry; public manifest; clear `LEGAL-ATLAS.md` |
| R6 | **Embedding-model commoditisation** | high | **positive** | Benefit not threat — cheaper for us; moat lives in the layer above (SOLID/bridge/Atlas/sessions) |
| R7 | **Public MCP server attack surface** — exposed MCP endpoints flagged as vulnerability class by Bitsight (2026) | medium | high | OAuth 2.1 + DCR is already in place; per-IP + per-tenant rate limits in F2.2; G.2 pen test before F5 sales |
| R8 | **Stripe freeze / payment processor ban** | low | high | Standard SaaS; have a Paddle / Lemon Squeezy contingency contact pre-listed; webhook abstraction in `ministr-cloud` makes the swap mechanical |
| R9 | **License-flip (F0) backlash from existing contributors** | very low | low | User is sole author at time of writing; MIT is the most-permissive choice; document the open-core thesis publicly to set expectations |
| R10 | **Single-founder bus factor** | high | high | Unavoidable mid-stage; mitigate via aggressive architecture docs (white-paper-grade write-ups of SOLID/coherence/bridge); G.3 SOC2 documentation creates a forced documentation discipline |
| R11 | **Free-tier indexing-abuse cost spiral** | n/a (eliminated by B3) | — | No free cloud; per-IP + per-tenant rate limits still apply to paid tiers to mitigate leaked-key abuse |
| R12 | **GitHub App outage / API quota** | low | medium | Cache installation tokens at the indexer pod; fall back to PAT path on App-API 5xx |

**Files that DO NOT change in this roadmap (notable for stability):** the 12 bridge detectors at `ministr-core/src/code/bridge/{cgo,electron,ffi,flutter,grpc,http_route,jni,napi,pyo3,tauri,uniffi,wasm_bindgen}.rs`; the ~20 language parsers at `ministr-core/src/code/lang/`; the SOLID detector at `ministr-core/src/service/solid.rs`; the coherence module at `ministr-core/src/coherence.rs`. These are the moat artefacts — they get LARGER over time (more languages, more detectors, more SOLID rules) but the existing files stabilise.

## 9. "Done" criteria per phase

> Each phase ships when a single unattended end-to-end scenario passes. Repeated here from §4 for at-a-glance ops review.

- **F0** — `cargo metadata` shows MIT on all 6 OSS crates; `LICENSE-MIT` + `STEWARDSHIP.md` published; no `LicenseRef-Proprietary` text remains in the OSS half.
- **F1** — a paying user signs in with GitHub, creates a corpus, restarts the pod, the corpus is still there, and `/api/v1/billing/usage` reflects metered events.
- **F2** *(revenue moment #1)* — stranger lands on `ministr.ai/pricing` → clicks "Start Pro" → completes Stripe Checkout → Tauri panel shows Pro badge → installs GitHub App on a private repo → clones it → queries it → queries Atlas v0 — all unattended in under five minutes.
- **F3** *(revenue moment #2)* — 3-seat team's owner invites two coworkers by email, all three accept, owner shares an org-owned corpus, all three can query, dashboard matches the live Stripe invoice, a coherence event fires a Slack webhook within 30s, bridge visualizer renders the corpus graph.
- **F4** — Pro user queries any of 5K Atlas repos with fresh (≤7d) results <500ms p95; public manifest matches the live blob set byte-for-byte; opt-out signals honored within one cron; Team annotation overlays scoped to org only.
- **F5** *(revenue moment #3)* — enterprise customer installs ministr in their own VPC via Helm, federates to Entra ID, indexes a private repo, mirrors a 100-repo Atlas subset into VPC, streams immutable audit to Splunk, rotates CMK in Azure Key Vault — all gated by a license key our portal issued.
- **F6** — agent's session ID resolves to the same budget/drops state from any pod; one MCP URL returns a unified tool surface across own corpora + selected Atlas reads.
- **G.1** — counsel opinion published at `LEGAL-ATLAS.md`; F4.1 gates open.
- **G.2** — third-party pen test report on file; findings remediated; F5 sales gates open.
- **G.3** — Drata/Vanta GRC platform adopted; first SOC2 Type 1 audit complete; report on Trust Center.

## 10. Out of scope (explicitly NOT building)

- **Our own coding assistant / chat UI.** ministr is the substrate, not the agent. Cursor / Claude Code / Continue / Amp / Cody-as-Amp are the integration points.
- **IDE / LSP plugins.** MCP is the integration surface; building VS Code or JetBrains plugins is the agent's job, not ours.
- **General-purpose web search MCP.** Commodity; SerpAPI MCP / Brave MCP / Tavily MCP exist.
- **Our own embedding model training.** Models commoditise; ride the wave (BGE, jina, voyage); moat lives above the model layer.
- **`/api/v1/corpora/{id}/ask` on cloud.** Containers have no `claude` CLI in PATH; would require an Anthropic-API-direct rewrite of the `Inference` trait, not committed to this roadmap. (Carry-over from previous plan.)
- **Multi-cloud day-one.** Azure only; AWS region per Enterprise contract (B6).
- **Source-available Enterprise** (à la BSL). Closed proprietary crate is cleaner (B4).
- **Free Cloud tier.** Resolved B3 — local stays MIT, cloud is paid from $20 (matches user decision).
- **Community RFC process for the roadmap.** This document is published not negotiated; future major bets get individual RFCs or design docs.

No carry-overs lost.

### Discovered during /roadmap-refresh (2026-05-21)

Surfaced during an F4 + G.1 deliberate + ministr + serpapi research cycle. None implemented; surfaced for user review.

- [x] **F4.x — Embedder choice for Atlas at scale** *(2026-05-21, resolved → B9)* *(was: blocks F4.2 cron design; decision-required)*
  - **Resolution.** Locked **`Qwen3-Embedding-0.6B` INT8-quantised** as the single Atlas embedder (Option 1 — all-open) per B9 in §6 Branching decisions.
  - **Why this model specifically.** 2026 research cycle (serpapi, May 2026): Baseten's Sep 2025 "best open-source embedding models" guide explicitly recommends Qwen3-Embedding-8B as the SOTA open-weight overall; Medium analysis (Jun 2025) shows Qwen3-Embedding "significantly outperforms BGE-M3 across standardized benchmarks". Qwen3-Embedding-0.6B is the smaller sibling — Apache-2.0 weights, 32K context, 1024-dim output, INT8-quantises to ~150MB suitable for the Atlas spot-CPU pool. The 0.6B variant beats OpenAI text-embedding-3-large on MTEB per LocalLLaMA threads while staying CPU-runnable.
  - **Why not the alternatives.** voyage-code-3 (closed API, $0.18/M tokens) was ruled out per the open-core thesis. Nomic Embed Code (code-specialist, smaller) was strong but Qwen3-Embedding-0.6B handles general+code well from a single model — important since Atlas blobs are queried alongside docs corpora. BGE-Code/BGE-M3 underperforms Qwen3 in 2026 benchmarks.
  - **The constraint upheld.** Atlas blobs are queried by both cloud-hosted callers AND any future on-prem mirror (F4.4); a single open-weight model preserves the one-curated-network promise. 1024-dim avoids pgvector's 2K HNSW ceiling.
  - **Headroom.** Bump to `Qwen3-Embedding-8B` for premium indexing if the quality delta vs closed APIs becomes a customer-cited concern. The blob format stays interoperable as long as the embedder family matches.
  - **Validation:** decision captured in §6 row B9; F4.2's worker template references B9 (this iteration updates F4.2's "INT8 quantised embedder" carry-over note). Resolved without writing any Rust — F4.2's cron can now be designed against a locked model when G.1 closes.

- [ ] **G.1+ — Bartz-anchored legal opinion shape** *(refinement, not new chunk; G.1 carry-along)*
  - When commissioning the G.1 counsel opinion, **cite *Bartz v. Anthropic* (N.D. Cal., June 2025) as the doctrinal anchor** and ask counsel to address how retrieval indexes differ from training corpora (Bartz held training on lawfully-acquired works fair use; pirated acquisition is NOT fair use; ministr's git-clone-from-public-HTTPS path is the lawful-acquisition vector). Counsel should specifically address: (a) does an HNSW embedding-vector index count as a "transformative use" the same way training corpora do; (b) does serving retrieved snippets from public OSS via MCP introduce a different copyright posture than embedding-based retrieval; (c) what's the AGPL/GPL/LGPL treatment for retrieval indexes given the 2025–2026 fair-use jurisprudence. Adds maybe 1–2 questions to the engagement — no new chunk, just shaping G.1's scope sharper.

### Discovered during /roadmap-refresh (2026-05-23)

Surfaced via serpapi research cycle on MCP ecosystem, competitive landscape, and email delivery.

- [ ] **F3.1b-ii-c Resend bounce webhook handler** — `POST /webhooks/resend` endpoint receiving Resend's `email.bounced` webhook events. On bounce, mark the email address in a `bounced_emails` table so future invite sends skip it (or warn the admin). Resend webhook signature verification uses svix-style HMAC. Small, well-scoped chunk; unblocked once the operator's Resend dashboard is configured.
- [ ] **F7 — MCP 2026-07-28 spec migration** — see §F7 above. The highest-priority new track; creates 6 unblocked code chunks.
  > NOTE (refresh 2026-05-23): consider promoting F7 to the top of the pending queue — rmcp will update to the new spec and our `initialize`-dependent architecture will break.

### Discovered during PHASE6 azure-demo (2026-05-20)

These gaps surfaced when fixing `just azure-demo`'s smoke test end-to-end. The smoke now passes (clone → worker indexes → bundle uploads → pod recycle → lazy restore → `/api/v1/corpora` reports 44 files), but probing the cloud over `/mcp` revealed that the MCP query surface is still single-corpus.

- [x] **F2.x — Tenant-aware corpus routing on `/mcp`** *(extends F1.2 #3; gates F2 multi-tenant correctness)* — F2.x-a/b/c/d all landed. Thread closed.
  - [x] **F2.x-a Mechanical: `Backend::Registry` variant + per-call resolver** *(2026-05-20)*
    - [x] New `Backend::Registry { default_service, registry }` variant in `ministr-mcp/src/backend/mod.rs`. Resolver `resolve_registry_handle(default, registry, project)` calls `registry.ensure_present(project_as_corpus_id)` and returns `Ok(Arc<CorpusHandle>)` on hit (including blob lazy-restore) or `Err(default_service)` on `None`/unknown/restore-failure — matches `DaemonMultiBackend::for_project`'s typo-tolerance.
    - [x] All 14 dispatch arms (`survey`, `survey_with_exclude`, `read_section`, `extract_claims`, `search_symbols`, `definition`, `references`, `impact`, `dead_code`, `solid`, `related_claims`, `compress`, `toc`, `bridges`) call through `handle.service.<method>` for the registry hit case, with `Err`-fallback to the bound `default_service` so existing single-corpus tests stay green.
    - [x] `MinistrServer::with_corpus_registry` (`ministr-mcp/src/server/builders.rs`) now swaps `Backend::Local` → `Backend::Registry` when called, so the existing `cmd_serve_http` wiring picks up the new variant with no caller-side changes. Stdio / proxy paths are unaffected (no `with_corpus_registry` call there).
    - **Validation:** workspace `cargo test` + `cargo clippy --workspace --all-targets -- -D warnings -W clippy::pedantic` pass. Live cloud probe via `/tmp/ministr-mcp-query.py` (the smoke harness from 2026-05-20) deferred to next deploy.
  - [x] **F2.x-b Tenant isolation through tokio task-local + Postgres filter** *(2026-05-20)*
    - [x] New `TenantCorpusFilter` trait in `ministr-api/src/tenant_filter.rs` (MIT open-core seam, mirrors F2.1's `InstallationTokenMinter`). `PostgresTenantCorpusFilter` impl in `ministr-cloud/src/tenant_filter.rs` queries `cloud_corpora.tenant_id` per call (PK lookup). Permissive on legacy `tenant_id IS NULL` rows; strict otherwise. Fail-closed on storage errors.
    - [x] `Backend::Registry` gained `tenant_filter: Option<Arc<dyn TenantCorpusFilter>>` + a `registry_with_filter` constructor. All 14 dispatch arms accept `tenant_subject: Option<&str>` and thread it into `resolve_registry_handle`. Cross-tenant / typo / restore failure / filter storage error all collapse to the same `Err(default_service)` shape — existence-leak-resistant.
    - [x] Threading mechanism: `tokio::task_local!` in `ministr-mcp/src/tenant_scope.rs`. Axum middleware `scope_tenant` runs AFTER `validate_token_middleware` (which sets the `Tenant` extension) and BEFORE rmcp's `StreamableHttpService`, scoping the next.run future. Tool handlers in `MinistrServer` read via `crate::tenant_scope::current()`. Why task-local instead of `RequestContext<RoleServer>` extraction: rmcp 1.5 makes `Peer::new` `pub(crate)`, blocking 35 unit-test call sites from constructing a fake ctx — task-local needs zero test changes.
    - [x] Wired in `cmd_serve_http`: when `cloud_pool` is `Some`, the server is built via `with_corpus_registry_and_filter`; self-hosted serve continues to use `with_corpus_registry` (no filter mounted). Middleware is mounted on the `mcp_router` unconditionally — self-hosted just sees no `Tenant` in extensions and scopes `None`.
    - **Validation:** four new unit tests in `backend::tests` cover the 4 decision arms — `project=None` skips filter; missing `tenant_subject` denies; explicit deny falls back; storage error fails closed. Workspace `cargo test` + `cargo clippy` clean. Cross-tenant probe via the live `/tmp/ministr-mcp-query.py` harness deferred to next deploy.
  - [x] **F2.x-c Session default-corpus selection** *(2026-05-20)*
    - [x] Extended `TenantCorpusFilter` trait (`ministr-api/src/tenant_filter.rs`) with `default_corpus_for_tenant(tenant_subject) -> Option<String>` — default impl returns `Ok(None)` so existing impls compile without change. `PostgresTenantCorpusFilter` overrides to `SELECT corpus_id FROM cloud_corpora WHERE tenant_id = $1 ORDER BY created_at DESC LIMIT 1` (covered by the existing `idx_cloud_corpora_tenant` partial index from migration 0003 — single index probe + read).
    - [x] `Backend::Registry::resolve_registry_handle` (`ministr-mcp/src/backend/mod.rs`) gained a project=None branch: when `tenant_filter` and `tenant_subject` are both `Some`, consult `default_corpus_for_tenant`. On hit, the resolver re-runs the `allowed` check (uniform treatment — same filter implementation obviously approves its own choice) then calls `ensure_present` with the chosen `corpus_id`. On `Ok(None)` or `Err`, falls back to `default_service`.
    - [x] Five new unit tests cover the F2.x-c decision tree (`project_none_consults_default_corpus_then_falls_back`, `project_none_no_tenant_skips_filter_entirely`, `project_none_no_filter_falls_back`, `project_none_default_corpus_drives_lookup`, `project_none_default_corpus_error_falls_back`).
    - **Validation:** workspace `cargo test` + `cargo clippy --workspace --all-targets -- -D warnings -W clippy::pedantic` clean. Live: authenticated tenant with one indexed corpus calls `ministr_survey` without `project` → should hit that corpus (deferred to next deploy).
  - [x] **F2.x-d Stamp `cloud_corpora.tenant_id` on upsert** *(2026-05-20)*
    - [x] `PostgresCorporaRepo::upsert`, `PostgresIndexJobSink::create_pending`, and `PostgresIndexJobSink::register_corpus_only` (the three cloud_corpora write sites) consult a new `resolve_tenant_id()` helper that prefers `ministr_mcp::tenant_scope::current()` over the constructor's configured `tenant_id` fallback. Worker (IngestionRunner) doesn't write cloud_corpora, so background-task upserts are not an issue.
    - [x] `scope_tenant` middleware mounted on `daemon_read_router`, `daemon_write_router`, `daemon_bundle_router`, `daemon_obs_router` in `cmd_serve_http` (as an inner layer that runs after `validate_scope_middleware` populates `Tenant` in extensions). Self-hosted serve still gets the middleware mounted; it sees no `Tenant` and scopes None — same code path in both modes.
    - [x] `ON CONFLICT` clauses changed from `tenant_id = EXCLUDED.tenant_id` to `tenant_id = COALESCE(EXCLUDED.tenant_id, cloud_corpora.tenant_id)` so a `restore()`-driven re-upsert at boot (no axum request, no task-local) doesn't NULL out a previously-populated tenant_id.
    - [x] Two new unit tests in `corpora_repo::tests` cover the precedence fall-through (`resolve_tenant_id` outside scope → config; both None → None).
    - **Validation:** cargo test + clippy clean. Live: clone a private repo via the cloud path; `psql … -c "select corpus_id, tenant_id from cloud_corpora order by created_at desc limit 1"` should show the authenticated user's subject (deferred to next deploy). Old NULL rows stay permissive — tightening to strict-only behaviour is a follow-up migration concern.
  - **Original diagnostic evidence on record:** `/tmp/ministr-mcp-query.out` from 2026-05-20 showed `tools/list` returning all 20 tools, `ministr_toc` reporting `{documents:0, sections:0}` on the empty default, and `ministr_survey` with explicit `project=multi-b1cdc4d2` falling back to that empty default. F2.x-a is the fix for the symptom; F2.x-b closes the security follow-up.
